Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Introducing Al-Ta'liq al-Fasih: A Hanafi Usul Super-Commentary
Title page stating the book's name and author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three key texts in the Hanafi usul al-fiqh tradition mentioned on this title page and explain the relationship between a matn (base text), a sharh (commentary), and a hashiyah (super-commentary).

Core Idea
A super-commentary (hāshiyah) is a gloss on a commentary; here, al-Ta'liq al-Fasih explains al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, two pillars of Hanafi usul.

This passage is the title page of a modern Hanafi usul work. It names the book and its author, and tells us the tradition it belongs to: the commentarial chain of al-Tawdih and al-Talwih. Understanding this chain is essential for any student of Hanafi usul because these texts form the core curriculum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Works
List the three distinct titles mentioned: al-Tawdih, al-Talwih, and al-Ta'liq al-Fasih.
These are all works on usul al-fiqh, specific to the Hanafi school.
2
Determine the Hierarchy
Recognize that al-Tawdih is the base matn, al-Talwih is its sharh (commentary), and al-Ta'liq al-Fasih is a hashiyah (super-commentary) on both.
The phrase 'fi hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih' indicates that al-Ta'liq explains and resolves difficulties in both earlier texts.
3
Note the Author and Context
Identify the author as Abu Mas'ud Manzoor Ahmad Nu'mani and his affiliation with al-Jami'ah al-Arabiyyah al-Nuriyyah in Pakistan.
This shows the ongoing tradition of Hanafi scholarship in the Indian subcontinent.
4
Reflect on the Purpose of a Hashiyah
Understand that a hashiyah serves to clarify, critique, and expand upon the earlier commentary, often responding to objections and refining legal reasoning.
Hasiyah works are a key part of the Hanafi scholarly method, allowing for continuous development.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنَّ الدِينَ عِندَ اللهِ الإسْلَام (القرآن) هذه حواش معلقة على التوضيح والتلويح مسماة ب التعليق الفسيح في حل التوضيح والتلويح ألفها وحررها أبو مسعود منظور أحمد نعماني حفظه الله بالجامعة العربية النورية حبيب آباد طاهر والى بهاولپور - پاکستان مكتبة السياريح منرکی روڈ کوئٹہ
Indeed, the religion with Allah is Islam (Quran). This is a super-commentary (hawashi) on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih, named Al-Ta'liq al-Fasih fi Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, authored and written by Abu Mas'ud Manzoor Ahmad Nu'mani, may Allah preserve him, at the Arabic University Al-Nuriyya, Habibabad, Tahir Wali, Bahawalpur - Pakistan. Maktaba al-Siyarih, Manarki Road, Quetta.
Source pages p. 1

Commentary
This passage is the title page of a work called 'Al-Ta'liq al-Fasih fi Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. It is a super-commentary (hāshiyah) on two foundational texts of Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh: Al-Tawḍīḥ by Ṣadr al-Sharīʿah and Al-Talwīḥ by Saʿd al-Dīn al-Taftāzānī. The author, Abū Masʿūd Manẓūr Aḥmad Nuʿmānī, is a contemporary scholar associated with al-Jāmiʿah al-ʿArabiyyah al-Nūriyyah in Pakistan. The work aims to explain and annotate the original commentaries. The verse quoted (Qurʾān 3:19) indicates the central importance of Islam. The publisher is Maktabah al-Siyāriḥ in Quetta.

Key Terms
حواش (hawāshī): Super-commentary or glosses on a primary text
التوضيح (al-Tawḍīḥ): A Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh text by Ṣadr al-Sharīʿah
التلويح (al-Talwīḥ): A commentary on al-Tawḍīḥ by al-Taftāzānī

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which text is the base matn in the chain mentioned on the title page?
A) Al-Talwih
B) Al-Tawdih
C) Al-Ta'liq al-Fasih
D) Quran 3:19

Key Takeaway
The title page establishes that al-Ta'liq al-Fasih is a super-commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, situating it in the Hanafi usul tradition of layered commentary.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Virtue of Fiqh and the Chain of Hanafi Usul Commentaries
Front matter with hadith and commentary title

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hadith on understanding religion, explain its role in motivating fiqh study, and locate Al-Ta'liq within the Hanafi usul commentary tradition.

Core Idea
Understanding religion is a divine gift; this commentary bridges Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih for deeper usul mastery.

This lesson introduces the title page of Al-Ta'liq fi Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Tashrih, a super-commentary on two foundational Hanafi usul texts. The author begins with a famous hadith that underscores the high rank of fiqh. Understanding this hadith and the commentary chain will orient you to the purpose and importance of the work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith
Locate the hadith text in the source: 'مَن يُرِدِ اللَّهُ بِهِ خَيْرًا يُفَقِّهْهُ فِي الدِّينِ'. Recognize it as a Prophetic hadith on the virtue of understanding religion.
The Arabic in the source is slightly garbled but the core is clear.
2
Understand the hadith's significance for usul
The hadith establishes that deep understanding (tafaqquh) in religion is a sign of divine goodwill. This motivates the study of usul al-fiqh, which is the methodology for deriving rulings.
Tafaqquh includes both transmission (riwaya) and reasoning (diraya).
3
Identify the commentary chain
Note that Al-Ta'liq is a hashiya (marginal commentary) on Al-Tawdih and Al-Tashrih (likely Al-Talwih). Al-Tawdih is Sadr al-Shariah's matn, and Al-Talwih is Taftazani's super-commentary.
Al-Tashrih may be a scribal error for Al-Talwih.
4
Locate the author and his context
The author is Abu Mas'ud Manzur Ahmad Nu'mani, a Pakistani scholar linked to the Arabic University Nooriyah. This shows the living tradition of Hanafi usul commentary.
This work is a modern contribution to the sharh tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنَّ الدِّينَ عِندَ الله الإستُ الام العوالي من يُرِدِ اللهُ بِهِ خَير ايفقهه في الدين هذه حواش معلقة على التوضيح والتشريح سماة ب تعليق في حل التوضيح والتاريخ انفها و حررها ابو مسید منظور احمد نعمانی منی من الدرس بالجامعه العربيه النوريه حبيب آباد طاهر والى بھاولپور - پاکستان
Indeed, the religion with Allah is al-istu al-am al-awali. Whoever Allah intends good for, He gives him understanding in religion. These are marginal notes on Al-Tawdih and Al-Tashrih. Named 'Ta'liq fi Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Tashrih'. Written and edited by Abu Mas'ud Manzur Ahmad Nu'mani, from the lessons at the Arabic University Nooriyah, Habibabad, Tahir, Bahawalpur - Pakistan.
Source pages p. 2

Commentary
This passage is front matter: a title page from a Urdu commentary on the Hanafi usul works Al-Tawdih (by Sadr al-Shariah) and Al-Talwih (by Taftazani, though here called Al-Tashrih or Al-Tarikh – likely a scribal error). The author cites the famous hadith 'Whoever Allah intends good for, He gives him understanding in religion' to underscore the importance of fiqh. The work is titled 'Ta'liq fi Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Tashrih', and the author is Abu Mas'ud Manzur Ahmad Nu'mani, a scholar from Pakistan associated with the Arabic University Nooriyah.

Key Terms
حواش (hawashi): Marginal notes or super-commentary on a main text.
التوضيح والتشريح (al-tawdih wa al-tashrih): References to two foundational texts in Hanafi usul: Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shariah and Al-Talwih (or Al-Tashrih) by Taftazani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of citing the hadith 'Whoever Allah intends good for, He gives him understanding in religion' in this front matter?
A) To prove that understanding religion is obligatory upon every Muslim.
B) To highlight the virtue and importance of studying fiqh and usul.
C) To indicate that the author is a scholar of hadith.
D) To correct a misunderstanding about the text's title.

Key Takeaway
This commentary is a modern link in the Hanafi usul tradition, beginning with a hadith that reminds us that deep religious understanding is a divine blessing.

Introduction and Front Matter

5 min
The Author's Scholarly Credentials and the Authority of His Commentary
Preface describing the author's scholarly stature and teacher's trust

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholarly attributes of the commentator from the preface and explain how they contribute to the authority of his commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih.

Core Idea
A commentator's mastery in both transmitted and rational sciences, and his teacher's trust, establish the authority of his usul commentary.

This preface introduces us to the author of Al-Ta'liq al-Faseeh, Maulana Manzoor Ahmad Naumani. It highlights his teaching prowess, his command over both transmitted (manqul) and rational (maqul) sciences, and the fact that he was chosen as the successor of his eminent teacher, Maulana Habibullah Gangohi. Understanding this background helps us appreciate why this commentary is considered a reliable and valuable resource in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of this preface
Recognize that it is a biographical introduction meant to establish the author's credibility and the reliability of his commentary.
This is typical in classical Islamic works.
2
List the scholarly claims made about the author
Note the specific attributes: teaching ability, expertise in both transmitted and rational sciences, being a successor of a great scholar.
These claims build his authority.
3
Determine the relevance to usul al-fiqh
Explain why mastery in both manqul and maqul is essential for a commentator on usul texts like Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih.
Usul al-fiqh requires knowledge of both text-based reasoning and rational principles.
4
Connect the author's authority to the reliability of the commentary
Understand that the teacher's trust and the author's reputation lend weight to the explanations in the commentary.
A trusted commentator ensures accurate transmission of Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
مصنف کے حالات تمهید
تدریسی علمی مقام گرامی قدر راستا ذ مکرم حضرت مولانا منظور احمد صاحب نعمانی مہتم مدرسه عربیہ انوریہ حبیب آباد دامت برکاتہم اپنی علمی حیثیت میں تعارف کے محتاج نہیں بلکہ اپنی تدریسی ضیاء پاشیوں کی بدولت معروف و مشہور شخصیت ہیں۔ علما عظام آپ کی خداداد صلاحیتوں سے بخوبی واقف ہیں ۔ وقتا فوقتا آپ سے تدریسی استفادہ کیا کرتے ہیں۔ بعض بعض کتب کے مغلق اور حل طلب مقامات کی توضیح و تشریح کیلئے آپ کی طرف رجوع فرمایا کرتے ہیں۔ رہے طلبا ۔ کرام ان کا کیا پوچھنا وہ تو آپ کے درس کے علمی و تحقیقی ضیاء، اور سحبانی فصیحان انداز بیان پر پروانہ وار جمع ہوتے رہتے ہیں ۔
خدا تعالیٰ شاہد ہے کہ جب بھی آپ اپنی درسگاہ میں مسند آرکہ ہوتے ہیں ۔ تو آپ کے ارد گرد طلبہامہ کرام کا مجمع ہوتا ہے۔ آپ کے فصیحانہ افہام و تفہیم میں اتنا جاذبیت اور مٹھاس پایا جاتا ہے کہ ہر نوعیت کی طبعیت کا طالب علم ذکی وغنی منجو سماع نظر آتا ہے ۔ اور ان کی خندہ پیشانی سے ظاہر ہو رہا ہوتا ہے کہ ہر ایک اپنی استعداد کیمطابق آپ سے بہرہ یاب ہو رہا ہے۔
آپ درس نظامی کے نصاب کے ہرن میں اشتہاری مہمات کے حال ہیں۔ اور کتب کے علاس کو منصہ شہود پر لانے میں آپ کو سنجر اور ید طولی حاصل ہے۔ آپ شیخ المنقول بھی ہیں اور شیخ المعقول بھی ۔ آپ اتنا خوش قسمت اور خوش نصیب ہیں کہ آپ میں ان بہترین علمی خوبیوں اور جوہروں کو دیکھ کر مردم شناس ہنستی شیخنا العظم صاحب الشریعیت والطہ لہ تیت حضرت مولانا حبیب اللہ صاحب گمانوی قدس الله سرو نے اپنے وسیع حلقہ تلامذہ میں سے آپ کو ہی اپنا جانشین پسند فرمایا اور مدرسہ عربیہ انوریہ عیسی گرانمایہ مانت جسے وہ اپنا اخروی سرمایہ سمجھتے تھے ۔ آپ کے سپرد فرما گئے۔ عرض تدریسی اور علمی حیثیت میں تو آپ کا لشمس فی عبد السلام ہیں ۔
مقصور
البتہ آپ کے نقش حیات مختصر کچھ اس طرح سے ہیں جنہیں میں خود بتقاضائے محبت لکھ
رہا ہوں اور لکھنا اپنی سعادت سمجھتا ہوں ۔
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.
Preface on the author's conditions.
The honored and respected teacher, Maulana Manzoor Ahmad Naumani, the principal of Madrasa Arabia Anoria Habibabad - may his blessings endure - does not need introduction in his scholarly capacity, but is a famous and well-known personality due to his teaching illuminations. The great scholars are well aware of his God-given abilities. From time to time, they benefit from his teaching. For the explanation and clarification of difficult and problematic points of some books, they refer to him. As for the noble students, what can be asked? They gather like moths around the scientific and research illumination of his lessons and his clear, eloquent style of expression.
Allah Almighty is witness that whenever you sit on the teaching chair in your classroom, a crowd of noble students gathers around you. In your eloquent understanding and explanation, such attraction and sweetness is found that every type of student - intelligent and wealthy - appears attentive in hearing. And from their smiling faces, it appears that each one is benefiting from you according to his capacity.
You are well-versed in the intricacies of the Dars-e-Nizami curriculum. And in bringing the meanings of books to the stage of manifestation, you possess [؟] and a long hand. You are both a teacher of transmitted sciences and a teacher of rational sciences. You are so fortunate that seeing these excellent scholarly qualities and gems in you, the connoisseur of men, our great teacher, the possessor of Sharia and purity, Hazrat Maulana Habibullah Gangohi - may Allah sanctify his secret - chose you from among his wide circle of students as his successor and entrusted to you the Madrasa Arabia Anoria [؟] which he considered his capital for the Hereafter. In your teaching and scholarly capacity, you are like the sun in the sky of [؟].
Limited.
However, your brief life sketch is as follows, which I myself am writing due to the demands of love and consider writing it my good fortune.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is a preface (تمہید) written by a student or colleague of Maulana Manzoor Ahmad Naumani, the author of this commentary (التعلیق الفسیح). It serves as a biographical introduction, praising his teaching abilities, scholarly command, and his selection as the successor of his eminent teacher, Mawlana Habibullah Gangohi. The preface highlights the author's expertise in both transmitted (منقول) and rational (معقول) sciences, indicating his comprehensive knowledge in the Islamic sciences, which is essential for a commentator on usul al-fiqh texts like Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih. The passage sets the stage for the reader to appreciate the authority and reliability of the author's commentary. It does not contain any legal rulings but rather establishes the credibility of the author.

Key Terms
تمہید (tamheed): Preface or introduction to a book, often containing background information about the author or the work.
منقول (manqul): Transmitted sciences, i.e., knowledge derived from revealed texts (Quran, Hadith) and their traditional interpretations.
معقول (maqul): Rational sciences, including logic, dialectics, and principles of jurisprudence that rely on reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The authorship of Al-Tawdih
B) The Madrasa Arabia Anoria as his successor
C) The task of writing Al-Ta'liq al-Faseeh
D) His personal library of rare manuscripts

Key Takeaway
This preface establishes the commentator's authority through his mastery of both transmitted and rational sciences and his teacher's trust, making his usul commentary a reliable source.

Introduction and Front Matter

Introduction to al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih and the Hashiyah Genre
Opening remarks of the commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main texts and the author of this hashya, and explain the purpose of a hashya in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
A hashya is a supercommentary that clarifies and expands upon a base commentary, not a standalone work.

This opening passage of al-Taliq al-Fasih introduces the author, the texts he is glossing, and his scholarly motive. Understanding the genre of hashya is essential for navigating later usul discussions, as it orients the student to the layered nature of Hanafi scholarly writing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his self-description
The author describes himself as 'al-ʿabd al-faqīr ilā Allāh al-ghanī Manṣūr Aḥmad al-Nuʿmānī'. Note the humility and dependency on Allah, a common trope in Islamic scholarly introductions.
The name al-Nuʿmānī suggests affiliation with the madhhab of Abū Ḥanīfa al-Nuʿmān.
2
Identify the base texts being glossed
The author states he is writing 'ḥawāshin muʿallaqah ʿalā al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ'. Al-Tawḍīḥ is by Ṣadr al-Sharīʿa, and al-Talwīḥ is its commentary by Saʿd al-Dīn al-Taftāzānī.
These are two foundational texts in Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh.
3
Understand the structure of the hashya
The author explains he writes 'qāla al-muṣannif fī al-Tawḍīḥ' and 'qāla al-shāriḥ fī al-Talwīḥ' to distinguish the base text from the commentary, then adds his own gloss. This three-layer structure (matn → sharḥ → ḥāshiyah) is typical.
Students must be careful not to confuse the different voices.
4
Note the title and date
The work is titled 'al-Taʿlīq al-Fasīḥ fī Ḥall al-Tawḍīḥ wa al-Talwīḥ' and was completed in Jumādā al-Thāniyah 1140 AH. This gives historical context.
The title means 'The spacious commentary in solving al-Tawḍīḥ and al-Talwīḥ'.
5
Analyze the opening of the commentary on the hamdalah
The author notes that al-Taftāzānī begins with 'al-ḥamdu lillāh' to indicate that true praise belongs to Allah by essence, not by acquisition. The word 'Allāh' is a proper name for the divine essence, so the deserving of praise is essential.
This type of theological-linguistic analysis is characteristic of uṣūl al-fiqh commentaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الحمد لله الذي أحكم الدين القويم بالمحكماته ونوع سننه [؟] الكائنات، وأشرقه بالإجماع والقياس والاجتهادات. صلى الله تعالى على رسوله سيد البريات وعلى آله وأصحابه القادة والسادة. أما بعد: فيقول العبد الفقير إلى الله الغني منصور أحمد النعماني: هذه حواشٍ معلقة على التوضيح والتلويح، وأرجو من الله الكريم والرحيم أن ينفع به طلبة علم أصول الدين ويجعله لي ذخيرة سعيدة منجية بنجاة تامة في يوم الدين. أوضحت المتن بعد أن كتبت لفظ قال المصنف في التوضيح .. والشرح بعد لفظ قال الشارح في التلويح وسميتها التعليق الفسيح في حل التوضيح والتلويح .. وكان ذلك في شهر جمادى الثانية سنة أربعة عشر ومائة وألف. قال الشارح في التلويح: بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم الحمد لله الذي أحكم بكتابه أصول الشريعة للفراء [؟] . شارح علیه الرحمه نے اپنی شرح کا انبساط [؟] کرتے ہوئے اور تسمیہ کے بعد اللہ تعالیٰ کا حمد ادا کرتے ہوئے کہا الحمد لله تو حمد کو مختص بالله عزیر [؟] کر کے اشارہ کیا کہ حقیقتاً مستحق حمد و ستائش صرف اللہ تعالیٰ ہے اور لفظ اللہ چونکہ ذات باری تعالیٰ کا علم ذاتی ہے اسلئے ملتے لفظ اللہ سچی استحقاق ذاتی ہے اور آگے چند اوصاف ذکر کر کے استحقاق اشارہ کیا کہ باری تعالیٰ مستحق حمد باستحقاق ذاتی ہے اور آگے چندا [؟] کی طرف اشارہ كيا الذى احكم الاحكام الاتقان یعنی ایک شیشی [؟] کو مستحکم اور پختہ کرنا بكتابه میں بار سیبیہ [؟] ہے اصول جمع ہے اصل کی جسکا معنی ہے یا بنتی علیه غيره الشرعية تم لفقه و غيره من العلوم الدین یہ اللہ تعالٰی نے جو احکام اپنے عبادہ کے لئے مشروع فرماتے ہیں بایں حیثیت کہ زلال رحمت کے پیاسوں کے لئے مور د اور مقام مشرب ہیں ان کاشت نفریقہ اور شرقہ [؟] ان کہا جاتا ہے جیسے مشارع المارشار بین کا مورد ہوتے ہیں ۔ اور یہی احکام مشروعہ بایں حیثیت کہ ان کی اطاعت کی جاتی ہے اور اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف سے ان پر جزا ملے گی تو انہیں
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who has perfected the upright religion with its clear verses and diversified His laws [؟] for the creatures, and illuminated it through consensus, analogy, and ijtihad. May Allah bless His messenger, the master of creation, and his family and companions, the leaders and masters. To proceed: The poor servant in need of Allah, the Self-Sufficient, Mansur Ahmad al-Nu'mani, says: These are annotations on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, and I hope from Allah, the Generous and Merciful, that He benefit the students of the science of usul al-din through it and make it for me a blessed treasure that delivers with complete salvation on the Day of Judgment. I clarified the text after writing the words 'the author said in al-Tawdih...' and the commentary after the words 'the commentator said in al-Talwih', and I named it 'al-Taliq al-Fasih fi Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih'. That was in the month of Jumada al-Thaniyah of the year 1140 AH. The commentator said in al-Talwih: 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who has perfected in His book the principles of the Shariah for the [؟]' The commentator, may Allah have mercy on him, in his commentary, after beginning with the basmalah, praised Allah saying 'al-hamdu lillah', so he specified praise to Allah, indicating that true praise is only due to Allah, and the word 'Allah' because it is a proper name for the Essence, so the word 'Allah' indicates essential deservingness. Then he mentioned several attributes indicating that the Exalted deserves praise by essential deservingness. Then he pointed to 'the one who perfected' meaning 'itqan' i.e., strengthening and consolidating something. 'In His book' refers to the Quran. 'Usul' is plural of 'asl' which means something on which others are built. 'Al-shar'iyyah' is for fiqh and other religious sciences. These are the rulings that Allah has legislated for His servants, considered as sources (shara'i') for those thirsting for mercy, like watering places (mashari') are places of drinking. And these legislated rulings, in terms of being obeyed and rewarded by Allah, are called...
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his commentary (hāshiyah) on al-Tawdīh wa al-Talwīh, two classic works of Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh. The author, Manṣūr Aḥmad al-Nuʿmānī, identifies himself and explains the purpose and title of his work. He then begins commenting on the opening lines of al-Talwīh by al-Taftāzānī, which start with the basmalah and ḥamdalah. The commentary explains that praising Allah is exclusive to Him because only He deserves it by essence, not by acquisition. The word 'Allah' is a proper name for the divine essence, indicating that praise is inherently due to Him. The phrase 'alladhī aḥkama' (who perfected) refers to making something firm and strong. 'Bi-kitābihi' refers to the Quran. 'Uṣūl al-sharʿiyyah' refers to the foundations of Islamic law, which are the sources from which rulings are derived. The author then digresses into an Urdu explanation of the term 'sharāʾiʿ' as watering places for those thirsty for mercy, drawing an analogy between divine rulings and sources of water. This opening establishes the text's genre as a supercommentary (ḥāshiyah) and sets a scholarly tone.

Key Terms
التوضيح (al-Tawdih): A famous Hanafi usul text by Sadr al-Sharia
التلويح (al-Talwih): A commentary on al-Tawdih by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani
حاشية (hashiya): A supercommentary or gloss on a sharh, often clarifying and expanding upon it

Al-Taliq al-Fasih is a hashya on the foundational Hanafi usul texts al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, written by Mansur Ahmad al-Nu'mani in 1140 AH to aid students in understanding the layered commentary tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Author's Preface: Definitions of Usul al-Fiqh and the Role of Revelation
Author's preface defining terms and methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shari'ah, din, and millah as distinct aspects of the same reality, and explain why religious doctrines must conform to the Qur'an to be valid.

Core Idea
Shari'ah, din, and millah are one reality viewed from different angles; doctrines require Qur'anic conformity to be sound.

In his preface, the author Manzur Ahmad al-Nu'mani introduces his commentary and clarifies foundational terms. This lesson unpacks his definitions of shari'ah, din, and millah, and the crucial principle that while rational proofs can establish God's existence, the correct formulation of doctrines must align with revelation. Understanding these distinctions is essential for the Hanafi methodological approach to usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his work
The author identifies himself as Manzur Ahmad al-Nu'mani and names his commentary al-Ta'liq al-Fasih fi Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. He explains that he writes the matn from al-Tawdih and the commentary from al-Talwih, dating the work to 914 AH.
Knowing the source pedigree helps assess authority.
2
Define the three terms: shari'ah, din, millah
The author explains that the same divine law is called shari'ah when considered as legislation for servants, din when viewed in terms of obedience and reward, and millah when regarded as a transmitted and compiled system. The multiplicity of names arises from different perspectives, not different realities.
This terminological precision is typical in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the relationship between rational proofs and the Qur'an for doctrines
The author argues that rational proofs can establish the existence of God and His attributes, but the validity and correctness of religious doctrines (aqaid) depend on conformity to the Qur'an. The proof of the Qur'an itself rests on prior belief in God and prophethood, but this is not circular because the doctrines are not proven solely by the Book; rather, the Book provides the standard for their correctness.
This resolves an apparent methodological tension: reason precedes revelation, yet revelation authorizes reason.
4
Explain the phrase 'ahkama bi kitabihi usul al-shari'ah'
The phrase means that Allah strengthened (ahkama) the foundations of the Sharia through His Book. The author notes that strengthening (ihkam) is different from proof (ithbat); the Book's role is to consolidate and validate the principles, not to create them from nothing.
This subtle distinction prevents a circular dependence of revelation on itself.

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who has strengthened the upright religion with its decisive verses, diversified the creations through His Sunnah, and illuminated it with consensus, analogy, and ijtihads. May Allah bless His Messenger, the master of mankind, and his family and companions, the leaders and masters. After this: the poor servant in need of Allah, the humble Manzur Ahmad al-Nu'mani, says: This is a marginal commentary on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, and I hope from Allah, the Generous and Merciful, that He benefits the students of the science of usul al-din through it and makes it for me a happy treasure that brings complete deliverance on the Day of Judgment. I clarified the matn after writing the words: 'the author said in al-Tawdih...' and the commentary after the words 'the commentator said in al-Talwih', and I named it al-Ta'liq al-Fasih fi Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih. That was in the month of Jumada al-Thani in the year 914 AH. The commentator said in al-Talwih: In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah who has strengthened with His Book the foundations of the Sharia. The commentator (may mercy be upon him) began his commentary by praising Allah after the basmalah... (Urdu commentary follows explaining the text: the meaning of 'al-hamdu lillah', the exclusivity of praise to Allah, the word 'Allah' as the proper name of the Essence, etc.) The summary is that in 'usul al-shari'ah', 'shari'ah' means the religion of Islam which Allah has legislated for His servants, and 'usul' means the religious principles, and 'ahkam' means strengthening and consolidating. So Allah has strengthened the doctrines and obligations through His Book. Although the proof of religious doctrines can be by rational proofs, their evidence is not dependent on the Book of Allah; rather, the proof of the Book of Allah is dependent on the doctrines. Because until one believes in the existence of God, His attributes of speech and sending messengers, and affirms them, how can the Book of Allah be established? Therefore, the proof of the principles of faith is not dependent on the Book; otherwise a circular argument would occur. However, the doctrines from the perspective of being considered valid are dependent on the Book, meaning that valid and correct doctrines are those that are in accordance with the light of the Book. Otherwise, even the philosophers among the divine scholars discuss doctrines, but since they are not in accordance with the light of divine revelation, they are not considered valid. So doctrines, since their correct proof from the Book is established, their consolidation comes from the Book of Allah, for that reason He said 'established' not 'proved'. The second phrase: 'raising by His address' etc.: 'raising' means declaring honor and elevating rank in acceptance, and 'address' means the address of Allah related to the actions of the legally responsible, and 'branches of the Hanifiyya?'
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This lesson is the author's introduction to his marginal commentary (hashiaya) on al-Tawdih and al-Talwih, two major works of Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins with the basmalah and hamd, praising Allah for establishing the religion with His decisive verses, and for diversifying creation and illuminating the religion through consensus, analogy, and ijtihad. He then identifies himself and his work, explaining his method: he writes the matn from al-Tawdih and then the commentary from al-Talwih. He names his work al-Ta'liq al-Fasih fi Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih and dates it to Jumada al-Thani 914 AH. After this, he quotes the beginning of al-Talwih and provides a detailed Urdu commentary explaining the phrases. He explains the meaning of 'al-hamdu lillah' as exclusive to Allah, and that Allah is the proper name of His essence. Then he explains the phrase 'who strengthened with His Book the foundations of the Sharia'. He breaks down 'ahkam' as meaning to strengthen and consolidate, 'usul' as the plural of 'asl' meaning that on which something else is built, and 'shari'ah' as the legal rulings legislated for the servants. He then distinguishes between the terms 'shari'ah', 'din', and 'millah' as different aspects of the same reality. The commentary then elaborates on the nature of religious doctrines (aqaid) and their relationship to rational and revealed proofs. The author argues that while rational proofs can establish the existence of God and His attributes, the correct and valid doctrines must be in accordance with the Book of Allah. The proof of the Book itself depends on prior belief in God and His messengers, but this does not create a vicious circle because the doctrines are not proven solely by the Book; rather, their correct formulation and validation come from the Book. This discussion is foundational for understanding the role of revelation in Islamic theology and jurisprudence.

Key Terms
اصول الشريعة (usul al-shari'ah): The foundational principles of Islamic law, which are established and strengthened by the Book of Allah.
شريعة (shari'ah): The religion of Islam as legislated by Allah for His servants.
دین (din): The religion considered in terms of obedience and reward from Allah.
ملت (millah): The religion considered in terms of its transmission and compilation.
قرآن (qur'an): The revealed Book of Allah, whose proof depends on prior belief in God and prophethood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author in his preface, how are shari'ah, din, and millah related?
A) They are completely different and unrelated concepts.
B) They are three different names for the same divine reality, each emphasizing a different aspect.
C) Shari'ah is the broadest, din is a subset, millah is a subset of din.
D) They are three historical stages of revelation.

Key Takeaway
Shari'ah, din, and millah are one reality; revelation is the ultimate criterion for doctrinal validity, even though reason plays a role in proof.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Defining Shari'ah and Usul in Hanafi Thought
Definition and terminological clarification of fundamental usul concepts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi definitions of sharī‘ah and uṣūl, and differentiate between dīn and millah based on the passage.

Core Idea
Sharī‘ah is the divine law; uṣūl are its firm principles; dīn and millah are two perspectives on the same reality.

In the opening of this usul commentary, the author provides precise definitions of key terms. He notes that ‘dīn’ and ‘millah’ refer to the same essential reality but differ in aspect: dīn emphasizes the religion itself, millah emphasizes the path or community. Sharī‘ah then is defined as the religion Allah prescribed for His servants, and uṣūl are the religious principles (the four proofs). This lesson unpacks these definitions.

Guided Path
1
Locate the terms
Find where the terms 'dīn', 'millah', 'sharī‘ah', and 'uṣūl' are explicitly discussed in the Arabic text.
Look at the beginning and near the middle of the passage.
2
Compare dīn and millah
Note that they share a single musammā (named reality) but differ in conceptualization: dīn focuses on the religion itself, millah on the path or community.
The author says: 'مسمیٰ ایک ہے اور اختلاف حیثیات کیوجہ سے اسامی مختلف ہیں'.
3
Confirm the Hanafi definitions
Extract the definition: sharī‘ah = the religion of Islam which Allah prescribed for His servants; uṣūl = the religious principles (the four sources).
The passage states: 'اصول الشریعہ میں شریعہ سے مراد دین اسلام ہے جو اللہ تعالی نے اپنے عباد کیلئے مشروع فرمایا اور اصول سے مراد القائد الدینیہ ہیں'.
4
Apply the distinction
Understand that uṣūl al-sharī‘ah means 'the principles of Islamic law' and refers to the four proofs, not just the laws themselves.
This sets the foundation for the rest of usul al-fiqh.

دین کہا جاتا ہے ۔ بایں حیثیت ان کی اسلام اور کتابت کرائی جاتی ہے تو اسے ملتہ کہا جاتا ہے۔ مسمیٰ ایک ہے اور اختلاف حیثیات کیوجہ سے اسامی مختلف ہیں۔ الغراء إلى البيضاء الوضحاء الوضاء میں فی خضار ورفع بخطابه خطاب کا معنی ہے تو جہہ الکلام نخوا حاضر پھر اس ں کلام کو بھی خطاب کہہ دیتے ہیں جس کے ساتھ خطاب واقع ہوا ہے یعنی ما تقع به التخاطب، فروع الحنيفية اى الملة الحنيفية الى السائلة من الباطل إلى الحق ويمكن ان تكون منسوبة الى سید نا ابراهیم علی نبینا و برنا علیہ اسلام کا قال الله تعالى فاتبع ملت ابراہیم مضيفا - السمحة الى السهلة لما فيها من رفع الاخر و الانحلال التي كانت على من قبلنا البيضاء لغاية وضوحها ونقائها عن دنس الارتياب - حتى اضحت ای صارت كلمته الباقية الى كلمة التوحيد - راسخة الاساس - راسخه بمعنى ضبوط و مستحکم اساس اصل اور بنیاد کو کہتے ہیں۔ شامخة البناء - اسی عالیہ بنا رہا اصلها ثابت وفرعها فی اسماء جیسے تفسیر میں آیا ہے کہ شجرہ طیبہ ہے کہ شجرہ طیبہ سے مراد نخلہ ہے جیسے اس کی جڑیں گہری اور مضبوط ہوتی ہیں اورث خیس آسمان کیجانب اونچی اسی طرح کلمہ طیبہ کے اصول مستحکم اور فروع نہایت بلند ہیں بالدلائل النقلية والعقلية حاصل یہ کہ اصول الشریعہ میں شریعہ سے مراد دین اسلام ہے جو اللہ تعالی نے اپنے عباد کیلئے مشروع فرمایا اور اصول سے مراد القائد الدینیہ ہیں اور احکام سے مراد مستحکم اور پخت کرنا ہے تو عقائد و علینہ کو اپنی کتاب سے اللہ تعالیٰ نے مستحکم فرما د یا اگرچه عقائد دینیہ کا اثبات دلائل عقلیہ سے ہوتا ہے انکا ثبوت کتاب اللہ پر موقوف نہیں ہے بکہ کتاب اللہ کا ثبوت موقوف على العقائد ہے کیونکہ جب تک وجود الیہ اور اس کی صفات از قسم کلام اور ارسال رسل کا اعتقاد اور اترار نہ ہو تو کتاب اللہ کیسے ثابت کی جاگتی ہے جو خدائے تعالیٰ کے وجود قائل نہیں ہے یا اس کی صفات کا قائل نہیں ہے وہ کتاب کا کتاب اللہ ہو تا کہاں تسلیم کر سکتا ہے ۔ لہذا اصول عقائد کا ثبوت موقوف علی الکتاب نہیں ہے۔ ورنہ تو دور لازم آئیگا البتہ عقائد من حیث الاعت داد موقوف علی الکتاب ہیں یعنی عقائد معتد بہا اور صحیح اسوقت ہوں گے جب کتا الشے کی روشنی کے مطابق ہوں ورنہ تو حکمہ الہیہ والے علماء بھی بحث عن العقائد کرتے ہیں چونکہ وہ وحی الہی کے نور کے مطابق نہیں ہے اس لئے معتد بہا نہیں ہیں تو عقائد چونکہ انکا راعت راد ثابت من الكتاب ہوتا ہے تو گویا ان کا استحکام کتاب اللہ العزیز سے ہوا اس لئے حکم یکتا بہ کہا اثبت نہیں کہا دوسرا فقره رفع بخطابہ الخ میں رفعت سے مراد اعلام قدر اور رفعتہ مرتبہ فی القبول ہے اور خطاب سے مراد خطاب اللہ تعالی المتعلق با فعال المکلفین مراد ہے اور فروع الحنيفية من فروع سے مراد
احکام عملیہ ہیں۔ بہر حال ان کی رفعت مرتبہ فی القبولیت خطاب اللہ العزیز الملک المین کے ساتھ حاصل ہے گلمته الباقیہ کلمہ سے مراد کلمہ شہادت ہے جو السنہ عباد پر الی یوم القیمہ باقی رہیگا اور اس کلمہ کی اساس ایمان اور تصدیق قلبی ہے چونکہ کلمہ شہادت احترار باللسان ہے آخر اقرار صحت عند الشرع موقوف على التصدیق ہے اور رسوخ سے مراد اطمینان قلب اور ازمان جنان ہے اور شامخ البناء میں بنار سے مراد العمل الصالح ہے جو اقتدار کی فرع اور نتیجہ ہے، تو اساس کلمہ کے رسوخ کو مرتب کیا علی احکام اصول الشريعة ، ارتفاع بناء کو مرتب کیا علی رفع مشروع الخفيفيه على طريقة اللف والنشر المرتب - أو قد من مشكوة الزاو قد من الايقاد بمعنی آتش افروختن اراد به الظهار المشكورة الكرة الغير النافذة التي يوضع فيها السراج لفظ مشكواة استعاره لصدر لنبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم وقلبہ ہے مشکواۃ جو مشبہ یہ ہے ذکر کیا اور مراد صدر النبوۃ ہے جو مشیر ہے تو استعارہ مصرحہ ہو گا اور سراج سے مراد احادیث وسنتہ کے الفاظ ہیں اور انوار سے مراد ان کے منطوقات اور مفہومات ہیں۔ ارقد کی نسبت اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف ہے جب کے اندر اشارہ ہے کہ احادیث اور سنتہ کا القاء بھی من جانب اللہ ہے جیسے فرمایا وما ینطق عن الهوى ان هو الا وحي يوحى - واوضح الاجماع الامراء علی اقتفاء ای اتباع آثار با ای آثار استه - قياسا ومنها جا۔ اسی طریقا واضحا تو براعتہ استمال کے طور پر اصول اربعہ کا بالترتیب ذکر کیا۔ احکم بکتا بہ میں کتاب اللہ کا مشکواۃ السنتہ میں سنہ پھر اجماع اور پھر قیاس کا ذکر فرمایا حقی صادفت بتارا الخطاب ای وجدت التقاد اور ایضاح پر یہ مرتب ہے۔ بخار علوم اور صدی کا متلاطم ہونا او قد پر مرتب ہے اور رایت الناس اوضح پر مرتب ہے یعنی مشکواۃ سنہ سے علوم دہری کے بار تلاطم ہوئے اور اجماع وآراء کے لئے جب قیاس و منہاج کی توضیح ہوئی تو لوگوں نے دین اسلام میں جوق در جوق داخل ہونا شروع کر دیا ۔ والصلوة محمد کے بعد یہ صلواۃ علی الرسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہے جو اس کتاب اور ملت حنیفیہ کے وصول الی العباد کا ذریعہ اور وسیلہ ہیں لہذا رفعت الک ذکرک کے مطابق بعد الحمد صلواۃ کا ذکر کرنا ضروری ہوتا ہے على من ارسله لساطع المحجة معوانا و ظهیرا۔ سطوع بمعنی ارتفاع ہے اور ساطع کی اضافت بطرف الحجتہ اضافہ صفت الى الموصوف ہے اسی الحجتہ الساطعہ اور لساطع کی جار مجرور معواناً کے متعلق ہے اور مجتہ ساطعہ سے قران حکیم کتاب اللہ اعزیز مراد ہے اور معوانا صحیفہ مبالغہ ہے بمعنی کثیر العونت اور ظہیر بعنی مستر الاعانہ کیونکہ فته امشبہ دال على الثبورت والدوام ہے سعوانا اور ظہیرا منصوب علی الفولیہ ہیں اور اس صورت میں ارسل کے ضمن میں معنی جعل ہوگا جیسے تین ہوتی ہو میں اور اگر تضمین نہ کی جائے تو پھر منصوب علی الحالیہ ہوں گے اسی ارسلہ حال کو نہ معوانا وظهيرا للحجة الساطعة -
It is called 'din'. In that regard, [when] they become Muslim and are made to write, then that is called 'millah'. The named reality is one, and due to difference of aspects, the names are different. 'Al-gharrā' ilā al-bayḍā' al-waḍḥā' al-waḍḍā' [contains] 'rafa'a bi-khiṭābihi' — the meaning of 'khitab' is 'toward the speech', present, then that speech is also called 'khitab' with which the address occurs, i.e., 'what one uses to address each other'. 'Furū' al-ḥanīfiyyah' i.e., the ḥanīfiyyah millah, from the deviation from falsehood to truth, and it can be attributed to our master Ibrahim (upon our Prophet and upon him peace), as Allah said: 'Follow the millah of Ibrahim' adding 'al-samḥah' to 'al-sahlah' because of what it contains of removing hardship and dissolution that were upon those before us. 'Al-bayḍā'' due to the utmost clarity and purity from the filth of doubt. Until it became, i.e., His remaining word, the word of tawhid. 'Rāsikhat al-asās' — 'rāsikhah' means firm and strong; 'asās' is the root and foundation. 'Shāmikhat al-binā'' — high building, its root is firm and its branches are in the heavens, as has come in the tafsir about the good tree, that the good tree refers to the date-palm, whose roots are deep and strong and its branches are high towards the sky; similarly, the principles of the good word are firm and its branches are extremely high with transmitted and rational proofs. The conclusion is that in 'uṣūl al-sharī‘ah', 'sharī‘ah' means the religion of Islam which Allah prescribed for His servants, and 'uṣūl' means the religious principles, and 'aḥkām' means to make firm and strong. So, beliefs and practices Allah made firm through His Book. Although the proof of religious beliefs is through rational proofs, their confirmation is not dependent on the Book of Allah; rather the Book of Allah's proof is dependent on beliefs. Because until belief in the existence of Allah, His attributes, the category of speech, and the sending of messengers, and affirmation is not present, how can the Book of Allah be proven? If someone does not believe in the existence of Allah or does not believe in His attributes, how can he accept that a book is the Book of Allah? Therefore, the proof of principles of faith is not dependent on the Book; otherwise a vicious circle would arise. However, beliefs, from the aspect of being considered, are dependent on the Book, i.e., beliefs are considered sound only when they accord with the light of the Book. Otherwise, the divine philosophers also discuss beliefs, but since they are not according to the light of divine revelation, they are not considered. So, since the confirmation of beliefs from the Book is proven, their firmness comes from the Book of Allah. That is why it is said 'aḥkama bi-kitābihī' (He made firm with His Book) not 'athbata' (He established). The second sentence: 'raf‘a bi-khiṭābihī' etc. — 'raf‘ah' means elevation of status and raising of rank in acceptance, and 'khiṭāb' refers to the address of Allah related to acts of the legally responsible. And 'furū' al-ḥanīfiyyah' — 'furū' means practical rulings. In any case, their elevation of rank in acceptance is with the address of Allah the Almighty, the Owner, the Secure. 'Kalimatuhu al-bāqiyah' — the word means the word of martyrdom (shahadah) which will remain on the tongues of servants until the Day of Resurrection. The foundation of this word is faith and heartfelt verification. Since the word of testimony is utterance by the tongue, its final acceptance in the Shari'ah is dependent on verification. And 'rasūkh' means tranquility of heart and certainty of the soul. And 'shāmikh al-binā' — 'binā'' refers to righteous actions, which are a branch and result of faith. So the firmness of the foundation of the word is linked to the rulings of the principles of Shari'ah, and the height of the building is linked to the elevation of the mild legislation — following the method of 'al-laff wa al-nashr al-murattab'. Or 'qadd min mishkāt al-zāw' — 'qadd' from 'al-īqād' meaning kindling fire; intended is the illumination of the 'mishkāt', the socket not pierced, in which the lamp is placed. The word 'mishkāh' is a metaphor for the chest of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his heart. 'Mishkāh' which is the metaphor is mentioned, and what is meant is the chest of prophethood which is illuminated, so it is an explicit metaphor. And 'sirāj' (lamp) means the words of hadith and sunnah, and 'anwār' (lights) means their apparent meanings and understood meanings. The attribution of 'awqad' (kindled) is to Allah, indicating that the inspiration of hadith and sunnah is also from Allah, as He said: 'Nor does he speak from desire; it is only revelation revealed.' And 'awḍaḥa al-ijmā‘a al-umarā’ ‘alā iqtifā’' i.e., following the traces, what traces? 'Qiyāsan wa minhā jāh' — in this clear way, with eloquence of style, he mentioned the four principles in order: 'Aḥkama bi-kitābihī' — the Book of Allah; 'mishkāt al-sunnah' — the Sunnah; then Ijma; then Qiyas. 'Ḥattā ṣādaftu bittāra al-khiṭāb' i.e., I found the conformity, and this is arranged upon clarification. 'Bakhār al-‘ulūm' (the boil of sciences) and the tumult of the chest is arranged upon 'awqad' (kindled), and 'ra’aytu al-nās' (I saw the people) is arranged upon 'awḍaḥa' (made clear), meaning: from the mishkāt of Sunnah the sciences began to boil, and when Ijma and opinions were clarified with Qiyas and methodology, people started entering into the religion of Islam in crowds. And after 'wa al-ṣalātu ‘alā Muḥammad' — this is prayer upon the Messenger (peace be upon him) who is the means and medium of this book and the Ḥanafī millah reaching the servants. Therefore, according to 'rafa‘nā laka dhikrak' (We have raised for you your mention), it is necessary to mention prayer after praise. Upon him whom He sent for the bright path, a helper and supporter. 'Sutū‘' means elevation, and the addition of 'sāṭi‘' to 'al-ḥujjah' is an attributive addition. 'Sāṭi‘ah' — the bright proof. 'Ma‘wanan' and 'ẓahīran' are accusative as adverbs, and in this case 'arsala' includes the meaning of 'ja‘ala' (made), like 'innī ja‘altu‘'. And if 'taḍmīn' is not applied, then they are accusative as 'ḥāl'. So he sent him as a helper and supporter for the bright proof.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is an introductory commentary from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work, likely explaining the opening of Al-Tawdih or Al-Talwih. The author begins by clarifying terminology: 'din' and 'millah' refer to the same reality but from different perspectives—'din' when considering the religion itself, 'millah' when considering it as a path or writing. The author then elaborates on the phrase 'al-gharrā' ilā al-bayḍā' al-waḍḥā' al-waḍḍā'', likely from the matn, explaining that 'rafa'a bi-khiṭābihi' refers to the address of Allah which elevates status. The 'furū' al-ḥanīfiyyah' (the branches of the Hanafi millah) are the practical rulings derived from the address of Allah. The passage emphasizes that the foundation (asl) of the 'kalimah al-ṭayyibah' (the good word of tawhid) is firm faith, and its branches are righteous deeds. The author then discusses the relationship between rational proofs and revealed texts: while rational proofs can establish the existence of Allah, the confirmation of correct beliefs depends on the Quran; otherwise a vicious circle would arise. This is a key Hanafi usul point: the Quran is the primary source for creed, but its own acceptance depends on prior belief in Allah and prophethood. The author then explains the metaphor of the mishkāt (niche) and sirāj (lamp), where the Prophet's heart is the niche and the words of Sunnah are the lamp, indicating that both Quran and Sunnah are divine revelation. Finally, the four sources (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) are presented in order, and the passage concludes with the necessity of sending salawat on the Prophet after praising Allah, as he is the means of conveying this knowledge.

Key Terms
شریعہ (sharī‘ah): The religion of Islam that Allah prescribed for His servants.
اصول (uṣūl): The religious principles; the foundations and sources of the Shari'ah.
ملت (millah): The divinely ordained path or community; specifically used for the religion of Ibrahim and Islam.
دین (dīn): The religion of Islam in its essence; the comprehensive reality of faith and practice.
کلمہ (kalimah): The word of tawhid (shahadah), which is the foundation of faith.
مشکواة (mishkāt): A metaphor for the chest or heart of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that holds the light of revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between dīn and millah?
A) They are completely different concepts
B) They are the same reality but differ in aspect
C) Millah is a subset of dīn
D) Dīn is the source of millah

Key Takeaway
Sharī‘ah is the prescribed divine law; uṣūl are its principles; dīn and millah are two perspectives on the same reality.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
The Four Sources of Hanafi Law and the Mishkāt Metaphor
Presentation of the four sources and theological grounding of Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four sources of Hanafi usul in order and explain the mishkāt metaphor linking the Sunnah to divine revelation.

Core Idea
The four sources are Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas; the Sunnah is divine revelation just like the Quran.

This passage explicitly presents the four foundational sources of Islamic law in the Hanafi school. The author uses the beautiful metaphor of the 'mishkāt' (niche) from the Quran to affirm that the words of the Prophet are not from his own desire but from divine inspiration. Understanding this hierarchical order is essential for any student of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Find the list of sources
In the Arabic text, identify where the author enumerates the sources: 'أحكم بكتابه' (Quran), 'مشكاة السنة' (Sunnah), then Ijma, then Qiyas.
The phrase 'اضول اربعہ' (four principles) signals the enumeration.
2
Understand the order
Note the sequence: Quran first, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas. This reflects their relative strength and priority in Hanafi istidlal.
The source text says 'بالترتیب' (in order).
3
Analyze the mishkāt metaphor
The phrase 'or qadd min mishkāt al-zāw' is an allusion to the Verse of Light (24:35). The author explains that the 'mishkāt' is the Prophet's chest/heart, and the 'sirāj' (lamp) is the words of hadith. This shows that the Sunnah is divinely inspired.
The author quotes 'Nor does he speak from desire' (53:3-4) to support this.
4
Recognize the epistemological significance
By placing Sunnah immediately after Quran and using revelation language, the author establishes that both are primary sources (waḥy). This is crucial for Hanafi usul's claim that Sunnah is an independent source of obligation.
This differentiates from views that treat Sunnah only as an explanation of Quran.

دین کہا جاتا ہے ۔ بایں حیثیت ان کی اسلام اور کتابت کرائی جاتی ہے تو اسے ملتہ کہا جاتا ہے۔ مسمیٰ ایک ہے اور اختلاف حیثیات کیوجہ سے اسامی مختلف ہیں۔ الغراء إلى البيضاء الوضحاء الوضاء میں فی خضار ورفع بخطابه خطاب کا معنی ہے تو جہہ الکلام نخوا حاضر پھر اس ں کلام کو بھی خطاب کہہ دیتے ہیں جس کے ساتھ خطاب واقع ہوا ہے یعنی ما تقع به التخاطب، فروع الحنيفية اى الملة الحنيفية الى السائلة من الباطل إلى الحق ويمكن ان تكون منسوبة الى سید نا ابراهیم علی نبینا و برنا علیہ اسلام کا قال الله تعالى فاتبع ملت ابراہیم مضيفا - السمحة الى السهلة لما فيها من رفع الاخر و الانحلال التي كانت على من قبلنا البيضاء لغاية وضوحها ونقائها عن دنس الارتياب - حتى اضحت ای صارت كلمته الباقية الى كلمة التوحيد - راسخة الاساس - راسخه بمعنى ضبوط و مستحکم اساس اصل اور بنیاد کو کہتے ہیں۔ شامخة البناء - اسی عالیہ بنا رہا اصلها ثابت وفرعها فی اسماء جیسے تفسیر میں آیا ہے کہ شجرہ طیبہ ہے کہ شجرہ طیبہ سے مراد نخلہ ہے جیسے اس کی جڑیں گہری اور مضبوط ہوتی ہیں اورث خیس آسمان کیجانب اونچی اسی طرح کلمہ طیبہ کے اصول مستحکم اور فروع نہایت بلند ہیں بالدلائل النقلية والعقلية حاصل یہ کہ اصول الشریعہ میں شریعہ سے مراد دین اسلام ہے جو اللہ تعالی نے اپنے عباد کیلئے مشروع فرمایا اور اصول سے مراد القائد الدینیہ ہیں اور احکام سے مراد مستحکم اور پخت کرنا ہے تو عقائد و علینہ کو اپنی کتاب سے اللہ تعالیٰ نے مستحکم فرما د یا اگرچه عقائد دینیہ کا اثبات دلائل عقلیہ سے ہوتا ہے انکا ثبوت کتاب اللہ پر موقوف نہیں ہے بکہ کتاب اللہ کا ثبوت موقوف على العقائد ہے کیونکہ جب تک وجود الیہ اور اس کی صفات از قسم کلام اور ارسال رسل کا اعتقاد اور اترار نہ ہو تو کتاب اللہ کیسے ثابت کی جاگتی ہے جو خدائے تعالیٰ کے وجود قائل نہیں ہے یا اس کی صفات کا قائل نہیں ہے وہ کتاب کا کتاب اللہ ہو تا کہاں تسلیم کر سکتا ہے ۔ لہذا اصول عقائد کا ثبوت موقوف علی الکتاب نہیں ہے۔ ورنہ تو دور لازم آئیگا البتہ عقائد من حیث الاعت داد موقوف علی الکتاب ہیں یعنی عقائد معتد بہا اور صحیح اسوقت ہوں گے جب کتا الشے کی روشنی کے مطابق ہوں ورنہ تو حکمہ الہیہ والے علماء بھی بحث عن العقائد کرتے ہیں چونکہ وہ وحی الہی کے نور کے مطابق نہیں ہے اس لئے معتد بہا نہیں ہیں تو عقائد چونکہ انکا راعت راد ثابت من الكتاب ہوتا ہے تو گویا ان کا استحکام کتاب اللہ العزیز سے ہوا اس لئے حکم یکتا بہ کہا اثبت نہیں کہا دوسرا فقره رفع بخطابہ الخ میں رفعت سے مراد اعلام قدر اور رفعتہ مرتبہ فی القبول ہے اور خطاب سے مراد خطاب اللہ تعالی المتعلق با فعال المکلفین مراد ہے اور فروع الحنيفية من فروع سے مراد
احکام عملیہ ہیں۔ بہر حال ان کی رفعت مرتبہ فی القبولیت خطاب اللہ العزیز الملک المین کے ساتھ حاصل ہے گلمته الباقیہ کلمہ سے مراد کلمہ شہادت ہے جو السنہ عباد پر الی یوم القیمہ باقی رہیگا اور اس کلمہ کی اساس ایمان اور تصدیق قلبی ہے چونکہ کلمہ شہادت احترار باللسان ہے آخر اقرار صحت عند الشرع موقوف على التصدیق ہے اور رسوخ سے مراد اطمینان قلب اور ازمان جنان ہے اور شامخ البناء میں بنار سے مراد العمل الصالح ہے جو اقتدار کی فرع اور نتیجہ ہے، تو اساس کلمہ کے رسوخ کو مرتب کیا علی احکام اصول الشريعة ، ارتفاع بناء کو مرتب کیا علی رفع مشروع الخفيفيه على طريقة اللف والنشر المرتب - أو قد من مشكوة الزاو قد من الايقاد بمعنی آتش افروختن اراد به الظهار المشكورة الكرة الغير النافذة التي يوضع فيها السراج لفظ مشكواة استعاره لصدر لنبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم وقلبہ ہے مشکواۃ جو مشبہ یہ ہے ذکر کیا اور مراد صدر النبوۃ ہے جو مشیر ہے تو استعارہ مصرحہ ہو گا اور سراج سے مراد احادیث وسنتہ کے الفاظ ہیں اور انوار سے مراد ان کے منطوقات اور مفہومات ہیں۔ ارقد کی نسبت اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف ہے جب کے اندر اشارہ ہے کہ احادیث اور سنتہ کا القاء بھی من جانب اللہ ہے جیسے فرمایا وما ینطق عن الهوى ان هو الا وحي يوحى - واوضح الاجماع الامراء علی اقتفاء ای اتباع آثار با ای آثار استه - قياسا ومنها جا۔ اسی طریقا واضحا تو براعتہ استمال کے طور پر اصول اربعہ کا بالترتیب ذکر کیا۔ احکم بکتا بہ میں کتاب اللہ کا مشکواۃ السنتہ میں سنہ پھر اجماع اور پھر قیاس کا ذکر فرمایا حقی صادفت بتارا الخطاب ای وجدت التقاد اور ایضاح پر یہ مرتب ہے۔ بخار علوم اور صدی کا متلاطم ہونا او قد پر مرتب ہے اور رایت الناس اوضح پر مرتب ہے یعنی مشکواۃ سنہ سے علوم دہری کے بار تلاطم ہوئے اور اجماع وآراء کے لئے جب قیاس و منہاج کی توضیح ہوئی تو لوگوں نے دین اسلام میں جوق در جوق داخل ہونا شروع کر دیا ۔ والصلوة محمد کے بعد یہ صلواۃ علی الرسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہے جو اس کتاب اور ملت حنیفیہ کے وصول الی العباد کا ذریعہ اور وسیلہ ہیں لہذا رفعت الک ذکرک کے مطابق بعد الحمد صلواۃ کا ذکر کرنا ضروری ہوتا ہے على من ارسله لساطع المحجة معوانا و ظهیرا۔ سطوع بمعنی ارتفاع ہے اور ساطع کی اضافت بطرف الحجتہ اضافہ صفت الى الموصوف ہے اسی الحجتہ الساطعہ اور لساطع کی جار مجرور معواناً کے متعلق ہے اور مجتہ ساطعہ سے قران حکیم کتاب اللہ اعزیز مراد ہے اور معوانا صحیفہ مبالغہ ہے بمعنی کثیر العونت اور ظہیر بعنی مستر الاعانہ کیونکہ فته امشبہ دال على الثبورت والدوام ہے سعوانا اور ظہیرا منصوب علی الفولیہ ہیں اور اس صورت میں ارسل کے ضمن میں معنی جعل ہوگا جیسے تین ہوتی ہو میں اور اگر تضمین نہ کی جائے تو پھر منصوب علی الحالیہ ہوں گے اسی ارسلہ حال کو نہ معوانا وظهيرا للحجة الساطعة -
It is called 'din'. In that regard, [when] they become Muslim and are made to write, then that is called 'millah'. The named reality is one, and due to difference of aspects, the names are different. 'Al-gharrā' ilā al-bayḍā' al-waḍḥā' al-waḍḍā' [contains] 'rafa'a bi-khiṭābihi' — the meaning of 'khitab' is 'toward the speech', present, then that speech is also called 'khitab' with which the address occurs, i.e., 'what one uses to address each other'. 'Furū' al-ḥanīfiyyah' i.e., the ḥanīfiyyah millah, from the deviation from falsehood to truth, and it can be attributed to our master Ibrahim (upon our Prophet and upon him peace), as Allah said: 'Follow the millah of Ibrahim' adding 'al-samḥah' to 'al-sahlah' because of what it contains of removing hardship and dissolution that were upon those before us. 'Al-bayḍā'' due to the utmost clarity and purity from the filth of doubt. Until it became, i.e., His remaining word, the word of tawhid. 'Rāsikhat al-asās' — 'rāsikhah' means firm and strong; 'asās' is the root and foundation. 'Shāmikhat al-binā'' — high building, its root is firm and its branches are in the heavens, as has come in the tafsir about the good tree, that the good tree refers to the date-palm, whose roots are deep and strong and its branches are high towards the sky; similarly, the principles of the good word are firm and its branches are extremely high with transmitted and rational proofs. The conclusion is that in 'uṣūl al-sharī‘ah', 'sharī‘ah' means the religion of Islam which Allah prescribed for His servants, and 'uṣūl' means the religious principles, and 'aḥkām' means to make firm and strong. So, beliefs and practices Allah made firm through His Book. Although the proof of religious beliefs is through rational proofs, their confirmation is not dependent on the Book of Allah; rather the Book of Allah's proof is dependent on beliefs. Because until belief in the existence of Allah, His attributes, the category of speech, and the sending of messengers, and affirmation is not present, how can the Book of Allah be proven? If someone does not believe in the existence of Allah or does not believe in His attributes, how can he accept that a book is the Book of Allah? Therefore, the proof of principles of faith is not dependent on the Book; otherwise a vicious circle would arise. However, beliefs, from the aspect of being considered, are dependent on the Book, i.e., beliefs are considered sound only when they accord with the light of the Book. Otherwise, the divine philosophers also discuss beliefs, but since they are not according to the light of divine revelation, they are not considered. So, since the confirmation of beliefs from the Book is proven, their firmness comes from the Book of Allah. That is why it is said 'aḥkama bi-kitābihī' (He made firm with His Book) not 'athbata' (He established). The second sentence: 'raf‘a bi-khiṭābihī' etc. — 'raf‘ah' means elevation of status and raising of rank in acceptance, and 'khiṭāb' refers to the address of Allah related to acts of the legally responsible. And 'furū' al-ḥanīfiyyah' — 'furū' means practical rulings. In any case, their elevation of rank in acceptance is with the address of Allah the Almighty, the Owner, the Secure. 'Kalimatuhu al-bāqiyah' — the word means the word of martyrdom (shahadah) which will remain on the tongues of servants until the Day of Resurrection. The foundation of this word is faith and heartfelt verification. Since the word of testimony is utterance by the tongue, its final acceptance in the Shari'ah is dependent on verification. And 'rasūkh' means tranquility of heart and certainty of the soul. And 'shāmikh al-binā' — 'binā'' refers to righteous actions, which are a branch and result of faith. So the firmness of the foundation of the word is linked to the rulings of the principles of Shari'ah, and the height of the building is linked to the elevation of the mild legislation — following the method of 'al-laff wa al-nashr al-murattab'. Or 'qadd min mishkāt al-zāw' — 'qadd' from 'al-īqād' meaning kindling fire; intended is the illumination of the 'mishkāt', the socket not pierced, in which the lamp is placed. The word 'mishkāh' is a metaphor for the chest of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his heart. 'Mishkāh' which is the metaphor is mentioned, and what is meant is the chest of prophethood which is illuminated, so it is an explicit metaphor. And 'sirāj' (lamp) means the words of hadith and sunnah, and 'anwār' (lights) means their apparent meanings and understood meanings. The attribution of 'awqad' (kindled) is to Allah, indicating that the inspiration of hadith and sunnah is also from Allah, as He said: 'Nor does he speak from desire; it is only revelation revealed.' And 'awḍaḥa al-ijmā‘a al-umarā’ ‘alā iqtifā’' i.e., following the traces, what traces? 'Qiyāsan wa minhā jāh' — in this clear way, with eloquence of style, he mentioned the four principles in order: 'Aḥkama bi-kitābihī' — the Book of Allah; 'mishkāt al-sunnah' — the Sunnah; then Ijma; then Qiyas. 'Ḥattā ṣādaftu bittāra al-khiṭāb' i.e., I found the conformity, and this is arranged upon clarification. 'Bakhār al-‘ulūm' (the boil of sciences) and the tumult of the chest is arranged upon 'awqad' (kindled), and 'ra’aytu al-nās' (I saw the people) is arranged upon 'awḍaḥa' (made clear), meaning: from the mishkāt of Sunnah the sciences began to boil, and when Ijma and opinions were clarified with Qiyas and methodology, people started entering into the religion of Islam in crowds. And after 'wa al-ṣalātu ‘alā Muḥammad' — this is prayer upon the Messenger (peace be upon him) who is the means and medium of this book and the Ḥanafī millah reaching the servants. Therefore, according to 'rafa‘nā laka dhikrak' (We have raised for you your mention), it is necessary to mention prayer after praise. Upon him whom He sent for the bright path, a helper and supporter. 'Sutū‘' means elevation, and the addition of 'sāṭi‘' to 'al-ḥujjah' is an attributive addition. 'Sāṭi‘ah' — the bright proof. 'Ma‘wanan' and 'ẓahīran' are accusative as adverbs, and in this case 'arsala' includes the meaning of 'ja‘ala' (made), like 'innī ja‘altu‘'. And if 'taḍmīn' is not applied, then they are accusative as 'ḥāl'. So he sent him as a helper and supporter for the bright proof.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is an introductory commentary from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work, likely explaining the opening of Al-Tawdih or Al-Talwih. The author begins by clarifying terminology: 'din' and 'millah' refer to the same reality but from different perspectives—'din' when considering the religion itself, 'millah' when considering it as a path or writing. The author then elaborates on the phrase 'al-gharrā' ilā al-bayḍā' al-waḍḥā' al-waḍḍā'', likely from the matn, explaining that 'rafa'a bi-khiṭābihi' refers to the address of Allah which elevates status. The 'furū' al-ḥanīfiyyah' (the branches of the Hanafi millah) are the practical rulings derived from the address of Allah. The passage emphasizes that the foundation (asl) of the 'kalimah al-ṭayyibah' (the good word of tawhid) is firm faith, and its branches are righteous deeds. The author then discusses the relationship between rational proofs and revealed texts: while rational proofs can establish the existence of Allah, the confirmation of correct beliefs depends on the Quran; otherwise a vicious circle would arise. This is a key Hanafi usul point: the Quran is the primary source for creed, but its own acceptance depends on prior belief in Allah and prophethood. The author then explains the metaphor of the mishkāt (niche) and sirāj (lamp), where the Prophet's heart is the niche and the words of Sunnah are the lamp, indicating that both Quran and Sunnah are divine revelation. Finally, the four sources (Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) are presented in order, and the passage concludes with the necessity of sending salawat on the Prophet after praising Allah, as he is the means of conveying this knowledge.

Key Terms
شریعہ (sharī‘ah): The religion of Islam that Allah prescribed for His servants.
اصول (uṣūl): The religious principles; the foundations and sources of the Shari'ah.
اجماع (ijmā‘): Consensus of the scholars of the Islamic community.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical deduction from existing rulings.
مشکواة (mishkāt): A metaphor for the chest or heart of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that holds the light of revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the four sources of Islamic law mentioned in the order of arrangement?
A) Quran, Ijma, Sunnah, Qiyas
B) Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas
C) Sunnah, Quran, Qiyas, Ijma
D) Ijma, Quran, Sunnah, Qiyas

Key Takeaway
The four sources of Hanafi usul are Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas; the Sunnah is divinely inspired revelation, as symbolized by the mishkāt metaphor.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
The Four Sources of Islamic Law: The Author's Preface
Commentary on the author's preface explaining the four sources and their derivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four sources of Islamic law as presented in the Hanafi preface, explain their hierarchical order, and interpret the metaphorical language used to describe them.

Core Idea
The four sources are presented hierarchically: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, each building on the previous.

This passage is a commentary on the introductory section of a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work. The author begins with praise and salutation, then clarifies that the four principles of Islamic law are derived in a specific sequence. The commentary uses rich metaphorical language—comparing the Prophet's heart to a lamp niche that holds the light of revelation—to emphasize the source and authority of each principle. Understanding this preface is key to grasping the structure of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rhetorical structure
The preface opens with praise of Allah, then salutation upon the Prophet. Recognize that this is not mere formality; it establishes the authority of revelation and the Prophet as the medium of transmission.
This pattern is common in classical texts.
2
Locate the four sources
The text explicitly mentions the four sources in order: 'Ahkam bi Kitabih' (the Book of Allah), then 'Mishkat al-Sunnah' (the Sunnah), then 'Ijma' (consensus), then 'Qiyas' (analogy). Note the deliberate sequence.
The order reflects decreasing priority: Quran → Sunnah → Ijma → Qiyas.
3
Interpret the metaphorical language
The commentary explains the metaphor of the lamp (mishkah) for the Prophet's chest, the lamp (siraj) for the words of hadith, and the lights (anwar) for the meanings. This imagery underscores that the Sunnah is a form of divine guidance.
The metaphor is taken from Quran 24:35 (the Light verse).
4
Understand the implied hierarchy
The sequence of mention is not random; it reflects the rank and priority of each source. The Quran is the ultimate foundation, followed by the Sunnah which derives from it, then Ijma which depends on both, and finally Qiyas which is extrapolation.
Hanafis consider this hierarchy essential for istinbat.
5
Recognize the role of istishab and istihsan
These terms appear in the salutation on the Companions, indicating that they adhered to the prophetic indications and held fast to clear texts. It hints at the secondary sources later discussed in usul.
Istishab and istihsan are specifically Hanafi tools.

احکام عملیہ ہیں۔ بہر حال ان کی رفعت مرتبہ فی القبولیت خطاب اللہ العزیز الملک المین کے ساتھ حاصل ہے۔ کلمہ سے مراد کلمہ شہادت ہے جو السنہ عباد پر الی یوم القیمہ باقی رہیگا اور اس کلمہ کی اساس ایمان اور تصدیق قلبی ہے۔ چونکہ کلمہ شہادت احترار باللسان ہے آخر اقرار صحت عند الشرع موقوف على التصدیق ہے۔ اور رسوخ سے مراد اطمینان قلب اور ازمان جنان ہے۔ اور شامخ البناء میں بنا سے مراد العمل الصالح ہے جو اقتدار کی فرع اور نتیجہ ہے۔ تو اساس کلمہ کے رسوخ کو مرتب کیا علی احکام اصول الشریعة، ارتفاع بناء کو مرتب کیا علی رفع مشروع الخفيفيه على طريقة اللف والنشر المرتب. أو قد من مشكوة الزاو قد من الايقاد بمعنی آتش افروختن اراد به الظهار المشكورة الكرة الغير النافذة التي يوضع فيها السراج. لفظ مشكوة استعاره لصدر لنبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم وقلبہ ہے۔ مشکواۃ جو مشبہ ہے ذکر کیا اور مراد صدر النبوۃ ہے جو مشیر ہے تو استعارہ مصرحہ ہو گا۔ اور سراج سے مراد احادیث وسنتہ کے الفاظ ہیں۔ اور انوار سے مراد ان کے منطوقات اور مفہومات ہیں۔ ارقد کی نسبت اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف ہے جب کے اندر اشارہ ہے کہ احادیث اور سنتہ کا القاء بھی من جانب اللہ ہے جیسے فرمایا وما ینطق عن الهوى ان هو الا وحي يوحى. واوضح الاجماع الامراء علی اقتفاء ای اتباع آثار با ای آثار استه. قياسا ومنها جا. اسی طریقا واضحا تو براعتہ استمال کے طور پر اصول اربعہ کا بالترتیب ذکر کیا۔ احکم بکتا بہ میں کتاب اللہ کا مشکواۃ السنتہ میں سنہ پھر اجماع اور پھر قیاس کا ذکر فرمایا۔ حقی صادفت بتارا الخطاب ای وجدت التقاد اور ایضاح پر یہ مرتب ہے۔ بخار علوم اور صدی کا متلاطم ہونا او قد پر مرتب ہے اور رایت الناس اوضح پر مرتب ہے یعنی مشکواۃ سنہ سے علوم دہری کے بار تلاطم ہوئے اور اجماع وآراء کے لئے جب قیاس و منہاج کی توضیح ہوئی تو لوگوں نے دین اسلام میں جوق در جوق داخل ہونا شروع کر دیا۔ والصلوة محمد کے بعد یہ صلواۃ علی الرسول صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہے جو اس کتاب اور ملت حنیفیہ کے وصول الی العباد کا ذریعہ اور وسیلہ ہیں لہذا رفعت الک ذکرک کے مطابق بعد الحمد صلواۃ کا ذکر کرنا ضروری ہوتا ہے۔ على من ارسله لساطع المحجة معوانا و ظهیرا۔ سطوع بمعنی ارتفاع ہے اور ساطع کی اضافت بطرف الحجتہ اضافہ صفت الى الموصوف ہے اسی الحجتہ الساطعہ اور لساطع کی جار مجرور معواناً کے متعلق ہے۔ اور مجتہ ساطعہ سے قران حکیم کتاب اللہ اعزیز مراد ہے۔ اور معوانا صحیفہ مبالغہ ہے بمعنی کثیر العونت اور ظہیر بعنی مستر الاعانہ کیونکہ فته امشبہ دال على الثبورت والدوام ہے۔ سعوانا اور ظہیرا منصوب علی الفولیہ ہیں اور اس صورت میں ارسل کے ضمن میں معنی جعل ہوگا جیسے تین ہوتی ہو میں اور اگر تضمین نہ کی جائے تو پھر منصوب علی الحالیہ ہوں گے اسی ارسلہ حال کو نہ معوانا وظهيرا للحجة الساطعة. وجعله الواضح المحجة سلطانا نصيرا المحجبة جادة الطريق بشيرا ونذيرا نذير المعنى ذا انذار او بمینی سمندر اور نیل مینی مفعل مستعمل ہے کیا جار نے قول الشاعر امن ریکا الداعی السمیع تو اسمیں سمیع بمعنی مری ہے۔ تم علان التزم ثمر تراخی رتبی کیلئے ہے کیونکہ صلوٰۃ و سلام رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر اصالہ ہے۔ اور صحابہ کرام رضوان اللہ علیہم اجم اجمعین پر پر تبت اغت نو خداشی فیتہ فی شریف ساخته اس میں اضافہ صفتہ الی الوصوف ہے اصل میں ہے في ساحة الشريفه، ساحة الدارفتار با یعنی فنار دار کو ساحہ کہتے ہیں یعنی صحن اور میدانی حصہ۔ كرامة الاستصحاب والاستحسان والكلمة اسم من التكريم بمعنى العظمية والتعظيم. استصحاب جعل اشتي مصاحب النفہ یعنی اپنے لئے کسی کو صاحب اور ساتھی بنالینا۔ والاستحسان عدایشی حسنا ایک شیر کو حسن شمار کرنا اور حسین سمجھنا۔ حاصل معنی یہ ہے کہ صلوہ نازل ہو ان حضرات پر جنہوں نے اپنے آپ پر لازم کر رکھا ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے اشارات کے موافق طریق عرفان و معرفت پر دلالت اور رہنمائی کرتے رہیں گے اور اس ہدایت اور رہنمائی میں جو نصوص ظاہرۃ البیان تھی انکو مضبوطی کے ساتھ تھاما اور پکڑا اور جو رسول اللہ صلی للہ علیہ وسلم نے اپنے ساختہ شریفہ میں ان کو اپنا صاحب اور ساتھی بنانے اور انھیں مستحسن قرار دینے کی کرامتہ اور فضیلہ سے نوازا اسکو انہوں نے اپنے لئے عظیمتر شمار کیا۔ المهاجرين والانصار - وہ حضرات جو ان اوصاف مثلثة من الالتزام و الاعتصام والاغتنام کے موصوف تھے جو کہ مہم تھے من انها جرین والانصار کے ساتھ تبیین کر کے ازالہ ابہام کر دیا۔ والذين اتبعوهم باحسان ۔ اس کا عطف من التزام پر ہے اس گراد تابعین اور تبع تابعین ہیں جو تاخر زمانی کیوجہ سے نعمت استصحاب و استحان تو حاصل نہ کر سکے لیکن مہاجری است اور انصار کی اتباع مستحسن طریق پر کی وہ اس صلواۃ میں درج ہیں اور احسان سے مراد یا تو عمل صالح ہر یاد ہی درجہ علیا ہے ان تعبد الله كانك تراه۔ وبعت من فإن علم الاصول میں وار کے متعلق کہا جاتا ہے کہ یہ بعوض اما ہے میں لیئے خان پر فاجزا ئیہ لائی گئی ہے یا داؤ عطف کی ہے لیکن ہو گا عطف القصہ علی القصہ۔ عطف اللہ علی امجلہ اچھا نہیں ہے کیونکہ ماقبل میں انشار حمد وصلوٰہ ہے جو معنی جملہ انشائیہ ہے جملہ خبریہ ہے عطف خبریہ علی الانث نیہ ہو جائیگا جو ستمن نہیں ہے اس لئے عطف القصیر علی القصہ بنایا جائے۔ شارح چونکہ یہ کتاب فن اصول فقہ میں تصنیف فرما رہے ہیں تو یہاں سے علت تعیین فن یش کر رہے ہیں فر ماتے ہیں کہ علم الاصول جو کہ جامع بین المعقول و منقول ہے کیونکہ اس فن
These are practical rulings. Nevertheless, their high rank in acceptance is obtained with the address of Allah, the Mighty, the King. 'Kalimah' means the word of testimony, which will remain on the tongues of servants until the Day of Judgment, and the foundation of this word is faith and heartfelt confirmation. Since the word of testimony is utterance by the tongue, ultimately the validity of acceptance in the law is dependent on confirmation. And 'firmness' means tranquility of heart and stability of the innermost self. And in 'lofty building', 'building' means righteous action, which is a branch and result of faith. So the firmness of the word is linked to the rulings of the principles of Sharia, and the elevation of the building is linked to the raising of the prescribed light things, in the manner of ordered dissemination. Or from the niche of the lamp, from the kindling meaning lighting a fire, intending by it the shining lamp, the solid glass sphere in which the wick is placed. The word 'mishkah' is a metaphor for the chest of the Prophet, peace be upon him, and his heart. The niche which is the thing being likened is mentioned, and what is meant is the chest of prophethood, which is the pointed-to thing, so it is an explicit metaphor. And by 'lamp' is meant the words of hadiths and Sunnah. And by 'lights' are meant their expressed and implied meanings. 'Kindling' is attributed to Allah, indicating that the imparting of hadiths and Sunnah is also from Allah, as He said: 'And he does not speak from desire; it is but revelation revealed.' And he clarified consensus, that the leaders are upon following, i.e., following the traces, whatever traces. By analogy and from it. In this clear way, he mentioned the four principles in order: in 'Ahkam bi Kitabih' he mentioned the Book of Allah, then in 'Mishkat al-Sunnah' the Sunnah, then consensus, then analogy. Truly, I found the presentation arranged thus. The billowing of the sciences and the vehemence is built upon this, and I saw the people upon clarification, meaning from the lamp of the Sunnah the waves of religious sciences billowed, and for consensus and opinions, when the clarification of analogy and methodology came, people began to enter Islam in droves. And after 'al-Salat' upon Muhammad, this is salutation upon the Messenger, peace be upon him, who is the means of transmission of this book and the Hanafi school to the servants, hence after praise, mentioning salutation is necessary, as his rank is elevated. Upon whom He sent as a helper and supporter for the luminous path. 'Satu' means elevation, and the addition of 'sati'' to 'hujjah' is an addition of attribute to the described, i.e., the brilliant proof. And 'li-sati'' is a prepositional phrase related to 'mu'awanan'. And by 'the brilliant proof' is meant the Wise Quran, the Mighty Book of Allah. And 'mu'awanan' is an exaggerated form meaning very helpful, and 'zahiran' meaning one who gives assistance, because the form fa'il indicates permanence and continuity. 'Mu'awanan' and 'zahiran' are accusative as predication, and in this case the verb 'arsala' implies the meaning of 'ja'ala' (to make), like in 'ta'ni'? And if the implication is not accepted, then they are accusative as circumstantial accusatives, i.e., 'arsalahu' in a state of being a helper and supporter for the brilliant proof. And He made the clear path a powerful helper, the road, a bearer of glad tidings and a warner. The meaning of 'nadhir' is one who warns, or like a sea and Nile? 'Muf'il' is used. The poet said: 'Amman ra'ayta al-da'i al-sami'' thus 'sami'' meaning 'muri'? You have adopted the consequence of distance in rank because salutation and peace upon the Messenger, peace be upon him, is fundamental. And upon the noble Companions, may Allah be pleased with them all, specifically those who adhered to the noble court, in which there is an addition of attribute to the described, originally 'in the noble court', 'sahat al-dar' means the courtyard, i.e., the open space of the house. The honor of istishab and istihsan, and the word is a noun of takrim meaning greatness and glorification. Istishab means taking someone as a companion for oneself. Istihsan means counting something as good. The sum meaning is that salutation be sent upon those who have made it incumbent upon themselves to continue to indicate and guide to the way of gnosis and recognition in accordance with the indications of the Messenger, peace be upon him, and in this guidance they firmly held onto the texts that were clear in their statement, and the honor and virtue by which the Messenger, peace be upon him, made them his companions in his noble court and deemed them excellent, they considered as great for themselves. The Muhajirun and Ansar - those who were described with these three attributes: commitment, adherence, and acquisition, which were important, and they explained them by mentioning the Muhajirun and Ansar to remove ambiguity. 'And those who followed them in excellence' - this is connected to 'commitment', meaning the Followers and the Followers of the Followers who, due to temporal delay, did not obtain the blessings of istishab and istihsan, but they followed the Muhajirun and Ansar in an excellent manner, so they are included in this salutation. And 'excellence' means either righteous action or the highest rank, i.e., 'that you worship Allah as if you see Him.' And in 'science of principles', it is said that 'wa' is for substitution or for conjunction, but it is conjunction of a story to a story. Conjoining a nominal sentence to a verbal one is not good because the previous is composed of praise and salutation, which is a declarative sentence, so conjoining a declarative sentence to an imperative would be problematic; therefore it is taken as conjunction of a story to a story. The commentator, since this book is composed in the field of usul al-fiqh, he now states the reason for defining the field, saying that the science of usul al-fiqh which combines the rational and the transmitted, because this field...
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This is a commentary on the introductory part (khatibah) of the book, which is a typical feature of classical works where the author begins with praise of Allah, salutation upon the Prophet, and an explanation of the subject matter. The commentator expands upon the metaphors used by the matn author, particularly the imagery of a lamp (mishkah) representing the Prophet's chest and heart, and the lamp representing the words of hadith and Sunnah. The main point is to show that the four sources of Islamic law (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) are derived in a hierarchical order, each subsequent source building upon the previous. The author also explains that the salutation upon the Prophet is necessary because he is the means of conveying the religion. The commentary then discusses the Companions (Muhajirun and Ansar) and those who followed them, emphasizing that they adhered to the prophetic indications and held fast to clear texts. The concepts of istishab (presumption of continuity) and istihsan (juristic preference) are mentioned as honors given to the Companions. The passage ends with a discussion on the nature of the subject of usul al-fiqh, which combines rational and transmitted proofs.

Key Terms
مشكاة (mishkah): A niche in a wall where a lamp is placed; used metaphorically here for the Prophet's chest or heart, which holds the light of revelation.
أصول أربعة (usul arba'ah): The four principles of Islamic jurisprudence: Quran, Sunnah, Consensus (Ijma), and Analogy (Qiyas).
استصحاب (istishab): Presumption of continuity; taking something as a companion; here it refers to the Companions' adherence to the Prophet's way.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; deeming something good; here it refers to the honor of being deemed excellent by the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the commentary, what is the order in which the four principles (usul arba'ah) are mentioned?
A) Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas
B) Sunnah, Quran, Ijma, Qiyas
C) Quran, Ijma, Qiyas, Sunnah
D) Ijma, Qiyas, Quran, Sunnah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's usul al-fiqh begins with a clear hierarchy of sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas, as established in the author's preface.
