Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Nature and Importance of Usul al-Fiqh and the Selection of al-Tanqih wa al-Tawdih
Author eulogizes usul al-fiqh and explains his choice of text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the nature of usul al-fiqh as a discipline combining rational and transmitted proofs, and state why the author selected al-Tanqih wa al-Tawdih as his text.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the noblest science because it combines reason and revelation to establish the major premises of legal reasoning.

This passage opens the author's work on usul al-fiqh with a eulogy of the science and a justification for his chosen text. He emphasizes that usul al-fiqh is both rational (ma'qul) and transmitted (manqul), providing the universal premises that transform specific commands into binding rulings. He then praises al-Tanqih and its commentary al-Tawdih as the best works in the field, written by a great imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of praise
Locate where the author directly praises usul al-fiqh. Note the terms 'ajall' (noblest) and 'a'azz' (most precious) used to describe it.
The praise is in the context of the introductory oration.
2
Recognize the two components of usul
Find the phrase 'jami' bayn al-ma'qul wa al-manqul'. This indicates usul al-fiqh covers both rational methods (qiyas, ijma) and transmitted texts (Quran, Sunnah).
This dual nature is a distinctive feature of Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the role of usul in qiyas
The passage explains that usul provides the major premise (kubra) in qiyas, e.g., 'kull ma'mur min al-shari' wajib'. This is the universal rule that allows deriving rulings from specific commands.
Without usul, one cannot move from a text to a general ruling.
4
Note the author's claim of usul's nobility
The author states usul is 'ajall ma yutanasam qubūlahu' (noblest of what is sought) and 'a'azz ma yuttakhadhu malja'an li'l-'uqūl' (most precious refuge for intellects). This underscores its importance.
This sets the stage for why one should study usul.
5
Connect the praise to the specific text chosen
The author then praises 'al-Tanqih ma'a al-Tawdih' as works by an imam who is followed (muqtada bih) and a scholar like a sea (bahr). This explains his choice of these texts for his commentary.
The author values conciseness and depth in usul texts.

ہے لیکن ہو گا عطف القصہ علی القصہ - عطف اللہ علی امجلہ اچھا نہیں ہے کیونكہ ماقبل میں انشار حمد وصلوٰہ ہے جو معنی جملہ انشائیہ ہے جملہ خبریہ ہے عطف خبریہ علی الانث نیہ ہو جائیگا جو ستمن نہیں ہے اس لئے عطف القصیر علی القصہ بنایا جائے ۔ شارح چونکہ یہ کتاب فن اصول فقہ میں تصنیف فرما رہے ہیں تو یہاں سے علت تعیین فن یش کر رہے ہیں فر ماتے ہیں کہ علم الاصول جو کہ جامع بین المعقول و منقول ہے کیونکہ اس فن کے اندر جن امور کے حالات کی بحث کی جاتی ہے بعض از قسم معقولات ہیں جیسے مباحث اجتماع و قیاس اور بعض از ختم منقولات جیسے کتاب دستہ اور اسی طرح دلائل بعض از معقولات میں اور بعض از منقولات النافع في الوصول الى مدارك المحصول یہ علم الاصول کی صفت ثانیہ ہے لفظ مدارك کا معنے مواضع الادراك ہے لیکن مراد اس سے دلائل ہیں جن سے احکام حاصل ہوتے ہیں یعنی علم اصول جو نافع سے فی الوصول الى ادلۃ الاحکام یا مدارك سے مراد قواعد کلیہ ہیں جو اثبات احکام میں كبر کی قیاس بنتے ہیں اور صغری سہلہ الحصول کے ساتھ مل کر اثبات احکام کا ذریعہ بنتے ہیں جیسے یوں کہا جائے کہ الصلوۃ مامورة من الشارع اسكے بعد كبرى آئیگا كل مأمور من الشارع واجب تو یہ کبری اصول فقہ کا مسئلہ ہے اس تک پہنچنے میں علم الاصول نافع ہے اور پھر اس کے ذریعے احکام فقیہ تک وصول ہوگا ۔ اجل ما يتنسو ہم ان کی خبر ہے اور لفظ علم الاصول اس کا اسم ہے اتنم بوئیدن یقال تنسمت روح الحياة بمعنی نیم حیات را یافتم اور یہ فل متعدی ہے اور لفظ قبول اسکا مفعول ہے قبول القبول میں پہلا قبول بمعنی ریح الصبار ہے اور قبول ثانی مصدر ہے معنی مقبولیتہ اور اضافہ مشبہ بہ الی امشبہ ہے یعنی مقبولیہ بمنزلہ ریح الصبار کے ہے کہ دونوں باعث راحت وفرحت ہیں۔ معنی یہ ہوگا کہ علم الاصول ان تمام اشیاء میں سے جن سے احکام اور اثبات احکام پر بار صبا قبولیت کی چلتی تھی اجل اور عظیم تر تھا۔ واعز ما يتخذ لفظ متخذ ماخوذ من الانتخاف ہے جو مستعدی الی المغولین ہوتا ہے اس کا مفعول ستتر ہے جو علم الاصول کی طرف راجع ہو کہ نائب فاعل ہے اور مفعول ثمانی عقول العقول ہے اسمیں عقول اول یعنی ملجاً اور جائے پناہ کے ہے اور عقول ثانی بمعنی قوۃ مدركہ ہے اسلام کی میں لفظ اعلام جمع ہے علم کی جو بمعنی رایہ یعنی جھت ڈا ہے اس فقرے کا معنی یہ ہو گا یعنی وہ اشیاء جن کو حق کے جھنڈے بلند کرنے کے بارے عقلوں کی جائے پناہ بنا یا جاتا تھا ان تمام میں سے علم الاصول اعز اور عزیز ترین تھا ان دو فقروں میں میں علم الاصول کی عظمت بیان کر کے اشارہ کر دیا کہ یہ فن اس لائق تھا کہ اس میں کتار کی جائے تو علت تعیین فن ہوگئی۔ اس کے بعد تنقیح و توضیح کی مدح کر کے علت تعیین متن پیش کر ر ہے یعنی یہ واضح کر رہا ہے کہ میں نے اس متن کو برائے تشریح کیوں متعین کیا تو فرمایا کہ ان کتاب التنفيج مع شرحه تح بع متن ہے تو ضیح کا مصنف رونے پہلے اپنی کتا۔ تنقیح لکھی جو اصول بزدوری کا خلاصہ تھی اور پھر اس تنقیح کی شرح کی جس کا نام توضیح ہے یہ تنقيح مع التوضيح تصنیف تھی للامام امام من یقتدی بہ کو کہا جاتا ہے۔ والبحرین بہت بڑے عالم کو تحر یہ کہتے ہیں کا نہ بحر كل سئکتہ تعرض علیہ علم الهداية علم بفتح اللام بمعنى الرابيه او تحریرہ
And He made the clear path a victorious Sultan, the highway a road's guide, a bringer of good news and a warner. And the linguistic explanation of 'salat' and 'salam' upon the Messenger and the Companions. The meaning of 'karamat al-istishab wa al-istihsan'... Then the author says: 'Ilm al-usul is comprehensive of the rational and transmitted. And it is the most beneficial in reaching the sources of the rulings or the universal rules that serve as major premises in qiyas. And the noblest of what is sought, and the most precious of what is adopted. Then he praises al-Tanqih and its commentary al-Tawdih as the best works, chosen for explanation.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage is the author's introductory eulogy for the science of usul al-fiqh and his justification for selecting the specific text (al-Tanqih with its commentary al-Tawdih). He begins with an Urdu explanation of the Arabic phrases praising the Prophet and the Companions, focusing on the terms 'istishab' and 'istihsan' and their significance. Then he states that usul al-fiqh is a discipline that combines ma'qul (rational matters like qiyas and ijma') and manqul (transmitted matters like the Quran and Sunnah). The author explains that this science provides the major premises (kubra) for legal reasoning, as in the example: 'Prayer is commanded by the Lawgiver; every commanded thing is obligatory; therefore prayer is obligatory.' He then praises usul al-fiqh as the noblest and most precious of all sciences, because it is a refuge for intellects and raises the banners of truth. Finally, he explains his choice of al-Tanqih and al-Tawdih: the author of al-Tanqih first wrote a summary of Usul al-Bazdawi, then commented on it as al-Tawdih, and these works are by an imam who is followed and a scholar like a sea.

Key Terms
علم الأصول ('Ilm al-Usul): The science that deals with the sources of Islamic law and the methods of deriving rulings, combining rational and transmitted proofs.
الاستصحاب (al-Istishab): Presumption of continuity; the principle that a state of being (e.g., permissibility) remains until a change is proven.
الاستحسان (al-Istihsan): Preferring one analogy over a stronger analogy due to a stronger evidence or need.
التنقيح والتوضيح (al-Tanqih wa al-Tawdih): A book (al-Tanqih) and its commentary (al-Tawdih) by Sadr al-Sharia, summarizing Usul al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the role of usul al-fiqh in legal reasoning?
A) It only deals with transmitted texts like Quran and Sunnah.
B) It provides the major premises (kubra) in qiyas, such as 'every commanded thing is obligatory'.
C) It is unnecessary for deriving rulings.
D) It only discusses linguistic principles.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the noblest science because it uniquely combines rational and transmitted proofs to furnish the major premises for legal derivation, and this is why the author chose al-Tanqih wa al-Tawdih as its best exposition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Role of Usul al-Fiqh and Praise of Al-Tanqih
Praise of usul al-fiqh and the books Al-Tanqih and Al-Tawdih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the function of usul al-fiqh in deriving rulings and identify the purpose of the books Al-Tanqih and Al-Tawdih as described in the introduction.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh provides the major premises that connect revealed commands to fiqh rulings.

This passage is the introduction to a classical commentary on Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih. The commentator praises the science of usul al-fiqh and specifically the works Al-Tanqih and Al-Tawdih. We will examine the definition and scope of usul al-fiqh as presented here, and understand why these texts are considered comprehensive and authoritative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter of usul al-fiqh
The passage states that usul al-fiqh deals with both rational matters (ma'qulat) like syllogism and analogy, and transmitted matters (manqulat) like textual evidence. Note how the commentator classifies the proofs.
This classification is typical: usul covers both rational inference and textual sources.
2
Understand the term 'Madarik al-Mahsul'
The commentator glosses 'madarik' as either proofs (adillah) or universal principles (qawa'id kulliyah). Both interpretations are given, showing that usul provides the major premises for deriving rulings.
The phrase 'Al-Nafi' fi al-Wusul ila Madarik al-Mahsul' is the book's title: beneficial for reaching the proofs of rulings.
3
Analyze the example of deriving a ruling
The commentator gives an example: 'Prayer is commanded by the Lawgiver' (minor premise) and 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory' (major premise). The major premise is a principle of usul al-fiqh. This shows how usul principles are applied.
This illustrates the hanafi method: usul provides the kulli (universal) rule, and fiqh applies it to particular cases.
4
Appreciate the praise of Al-Tanqih and Al-Tawdih
The commentator uses poetic metaphors (e.g., 'most magnificent of what is breathed', 'most glorious of what is taken as refuge') to exalt these books. He also lists many other usul works and claims that Al-Tanqih summarizes and surpasses them all.
This rhetorical praise is typical in introductions, establishing the authority of the text being commented upon.

بہت بڑے عالم کو تحر یہ کہتے ہیں کا نہ بحر کل سئکتہ تعرض علیہ علم الهداية علم بفتح اللام بمعنى الرابيه او تحریرہ هم سینی جھنڈا یا پیر یعنی بدایتہ اور رہنمائی کی اسامل العلمیہ الدین یہ میں بمنزلہ رایہ اور فی تھا جیسے یہ اشیاء ہدایتہ سبیل میں مفید ثابت ہوتی ہیں اسی طرح ہدایتہ فی السبائل میں مفید تھا کا فادة الجبل - عالم الدراية عالم بختم العام اس کائنات اور موجودات ماسوی اللہ کو عالم کہا جاتا ہے درایتہ بمعنی اعلم والنہر یعنی علم و سمجھداری کی ایک مستقل عام ہے مدل ميزان المعقول - معقول کی ترازو کو عدل و انصاف سے رکھنے والا - ومنقع تنقیح کے معنی ہیں چھانٹنا اور صاف کرنا یعنی فروع واصول کی تنقیح مقصودہ بات متروک ہو جائے اور ہر اور برگزیدہ امور کے خزانے میں سے یہ ایک نصاب کامل تھی اور تھی پوری کفایت کرنے والی اور ہر مدید و بسیط یعنی طویل و عریفین مسائل اور کتب کی مستصفی یعنی صاف ستھرے امور کے لئے یہ کتاب بھر محیط تھی اور ان تمام امور کا احاطہ کئے ہوئے تھی اور یہ کتاب ایک ایسا کنز اور خزانہ تھا جو اپنے ماسوا تمام وجیز و وسیط یعنی مختصر اور درمیانہ درجے کی کتب سے معنی اور ہے پرواہ کر دینے والی تھی ۔ فيه كفاية اور میزان الاصول یعنی اصول قواعد نمی تر از دو کو سیدها اور درست رکھنے میں یہ کتاب بہت کافی تھی اور ان اصول کی مختلف انسان کو چھانٹ اور مہذب کر کے پیش کرنے میں اس کے اندر پوری کفایتہ موجود تھی ۔
[The text discusses] the matters whose rulings are investigated; some are rational (ma'qulat) like discussions of syllogism and analogy, and some are transmitted (manqulat) like the book of Dastah [؟]. Similarly, proofs are partly rational and partly transmitted. 'Al-Nafi' fi al-Wusul ila Madarik al-Mahsul' is the second attribute of this science of usul. The word 'madarik' means places of perception, but here it refers to proofs from which rulings are derived—i.e., the science of usul is beneficial for reaching the proofs of rulings. Or 'madarik' means universal principles (qawa'id kulliyah) that serve as the major premise in establishing rulings, which together with an easily obtainable minor premise become the means of establishing rulings. For example, one says: 'Prayer is commanded by the Lawgiver'; then the major premise comes: 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory.' This major premise is a issue of usul al-fiqh; the science of usul helps reach it, and through it the jurist arrives at rulings. 'The most magnificent of what is breathed'—this is the predicate, and the term 'ilm al-usul is its subject... [the text continues with poetic praise of usul al-fiqh and the book Al-Tanqih with its commentary Al-Tawdih, listing many book names and describing the book's comprehensiveness and utility].
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a front matter from a commentary on Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih. The commentator begins by explaining the scope of usul al-fiqh: it deals with matters both rational (like syllogism and qiyas) and transmitted (like textual evidence). He then glosses the book's title 'Al-Nafi' fi al-Wusul ila Madarik al-Mahsul', explaining that 'madarik' means proofs or universal principles. He illustrates with an example: the major premise 'Everything commanded by the Lawgiver is obligatory' is a rule of usul al-fiqh. The rest of the passage is an elaborate praise of the science of usul and specifically of the book Al-Tanqih by Sadr al-Shariah and its commentary Al-Tawdih. The commentator uses poetic metaphors (e.g., 'the most magnificent of what is breathed', 'the most glorious of what is taken as refuge for intellects') to exalt the book. He then lists numerous other works (e.g., Al-Mabsut, Al-Kafi, Al-Wiqayah, etc.) and claims that Al-Tanqih summarizes and surpasses them all. This rhetorical style is typical of introductions in the Hanafi tradition, intended to justify the choice of the text and motivate the student. The commentator also explains the meanings of 'tanqih' (sifting, refining) and 'tawdih' (clarification), indicating the book's purpose.

Key Terms
تنقیح (tanqih): Sifting and refining; the name of the matn (Al-Tanqih) by Sadr al-Shariah, a summary of usul al-fiqh.
توضیح (tawdih): Clarification; the name of the commentary (Al-Tawdih) by Sadr al-Shariah on his own Al-Tanqih.
مدارک (madarik): Literally places of perception; here it means proofs (adillah) or universal principles (qawa'id kulliyah) from which rulings are derived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the term 'madarik' refer to in the context of usul al-fiqh?
A) The names of books
B) Proofs or universal principles that help derive rulings
C) The minor premises in syllogisms
D) The act of commanding

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh provides the universal principles (madarik) that serve as major premises in syllogisms to derive fiqh rulings from revealed commands.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Praise of al-Tanqih and Motivation for al-Tawdih
Authorial preface praising base text and motivating commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Sadr al-Shari'ah wrote al-Tawdih despite al-Tanqih's fame, and identify the key attributes of al-Tanqih as described in the introduction.

Core Idea
A great usul text may still need a commentary to reveal its hidden subtleties and unique method.

This passage is the opening of a Hanafi usul commentary. The author praises the base text, al-Tanqih, as comprehensive and famous, yet argues that its depth and novel approach require further explanation. Understanding this motivation helps us appreciate the tradition of scholarly commentary in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base work and its attributes
List the praises given to al-Tanqih: it summarizes expanded works, is sufficient, a complete curriculum, a treasure, and encompasses all issues. Note the four pillars (Book, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas).
These attributes establish the book's authority.
2
Recognize the need for commentary
Despite its fame, the author says al-Tanqih contained hidden subtleties (latif nikat) and a unique methodology (manhaj badi') that needed disclosure. This is the motivation for al-Tawdih.
The commentary is not a correction but an exposition.
3
Trace the author's reasoning
The author uses a rhetorical question: if the base text is so excellent, why write a commentary? His answer: because it had unexplored depths that only a commentator could unlock.
This reflects the classical idea that a text's value is not diminished by needing explanation.
4
Note the autobiographical element
The author mentions finding scholars beyond the Oxus river whose hearts and minds were thirsty for this knowledge, indicating the practical demand for the commentary.
This adds a historical context of knowledge transmission.
5
Summarize the lesson's significance for usul al-fiqh
This introduction teaches that even authoritative texts require careful study and that commentaries serve to reveal deeper layers of meaning. It also shows the interconnectedness of Hanafi scholarship across regions.
As a student of usul, you learn to value both the matn and the sharh.

This book is like a flag and guide in the religious sciences, similar to guidance on the path. 'Alim al-dirayah' means knowledge of the universe and all besides Allah. 'Dirayah' means knowledge and understanding. 'Mizan al-ma'qul' means the scale of reason set with justice. 'Tanqih' means to sift and purify, i.e., one who sifts branches and principles. The author pointed to his two books: one on logic (Mizan) and one on usul (al-Tanqih). All these attributes apply to the book al-Tanqih, which is the subject of al-Tawdih. The book is a summary of every expanded work, sufficient in objectives, a complete curriculum from the treasury of selected matters, encompassing all lengthy and brief issues. It is a treasure surpassing all concise and intermediate works. It suffices in the scale of principles, sifting and refining the various aspects. It is the ultimate in clarifying the branches and their pillars, which are the four pillars: Book, Sunnah, Consensus, and Qiyas. Then he stated his reason for writing: despite its fame, it followed a unique path in revealing the secrets of research, raising the beacon of precision, and contained subtle points never before heard. Thus it achieved widespread fame, more than the sun at noon. And I found, while crossing beyond the river, many scholars whose hearts, livers, and intellects were thirsty for it.
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is the commentator's introduction, praising the base text (al-Tanqih by Sadr al-Shari'ah) and explaining why he wrote the commentary (al-Tawdih). The commentator describes al-Tanqih as a comprehensive work that summarizes all major expanded texts, covering every branch and principle of usul al-fiqh. He lists the four pillars of usul (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas). Despite the book's immense popularity and fame across the Islamic world, the commentator argues that it contained hidden subtleties ('lata'if nikat') and a novel methodology that required elucidation. Therefore, he wrote al-Tawdih to uncover these secrets and make them accessible. The passage also includes a brief autobiographical note about encountering eager scholars during his journey across the Oxus river.

Key Terms
تنقیح (tanqih): To sift and purify; in this context, the title of the base work on usul al-fiqh by Sadr al-Shari'ah.
توضیح (tawdih): Explanation; the title of the commentary on al-Tanqih by the same author.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the main reason Sadr al-Shari'ah wrote al-Tawdih?
A) Because al-Tanqih was incomplete and needed corrections.
B) Because al-Tanqih had hidden subtleties and a unique methodology that required explanation.
C) Because al-Tanqih was too brief and lacked essential details.
D) Because he wanted to criticize al-Tanqih's methodology.

Key Takeaway
Even a famous comprehensive text in usul al-fiqh may require a commentary to uncover its subtle points and unique methodology.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Four Pillars of Islamic Legal Sources (Arkan Arba'a)
Introducing the four foundational sources of Islamic law: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four foundational sources of Islamic law (al-Arkan al-Arba'a) and explain their hierarchical relationship in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas are the four pillars upon which all fiqh rulings are built.

In praising the original book, the commentator highlights that it perfected the four pillars: the Book (Quran), the Sunnah, Ijma (consensus), and Qiyas (analogy). These are the primary sources of Islamic law, recognized across all Sunni schools. For the Hanafi school, Qiyas plays a crucial role in deriving rulings for new cases, but it must be grounded in the primary sources. This lesson introduces each source and its authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sources
From the passage, pick out the four terms that the author calls the pillars (arkan).
These are Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas.
2
Understand the Hanafi hierarchy
Know that in Hanafi usul, the Quran is primary, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas. Qiyas is only used when no explicit text exists.
Other schools may place Qiyas differently.
3
Relate to the book's perfection
The book is praised because it covers all four pillars perfectly, meaning it provides proofs from each source for its rulings.

وهو نهاية مبائن جروع کی تھیں اور اس کے ارکان کی تعدیل میں یہ کتاب نباید اور انتہا کو پہنچی ہوئی تھی میان سے مراد دل اور دلائل ہیں جو فروع پر قائم ہوتی مرادا پر ہیں اور ان اولہ کے ارکان وہی ارکان اربعہ کتاب وسنتہ جہان و قیاس ہیں ۔ نو قد سلک اسے وجہ تصنیف پیش کر رہے ہیں اصل میں سوال یہ ہوتا تھا کہ جب یہ کتاب اتنی اوصاف اور فضائل کے ساتھ متصف تھی تو ہر طالب علم براہ راست اس سے اس سے مستفید ہو سکتا تھا تو پھر آپ کو کسی ضرورت نے تفریح کی تصنیف پر مجبور کیا تو فرمایا هم قد سلک یعنی اسرار تحقیق کو منکشف کرنے میں اس نے منہاج بدیع اور طریق عجیبہ لینی اختیار کیا تھا اور منار تدقیق کو بلند اور مرتفع کرنے میں غایہ فصولی پرستو لی اور غالب ہو ا تھ‎ے اور مع شریف اس کے ساتھ شریف زیادات موجود تھیں جن کو افکار کے ہاتھوں نے چھواتک نہیں تھا ۔ ولطیف نکات اور لطیف نکتے بھی اس کے اندر موجود تھے جن کے ساتھ اولو الابصار نے لوگوں کے آذان کے رتق و بوجہ نہیں توڑے تھے یعنی اولو الابصار ایسے نکتے لوگوں نے پہلے سنے ہوں ایسا نہیں تھا بلکہ مصنف کی ذہنی پیدا وار تھے ولهذا طار * چونکہ یہ فضائل مذکورہ کی جامع تھی اسلئے اسے بڑی مقبولیت اور شہرت حاصل تھی اور طراف و اقطار دنیا میں ایسے اڑ کر پہنچی جیسے امطار اور بارشیں کائنات کے کونے کونے میں پہنچتی ہیں اور امعان وبلاد میں امثال کی طرح یہ کتاب ضرب المشن ہوگئی اور آفاق و اکتشاف میں آنے شہرت کا حصہ وافر حاصل کرلی۔ لا اشتهار الشمر صرف ایسے نہیں جیسے شمس کو نصف بہار میں درجہ شہرت حاصل ہے بلکہ اس سے زیادہ شهرت حاصل تھی ولقد صادفت یہ تفریح کی وجہ تصنیف کا تمر ہے۔ صادفت ای مود دانست ای وجته - تاندی مصدر سیمی ہے بحذف مصاف ظرف ہے ای وجدت وقت اجتيازي بماوراء النهر جار مجرور متعلق ہے اجتاز کیساتھ جو محبت ز کا مفہوم ہے لكثير من فضلاء یہ چار مجرور صادفت کے متعلق ہے افئدة بعنی القلوب مفعول ہے صادفت ا ما دقت کا اور اگلے کے معطوفات اکباد ، عقول و غیره سب مفعول به پلین معطوف علیہ کے ساتھ مل کر تھوى اليه اى تسبيل الله واكباد مع ہے کہد کی بیعنی جگر هائمة عليه نام الرجل امی عطش مائتہ کے معنی ا عطش کے ہونگے لیکن اس کے ضمن میں حریق کا مفہوم نے کہ علیہ کے ساتھ مستعدی کیا گیا معنی ہوگا

تھے
حریمته على كشف الكتاب و عقولا مراد صاحب عقول میں حاشیہ گھٹنے ٹیکنا ینے ایل عقول بین یدیہ یعنی اس کتاب کے سامنے گھٹنے ٹیکے ہوئے میٹھے ورغبات یہ رقب یہ رغب فی شیئی سے ہے یعنی کسی شیئی میں رغبت اور شوق کرنا۔ مستوقفة المطايا لدینہ یعنی رغبات اپنی سواریوں کو اس کتا بے سامنے رو کے ہوئے تھے تاکہ اس کتاب سے فوائد و عطایا حاصل کریں تو رغبات کو تشبیہ دی اصحاب الطایا کے ساتھ اور یہ تشبیہ معظم فی النفس ہے یہ استعارہ بالکنایہ ہے اور قرینہ اس کے لئے لفظ مٹایا ہے جو اصحاب مطلیا کے لئے لازم ہے یہ استعارہ تخیلیہ ہوا اور سمایا یعنی سواریو کو مقصود کے سامنے روکنا یہ ملائمات میں سے ہے یہ استعارہ تر شیمیہ ہوا ۔ جہاں ذکر مشبہ ہو اور مشبه به متروک ہو اور تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہو تو اس کو استعارہ بالکنایہ کہتے ہیں لوازمات مشبہ بہ کو مشبہ کے لئے ثابت کرنا یہ استعارہ تخیلیہ ہوتا ہے جو استعارہ تکیہ قرینہ بنتا ہے اور ملاکات و مناسبات مشبہ بہ کا مشہد کے لئے ثابت کرنا استعارہ شیخیہ ہوتا ہے جیسے مخالب المنیہ نشبت بغلال نفیسہ کو اپنے نفس میں تشبیہ کیا گئی سبیع کے ساتھ نینہ سے مراد تو موت ہے اور با لسبع مضمر فی النفس ہے یہ استعاره بالکنایہ ہے مخالب جو از لوازمات سبع ہے اس کا اثبات للمنة جو کہ مشبہ ہر اور انشاب جو لوازمات میں سے تو نہیں البتہ ملاسمات میں سے ہے اسکا اثبات تر شیمیہ ہے اور جہاں ذر اور ماں ذکر مشبہ بہ ہو اور ارادہ مشبہ کا ہو بالقرمیتہ تو اسکو استعارة مصرصہ اور کہتے ہیں جیسے رایت اسلایر می تو بقر مینہ یہ می اسد سے مراد رجل شجاع ہے۔ یہ ہے استعارہ مصرحہ

لئے
دی
معتصمير
في كشف الاستار بالحواشي
حواشی ہم معنی اطراف کے ہے مراد اس سے ماکتب علی الاطراف و الجوانب یعنی اس کتاب کے مستورہ دقائق کے کشف میں انہوں نے حواشی اور اطراف کو اخذ کر رکھا تھ اور ان حواشی کے ساتھ معتصم یعنی تھامنے اور پکڑنے والے تھے جس سے پورے فوائد اور دقائق منکشف نہیں ہو سکتے تھے اس لئے فرمایا کہ قانيين في جارة اللثالی بالاصداف یعنی اس کتاب کے اسرار جو بمنزلہ بھارتے تھے ان انہیں سے لٹالی یعنی موتیوں کے بجائے اصداف پر قانع تھے یعنی حقیقی فوائد اور جواہر
And it was fully explanatory of the branches, and in the amendment of its pillars, this book reached the peak and limit. By 'main' is meant proofs and evidences that stand upon the branches, and those pillars are the four pillars: the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. He did not follow a path in presenting the reason for composition. Originally the question was: when this book was characterized with such qualities and virtues, every student could benefit directly from it, so what necessity forced you to write a commentary? He said: 'I did follow' meaning that in uncovering the secrets of research, he adopted a novel method and a wonderful way, and in raising the beacon of precision, he strove to the utmost and prevailed. And with the noble additions that the hands of thoughts had not touched. And subtle points and delicate hints were present in it, with which the possessors of insight had not broken the seal of people's ears before; rather, they were the author's own mental productions. Therefore it flew. Because it encompassed these mentioned virtues, it gained great acceptance and fame, and it reached the regions of the world as rains reach every corner of the universe. In cities and countries it became proverbial, and in horizons and discoveries it obtained a full share of fame. Its fame is not like that of the sun in mid-spring, but even greater. And indeed I encountered this commentary's reason for composition. 'Sadaftu' meaning I found. 'Itta ja'zi' is a source with deletion of the genitive, it is an adverb, meaning I found at the time of my crossing beyond the river. The prepositional phrase is related to 'ijtaza' which gives the meaning of love. 'Li kathirin min fudala' is a prepositional phrase related to 'sadaftu'. 'Af'idah' meaning hearts is the object of 'sadaftu'. 'Akbad', 'uqul', and others are all objects connected with the previous. All together 'tawi ilayhi' meaning they yearn. 'Wa akbad' with 'h' meaning livers. 'Ha'imah 'alayhi' like thirst. The meaning of 'atish' but in it is the meaning of burning. Then he said: 'their livers thirsting for it'. Then 'Harimuhu 'ala kashf al-kitab' and 'uqul' meaning the possessors of intellects. In the margin: 'kneeling'. 'Uqul bayna yadayhi' meaning intellects kneeling before this book. 'Raghabat' from 'raghiba fi shay' meaning desire and longing. 'Mustawqifat al-mutaya ladayhi' meaning the she-camels of desires are halted before this book so that benefits and gifts may be obtained. So desires are likened to the owners of mounts, and this is a simile implicit in the mind. This is a metaphor by allusion (isti'ara bilkinayah), and the indicator for it is the word 'mutaya' which is necessary for the owners of mounts. This is an imaginative metaphor (isti'ara takhyiliyyah). 'Samaya' meaning halting the mounts before the desired object is among the suitable things; this is a corroborative metaphor (isti'ara tarshihiyyah). When the object of comparison is mentioned and the subject of comparison is omitted, and the simile is implicit in the mind, it is called metaphor by allusion. Affirming the necessary concomitants of the subject of comparison for the object of comparison is imaginative metaphor, which serves as the indicator for the metaphor. Affirming the compatible and appropriate attributes of the subject of comparison for the object of comparison is corroborative metaphor. For example: 'The claws of death struck such-and-such precious thing.' Death is likened to a beast; 'death' is the object of comparison, and 'beast' is implicit in the mind; this is metaphor by allusion. 'Claws' are among the necessary parts of a beast; affirming them for death (the object of comparison) is imaginative metaphor. And 'striking' is not among the necessary parts but among the suitable things; its affirmation is corroborative. When the subject of comparison is mentioned and the object of comparison is intended by way of primary meaning, it is called explicit metaphor (isti'ara musarrahah). For example: 'I saw a lion writing' where 'lion' means a brave man. This is explicit metaphor. For 'mu'tasim' in 'kashf al-asrar bi al-hawashi' - 'hawashi' is synonymous with 'atraf', meaning what is written on the margins and sides. That is, in uncovering the concealed subtleties of this book, they took to the margins and sides, and they clung to these margins, so that the full benefits and subtleties could not be uncovered. Therefore he said: 'Contenting themselves with shells instead of pearls' - meaning the secrets of this book, which were like pearls, they were content with shells instead of pearls, i.e., they were content with superficial things instead of the real benefits and jewels.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This is a front-matter passage from a commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, probably written by a later Hanafi scholar. The author begins by praising the original book (likely al-Tawdih or al-Talwih) describing it as fully explanatory of fiqh branches and having perfected the four pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. He then addresses a hypothetical question: if the original book was so perfect, why did the commentator need to write his own commentary? The answer is that the original author used a novel and precise method, included subtle points not previously known, and the book gained immense popularity. But despite its fame, the commentator found many scholars who, due to various exigencies, were unable to fully grasp the book's depths—they were content with superficial understanding (like collecting shells instead of pearls). Therefore, the commentator wrote his work to uncover the hidden treasures. The passage then provides a detailed linguistic and rhetorical analysis of certain phrases, explaining various types of metaphors (isti'ara bilkinayah, takhyiliyyah, tarshihiyyah, musarrahah). This serves to justify the need for a commentary that clarifies such subtleties. The discussion is typical of Hanafi usul works that combine fiqh with Arabic rhetoric and logic.

Key Terms
ارکان اربعہ (arkan arba'a): The four foundational sources of Islamic law: the Quran, the Sunnah, Ijma (consensus), and Qiyas (analogy).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the four pillars (arkan) of the book being praised?
A) The Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas
B) The Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Istihsan
C) The Book, Sunnah, Qiyas, and Urf
D) The Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Fatwa

Key Takeaway
The four pillars (arkan arba'a) are the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas, with a strict hierarchy: Quran first, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Rhetorical Analysis in Usul al-Fiqh: Metaphor Types (Isti'ara)
Explaining four types of metaphor used in praising the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between isti'ara bilkinayah, isti'ara takhyiliyyah, isti'ara tarshihiyyah, and isti'ara musarrahah in a legal text.

Core Idea
Understanding metaphor types is crucial for interpreting legal texts, as many Quranic and hadith expressions rely on figurative language.

The passage provides a detailed rhetorical analysis of the phrases describing the book's fame and scholars' engagement with it. The commentator explains four types of metaphor (isti'ara) that appear in the text, showing how literary analysis is integral to usul al-fiqh. This lesson unpacks those metaphor types and their application to legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of the metaphor
The commentator describes scholars' desires as halted mounts (mutaya) and their intellects as kneeling before the book. Recognize that these are metaphors.
The literal meaning is not intended.
2
Distinguish implicit vs explicit metaphor
Identify whether the subject of comparison (e.g., mount owners) is mentioned or only implied. If implied, it's isti'ara bilkinayah.
In bilkinayah, the original subject (musabbah bihi) is omitted.
3
Identify necessary vs suitable attributes
In the metaphor, 'mounts' (mutaya) are necessary for riders; affirming them for desires is isti'ara takhyiliyyah. 'Halting' (samaya) is suitable but not necessary; affirming it is isti'ara tarshihiyyah.
Necessary concomitants (lazim) vs. suitable attributes (mulaim).
4
Recognize explicit metaphor
When the subject of comparison (e.g., 'lion') is used directly for the object (brave man), it's isti'ara musarrahah.
In musarrahah, the word for the subject of comparison is mentioned.

وهو نهاية مبائن جروع کی تھیں اور اس کے ارکان کی تعدیل میں یہ کتاب نباید اور انتہا کو پہنچی ہوئی تھی میان سے مراد دل اور دلائل ہیں جو فروع پر قائم ہوتی مرادا پر ہیں اور ان اولہ کے ارکان وہی ارکان اربعہ کتاب وسنتہ جہان و قیاس ہیں ۔ نو قد سلک اسے وجہ تصنیف پیش کر رہے ہیں اصل میں سوال یہ ہوتا تھا کہ جب یہ کتاب اتنی اوصاف اور فضائل کے ساتھ متصف تھی تو ہر طالب علم براہ راست اس سے اس سے مستفید ہو سکتا تھا تو پھر آپ کو کسی ضرورت نے تفریح کی تصنیف پر مجبور کیا تو فرمایا هم قد سلک یعنی اسرار تحقیق کو منکشف کرنے میں اس نے منہاج بدیع اور طریق عجیبہ لینی اختیار کیا تھا اور منار تدقیق کو بلند اور مرتفع کرنے میں غایہ فصولی پرستو لی اور غالب ہو ا تھ‎ے اور مع شریف اس کے ساتھ شریف زیادات موجود تھیں جن کو افکار کے ہاتھوں نے چھواتک نہیں تھا ۔ ولطیف نکات اور لطیف نکتے بھی اس کے اندر موجود تھے جن کے ساتھ اولو الابصار نے لوگوں کے آذان کے رتق و بوجہ نہیں توڑے تھے یعنی اولو الابصار ایسے نکتے لوگوں نے پہلے سنے ہوں ایسا نہیں تھا بلکہ مصنف کی ذہنی پیدا وار تھے ولهذا طار * چونکہ یہ فضائل مذکورہ کی جامع تھی اسلئے اسے بڑی مقبولیت اور شہرت حاصل تھی اور طراف و اقطار دنیا میں ایسے اڑ کر پہنچی جیسے امطار اور بارشیں کائنات کے کونے کونے میں پہنچتی ہیں اور امعان وبلاد میں امثال کی طرح یہ کتاب ضرب المشن ہوگئی اور آفاق و اکتشاف میں آنے شہرت کا حصہ وافر حاصل کرلی۔ لا اشتهار الشمر صرف ایسے نہیں جیسے شمس کو نصف بہار میں درجہ شہرت حاصل ہے بلکہ اس سے زیادہ شهرت حاصل تھی ولقد صادفت یہ تفریح کی وجہ تصنیف کا تمر ہے۔ صادفت ای مود دانست ای وجته - تاندی مصدر سیمی ہے بحذف مصاف ظرف ہے ای وجدت وقت اجتيازي بماوراء النهر جار مجرور متعلق ہے اجتاز کیساتھ جو محبت ز کا مفہوم ہے لكثير من فضلاء یہ چار مجرور صادفت کے متعلق ہے افئدة بعنی القلوب مفعول ہے صادفت ا ما دقت کا اور اگلے کے معطوفات اکباد ، عقول و غیره سب مفعول به پلین معطوف علیہ کے ساتھ مل کر تھوى اليه اى تسبيل الله واكباد مع ہے کہد کی بیعنی جگر هائمة عليه نام الرجل امی عطش مائتہ کے معنی ا عطش کے ہونگے لیکن اس کے ضمن میں حریق کا مفہوم نے کہ علیہ کے ساتھ مستعدی کیا گیا معنی ہوگا

تھے
حریمته على كشف الكتاب و عقولا مراد صاحب عقول میں حاشیہ گھٹنے ٹیکنا ینے ایل عقول بین یدیہ یعنی اس کتاب کے سامنے گھٹنے ٹیکے ہوئے میٹھے ورغبات یہ رقب یہ رغب فی شیئی سے ہے یعنی کسی شیئی میں رغبت اور شوق کرنا۔ مستوقفة المطايا لدینہ یعنی رغبات اپنی سواریوں کو اس کتا بے سامنے رو کے ہوئے تھے تاکہ اس کتاب سے فوائد و عطایا حاصل کریں تو رغبات کو تشبیہ دی اصحاب الطایا کے ساتھ اور یہ تشبیہ معظم فی النفس ہے یہ استعارہ بالکنایہ ہے اور قرینہ اس کے لئے لفظ مٹایا ہے جو اصحاب مطلیا کے لئے لازم ہے یہ استعارہ تخیلیہ ہوا اور سمایا یعنی سواریو کو مقصود کے سامنے روکنا یہ ملائمات میں سے ہے یہ استعارہ تر شیمیہ ہوا ۔ جہاں ذکر مشبہ ہو اور مشبه به متروک ہو اور تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہو تو اس کو استعارہ بالکنایہ کہتے ہیں لوازمات مشبہ بہ کو مشبہ کے لئے ثابت کرنا یہ استعارہ تخیلیہ ہوتا ہے جو استعارہ تکیہ قرینہ بنتا ہے اور ملاکات و مناسبات مشبہ بہ کا مشہد کے لئے ثابت کرنا استعارہ شیخیہ ہوتا ہے جیسے مخالب المنیہ نشبت بغلال نفیسہ کو اپنے نفس میں تشبیہ کیا گئی سبیع کے ساتھ نینہ سے مراد تو موت ہے اور با لسبع مضمر فی النفس ہے یہ استعاره بالکنایہ ہے مخالب جو از لوازمات سبع ہے اس کا اثبات للمنة جو کہ مشبہ ہر اور انشاب جو لوازمات میں سے تو نہیں البتہ ملاسمات میں سے ہے اسکا اثبات تر شیمیہ ہے اور جہاں ذر اور ماں ذکر مشبہ بہ ہو اور ارادہ مشبہ کا ہو بالقرمیتہ تو اسکو استعارة مصرصہ اور کہتے ہیں جیسے رایت اسلایر می تو بقر مینہ یہ می اسد سے مراد رجل شجاع ہے۔ یہ ہے استعارہ مصرحہ

لئے
دی
معتصمير
في كشف الاستار بالحواشي
حواشی ہم معنی اطراف کے ہے مراد اس سے ماکتب علی الاطراف و الجوانب یعنی اس کتاب کے مستورہ دقائق کے کشف میں انہوں نے حواشی اور اطراف کو اخذ کر رکھا تھ اور ان حواشی کے ساتھ معتصم یعنی تھامنے اور پکڑنے والے تھے جس سے پورے فوائد اور دقائق منکشف نہیں ہو سکتے تھے اس لئے فرمایا کہ قانيين في جارة اللثالی بالاصداف یعنی اس کتاب کے اسرار جو بمنزلہ بھارتے تھے ان انہیں سے لٹالی یعنی موتیوں کے بجائے اصداف پر قانع تھے یعنی حقیقی فوائد اور جواہر
And it was fully explanatory of the branches, and in the amendment of its pillars, this book reached the peak and limit. By 'main' is meant proofs and evidences that stand upon the branches, and those pillars are the four pillars: the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. He did not follow a path in presenting the reason for composition. Originally the question was: when this book was characterized with such qualities and virtues, every student could benefit directly from it, so what necessity forced you to write a commentary? He said: 'I did follow' meaning that in uncovering the secrets of research, he adopted a novel method and a wonderful way, and in raising the beacon of precision, he strove to the utmost and prevailed. And with the noble additions that the hands of thoughts had not touched. And subtle points and delicate hints were present in it, with which the possessors of insight had not broken the seal of people's ears before; rather, they were the author's own mental productions. Therefore it flew. Because it encompassed these mentioned virtues, it gained great acceptance and fame, and it reached the regions of the world as rains reach every corner of the universe. In cities and countries it became proverbial, and in horizons and discoveries it obtained a full share of fame. Its fame is not like that of the sun in mid-spring, but even greater. And indeed I encountered this commentary's reason for composition. 'Sadaftu' meaning I found. 'Itta ja'zi' is a source with deletion of the genitive, it is an adverb, meaning I found at the time of my crossing beyond the river. The prepositional phrase is related to 'ijtaza' which gives the meaning of love. 'Li kathirin min fudala' is a prepositional phrase related to 'sadaftu'. 'Af'idah' meaning hearts is the object of 'sadaftu'. 'Akbad', 'uqul', and others are all objects connected with the previous. All together 'tawi ilayhi' meaning they yearn. 'Wa akbad' with 'h' meaning livers. 'Ha'imah 'alayhi' like thirst. The meaning of 'atish' but in it is the meaning of burning. Then he said: 'their livers thirsting for it'. Then 'Harimuhu 'ala kashf al-kitab' and 'uqul' meaning the possessors of intellects. In the margin: 'kneeling'. 'Uqul bayna yadayhi' meaning intellects kneeling before this book. 'Raghabat' from 'raghiba fi shay' meaning desire and longing. 'Mustawqifat al-mutaya ladayhi' meaning the she-camels of desires are halted before this book so that benefits and gifts may be obtained. So desires are likened to the owners of mounts, and this is a simile implicit in the mind. This is a metaphor by allusion (isti'ara bilkinayah), and the indicator for it is the word 'mutaya' which is necessary for the owners of mounts. This is an imaginative metaphor (isti'ara takhyiliyyah). 'Samaya' meaning halting the mounts before the desired object is among the suitable things; this is a corroborative metaphor (isti'ara tarshihiyyah). When the object of comparison is mentioned and the subject of comparison is omitted, and the simile is implicit in the mind, it is called metaphor by allusion. Affirming the necessary concomitants of the subject of comparison for the object of comparison is imaginative metaphor, which serves as the indicator for the metaphor. Affirming the compatible and appropriate attributes of the subject of comparison for the object of comparison is corroborative metaphor. For example: 'The claws of death struck such-and-such precious thing.' Death is likened to a beast; 'death' is the object of comparison, and 'beast' is implicit in the mind; this is metaphor by allusion. 'Claws' are among the necessary parts of a beast; affirming them for death (the object of comparison) is imaginative metaphor. And 'striking' is not among the necessary parts but among the suitable things; its affirmation is corroborative. When the subject of comparison is mentioned and the object of comparison is intended by way of primary meaning, it is called explicit metaphor (isti'ara musarrahah). For example: 'I saw a lion writing' where 'lion' means a brave man. This is explicit metaphor. For 'mu'tasim' in 'kashf al-asrar bi al-hawashi' - 'hawashi' is synonymous with 'atraf', meaning what is written on the margins and sides. That is, in uncovering the concealed subtleties of this book, they took to the margins and sides, and they clung to these margins, so that the full benefits and subtleties could not be uncovered. Therefore he said: 'Contenting themselves with shells instead of pearls' - meaning the secrets of this book, which were like pearls, they were content with shells instead of pearls, i.e., they were content with superficial things instead of the real benefits and jewels.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This is a front-matter passage from a commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih, probably written by a later Hanafi scholar. The author begins by praising the original book (likely al-Tawdih or al-Talwih) describing it as fully explanatory of fiqh branches and having perfected the four pillars: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. He then addresses a hypothetical question: if the original book was so perfect, why did the commentator need to write his own commentary? The answer is that the original author used a novel and precise method, included subtle points not previously known, and the book gained immense popularity. But despite its fame, the commentator found many scholars who, due to various exigencies, were unable to fully grasp the book's depths—they were content with superficial understanding (like collecting shells instead of pearls). Therefore, the commentator wrote his work to uncover the hidden treasures. The passage then provides a detailed linguistic and rhetorical analysis of certain phrases, explaining various types of metaphors (isti'ara bilkinayah, takhyiliyyah, tarshihiyyah, musarrahah). This serves to justify the need for a commentary that clarifies such subtleties. The discussion is typical of Hanafi usul works that combine fiqh with Arabic rhetoric and logic.

Key Terms
استعارہ بالکنایہ (isti'ara bilkinayah): A metaphor where the subject of comparison is omitted and only alluded to by affirming its necessary attributes to the object of comparison.
استعارہ تخیلیہ (isti'ara takhyiliyyah): An imaginative metaphor that affirms a necessary concomitant of the omitted subject of comparison to the object of comparison.
استعارہ ترشیحیہ (isti'ara tarshihiyyah): A corroborative metaphor that affirms something suitable (mulaim) – not a necessary concomitant – of the omitted subject of comparison to the object of comparison.
استعارہ مصرحہ (isti'ara musarrahah): An explicit metaphor where the subject of comparison is mentioned but is used to refer to the object of comparison by way of primary meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the metaphor 'the claws of death', 'claws' is an example of which type of metaphor?
A) Isti'ara musarrahah
B) Isti'ara takhyiliyyah
C) Isti'ara tarshihiyyah
D) Isti'ara bilkinayah

Key Takeaway
Rhetorical analysis distinguishes between necessary and suitable attributes in metaphors, which is essential for accurately interpreting legal texts.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Rhetorical Analysis of the Commentator's Preface: Types of Isti'ara
Explaining the rhetorical devices used in the author's preface to his commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify three types of isti'ara (bil-kinaya, takhyiliyya, tarshimiyya) used in a scholarly preface and explain how each contributes to the overall meaning.

Core Idea
In scholarly prefaces, metaphors reveal the author's view of his work's depth and the reader's effort.

This lesson dissects the opening lines of a commentary on al-Tanqih wa al-Tawdih, where the commentator uses elaborate metaphors to describe the difficulty of uncovering the text's hidden gems. Understanding these rhetorical devices is essential for usul students because interpreting authoritative texts often requires distinguishing literal from metaphorical language. By studying the commentator's choices, you will sharpen your ability to spot rhetorical strategies in classical usul works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first metaphor—the kneeling desires
In the first sentence, the author says desires (raghbat) knelt before the book. This is a metaphor. Note that the mushabbah (desires) is mentioned, the mushabbah bihi (people of mounts) is omitted. This signals isti'ara bil-kinaya. Look for the qarina (matāyā) that suggests the omitted.
The qarina is the word 'matāyā' (mounts), which is a necessary property of the omitted people of mounts.
2
Classify the subtypes—takhyiliyya and tarshimiyya
Within bil-kinaya, the author distinguishes two subtypes: takhyiliyya attributes a necessary property (lāzim) of the likened-to object (e.g., mounts) to the subject (desires), and tarshimiyya attributes a harmonious characteristic (mulā'im). In the example, 'mustawqifatu al-matāyā' is tarshimiyya because stopping mounts is harmonious, not necessary.
3
Apply the same analysis to the next metaphor—death as a beast
The author gives another example: 'makhālibu al-maniyyati nashabat'. Here, death is compared to a beast, with 'makhālib' (claws) as a necessary property (takhyiliyya) and 'inshāb' (grasping) as harmonious (tarshimiyya). This reinforces the classification.
4
Distinguish isti'ara musarraha
Later, the author uses explicit comparison by naming the mushabbah bihi (e.g., 'jarā'id' meaning beautiful women) intending the mushabbah (subtleties). This is musarraha, where both sides are mentioned, but the intention is the mushabbah.
Example: 'wa jarā'iduhu' where the subtleties are likened to beautiful women.
5
Connect rhetorical analysis to usul al-fiqh
Identifying whether a statement is literal or metaphorical is crucial for deriving rulings. For instance, a command like 'wa aqimu al-salah' is generally taken as haqiqah by Hanafis, but if a metaphorical context is identified, the ruling might change. The skill of recognizing isti'ara trains you to question the apparent meaning.

في كشف الاستار بالحواشي
حواشی ہم معنی اطراف کے ہے مراد اس سے ماکتب علی الاطراف و الجوانب یعنی اس کتاب کے مستورہ دقائق کے کشف میں انہوں نے حواشی اور اطراف کو اخذ کر رکھا تھ اور ان حواشی کے ساتھ معتصم یعنی تھامنے اور پکڑنے والے تھے جس سے پورے فوائد اور دقائق منکشف نہیں ہو سکتے تھے اس لئے فرمایا کہ قانيين في جارة اللثالی بالاصداف یعنی اس کتاب کے اسرار جو بمنزلہ بھارتے تھے ان انہیں سے لٹالی یعنی موتیوں کے بجائے اصداف پر قانع تھے یعنی حقیقی فوائد اور جواہر

تو ان حواشی سے منکشف نہیں ہوتے تھے البت غیر مستند به امور جو بمنزلہ اصراف کے غیر مقصود تھے جو ان حواشی سے حاصل ہو رہے تھے ان پر انہوں نے قناعت کر رکھی تھی ۔ لا تحل انامل الانظار عقد معضلات، انامل اللہ کی جمع معنی راس الا صبح یعنی پور سے عقد جمع ہے عقدہ کی بمعنی گره معضلات ممعنی مشکلات یعنی اس کے مشکلات میں جو گر ہیں لگی ہوئی تھیں انظار کے پورے انہیں حل نہیں کر سکتے تھے حل بمعنی کھولنا تو یہاں انتظار کو تشبیہ دی صاحب الانامل کے ساتھ یہ استعارہ بالکنایہ ہوا اور اشت انامل تیلیہ اور حل عقد تر شیعیہ ہوا ۔ ولا يفتح بنات الاروس الاصابع یعنی بیان کے پورے اس کے میلا دروازوں کو نہیں کھول سکتے تھے یہاں بھی بطور استعارہ بالکنایہ کے بیان کو ڈمی بنان کے تشبیہ دی جو مضمر فی النفس ہے بنان ذی بنان کے لئے لازم ہے اسکا اثبات ہے اور فتح تر مشکلات کتاب کو بطور استعارة بالکتا یہ کے تشبیہ دی ان خرام کیا تھے جنیر ابواب مغلقہ ہیں اور ابواب مغلقہ کا اثبات تخلیلیہ مغلقہ کا اثبات تخلیلیہ ہے اور فتح تر جیسے پہلے استفادہ کے لئے ترشیمیہ تھا۔ فلطائفه بعد یعنی ان حواشی و انظار اور بیان کے باوجود اس كتاب التنقيح مع التوضیح کے لطائف ابھی تک عجب الفاظ یعنی لفظوں کے پردوں میں مستور اور پوشیدہ پڑے تھے ۔ وجرائدة جمع فریدہ وہی الحبيبة من النساء معافی لطیفہ کو با گراند دی ذکر مشبہ بہ اور ارادہ مشیر استفادة مصرحه ہوا اور خیام تر شیخ مجاز ہے یعنی یہ خواہک جو بمنزلہ فوائد کے تھے وہ اب تک مقصود نے انجام تھے عشاق حضرات انکے دیدار کے خونمند تھے لیکن چونکہ فرائد اب تک مستور تھیں لئے کہا کہ : تری حوالیها همما یعنی ان خیام فرائد کے گرد تم دیکھتے ہم کو جنہوں ا مالینی
اور
نے اپنی گردنیں اونچی کر رکھی تھیں دون الوصول الیا کہ وہاں تک پہنچ نہیں سکتی واعينا ساهرة اور آنکھیں جن کی پتلیاں ان کے دیکھنے کے لئے لئے ہر وقت بیدار تھیں لیکن دیکھنا یکھنا نصیب نہیں ہو رہا تھا دون الوصول بطور حال کے اعینا کیساتھ مرتبط ہے یعنی تری احیتا سا ہرة الاحداق حال كونها متجاوزة عن الوصول اليها اى الى نا اللطائف التی ہی بمنزلہ افخر انتہ۔ اس فقرہ میں بھی ہم کو بطور استعارة بالکتایہ کے تشبیری
زی اعناق کے ساتھ اعناق جو کہ لازم شبہ یہ ہے اس کا اثبات تخییلیہ ہے اور اسے للمقاصد تر شیمیہ ہے ۔ امرت بلسان الالهام - الهام القار الخیر
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.
They were kneeling before the book; 'uqūl means the people of intellects; in the commentary, they knelt on knees before this book. 'Raghbat' comes from 'raghiba fi shay' meaning desire and longing for something. 'Mustawqifatu al-matāyā ladaynah' means that the desires had stopped their mounts before this book to obtain benefits and gifts from it. So desires were likened to people of mounts; this likeness is magnified in the mind. This is isti'āra bil-kināya, and the qarīna for it is the word 'matāyā', which is necessary for the people of mounts; this is takhyīliyya isti'āra. 'Samayā' meaning stopping the mounts before the desired object; this is from the harmony (mulā'imāt); this is tarshīmiyya isti'āra. Where the mushabbah is mentioned and the mushabbah bihi is omitted and the likeness is implied in the mind, this is called isti'āra bil-kināya. Establishing the necessary properties (lawāzim) of the mushabbah bihi for the mushabbah is takhyīliyya isti'āra, and that isti'āra serves as a preparatory qarīna. Establishing the correspondences and affinities (mulākāt wa munāsabāt) of the mushabbah bihi for the mushabbah is tarshīmiyya isti'āra. For example, 'makhālibu al-maniyyati nashabat': death was likened to a beast of prey in the mind; al-maniyya means death, and the beast is implied in the mind; this is isti'āra bil-kināya. 'Makhālub' which is a necessary property of the beast is established for death, which is the mushabbah, and 'inshāb' which is not from the necessary properties but from the affinities, its establishment is tarshīmiyya. And where both the mushabbah and mushabbah bihi are mentioned with the intention of the mushabbah, this is called isti'āra musarraha, like 'ra'aytu asadan' meaning I saw a brave man. This is isti'āra musarraha.

He took refuge in uncovering the hidden meanings by the commentaries; ḥawāshī is synonymous with aṭrāf; what is meant is what is written on the margins and sides. That is, in uncovering the concealed subtleties of this book, they had adopted the commentary and sides, and with those commentaries they were clinging and grasping, such that the complete benefits and subtleties could not be uncovered. Therefore, he said: 'qāni'īn fī jirārati al-lu'lu' bi al-aṣdāf': meaning the secrets of this book, which were like pearls, they were content with the shells (aṣdāf) instead of pearls; that is, the real benefits and jewels were not uncovered from those commentaries. Rather, non-substantive matters, which were like shells and not intended, what was being obtained from those commentaries, they were satisfied with them.

'Lā taḥillu anāmilu al-anẓār 'uqda mu'ḍilāt': 'anāmil' is plural of 'anmula' meaning fingertip; 'uqda' is plural of 'uqda' meaning knot; 'mu'ḍilāt' meaning difficulties. That is, the knots of difficulties that were in it, the fingertips of eyesights could not solve them. 'Ḥall' means opening; here, 'anẓār' (gazes) are likened to possessors of fingertips; this is isti'āra bil-kināya, and 'anāmil' is takhyīliyya, and 'ḥall al-'uqad' is tarshīmiyya.

'Wa lā yaftaḥu banātu al-urūs al-aṣābi'': meaning the fingertips of statements could not open the closed doors of it. Here also, by way of isti'āra bil-kināya, statement is likened to fingers, which is implied in the mind; 'banān' is a necessary property for fingers; its establishment is takhyīliyya, and 'fatḥ' (opening) of the book's difficulties is tarshīmiyya, as before for benefit.

'Fa-laṭā'ifuhu ba'd': meaning despite those commentaries, eyesights, and statements, the subtleties of this book 'al-Tanqīḥ maʻa al-Tawḍīḥ' were still veiled in the curtains of words, concealed and hidden. 'Wa jarā'iduhu' plural of 'jarīda', which is the beloved of women. Here, the subtle benefits (laṭā'if) are likened to beautiful women; mention of the mushabbah bihi and intention of the mushabbah, so it is isti'āra muṣarraḥa, and 'khayām' is a metaphorical plural; that is, these tents which were like benefits, they were not yet attained. The lovers were desirous of seeing them, but because the benefits were still veiled, he said: 'tarā ḥawālīhā himaman': meaning around these tents of benefits, you see aspirations, whose necks they had raised, without reaching them; and eyes that were awake and sleepless for seeing them, but seeing was not possible, 'dūna al-wuṣūl' is a state related to 'a'yunā', meaning you see around it sleepless eyes, being unable to reach them, i.e. to the subtleties which are like pearls. In this sentence too, by way of isti'āra bil-kināya, a likeness is made; 'a'nāq' is a necessary property for the likened; its establishment is takhyīliyya, and 'sal' (going) for the aims is tarshīmiyya. 'Amartu bi-lisāni al-ilhām - ilhām al-qār al-khayr'
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his commentary on al-Tanqīḥ maʻa al-Tawḍīḥ, focusing on rhetorical analysis (isti'āra). The author explains various types of metaphor used by the original author to describe the difficulty and depth of the text. He categorizes isti'āra into bil-kināya (implied metaphor) and muṣarraḥa (explicit metaphor), further breaking down takhyīliyya and tarshīmiyya subtypes. The purpose is to show how the commentator's work aims to uncover hidden meanings, but earlier commentators barely scratched the surface, content with shells instead of pearls. The language is highly ornate, typical of scholarly introductions in the Islamic tradition. For Hanafi usul students, understanding such introductions is crucial for grasping the author's methodology and the weight of his commentary.

Key Terms
استعارہ بالکنایہ (isti'āra bil-kināya): Metaphor where the mushabbah is mentioned and mushabbah bihi is omitted, with a qarīna indicating the comparison.
استعارہ مصرحہ (isti'āra muṣarraḥa): Metaphor where both mushabbah and mushabbah bihi are mentioned, but the mushabbah bihi is intended for the mushabbah.
استعارہ تخیلیہ (isti'āra takhyīliyya): A type of metaphor where a necessary property of the mushabbah bihi is attributed to the mushabbah.
استعارہ ترشیمیہ (isti'āra tarshīmiyya): A type of metaphor where an appropriate characteristic (mulā'im) of the mushabbah bihi is attributed to the mushabbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the author's classification of isti'āra, what is the key difference between isti'āra takhyīliyya and isti'āra tarshīmiyya?
A) One is explicit, the other is implicit.
B) One uses necessary properties (lawāzim), the other uses appropriate harmonies (mulā'imāt).
C) One is used in the Quran, the other in Hadith.
D) One requires a qarīna, the other does not.

Key Takeaway
The commentator’s metaphorical language in the preface is a deliberate rhetorical strategy to convey the difficulty and depth of the text; understanding these metaphors is essential for interpreting the author's methodological stance.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Author's Preface: Inspired Commentary on Al-Tawdih
Author's poetic introduction explaining inspiration for commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's claim of divine inspiration and explain how it functions as a rhetorical device in establishing his authority for the commentary.

Core Idea
The author claims divine inspiration to write this commentary, establishing his work as a compelled duty, not personal ambition.

This preface reveals the author's spiritual motivation. He uses elaborate metaphors to describe the text's hidden depths and his mission to unlock them. Understanding this helps appreciate the seriousness of scholarly commentary in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's complaint about previous glosses
The author says earlier glosses failed to disclose the true meanings and settled for non-authoritative matters. Recognize the starting point for his own work.
This sets up the need for a new commentary.
2
Analyze the metaphors for the text's difficulty
He uses 'fingertips of reflections cannot untie knots' and 'fingers of keys cannot open doors'. Understand what these represent: the limits of ordinary intellectual effort and expression.
These are metaphors for the depth and complexity of the text.
3
Understand the claim of divine inspiration
He says 'I was commanded by the tongue of inspiration'. Note that in Hanafi usul, inspiration is not a source of law; here it is a rhetorical device to authorize his work.
It emphasizes the seriousness of his task.
4
List the tasks he was commanded to perform
He must plunge into the sea of benefits, dive for pearls, unfold secrets, reveal treasures, make paths easy, and subdue rebellious elements.
Each task corresponds to a scholarly activity: extracting rulings, clarifying ambiguities, etc.
5
State the purpose of the commentary
The ultimate goal is to make the text of Al-Tanqih praiseworthy and its commentary Al-Tawdih clearer.

تو ان حواشی سے منکشف نہیں ہوتے تھے البتہ غیر مستند به امور جو بمنزلہ اصراف کے غیر مقصود تھے جو ان حواشی سے حاصل ہو رہے تھے ان پر انہوں نے قناعت کر رکھی تھی ۔ لا تحل انامل الانظار عقد معضلات، انامل اللہ کی جمع معنی راس الا صبح یعنی پور سے عقد جمع ہے عقدہ کی بمعنی گره معضلات ممعنی مشکلات یعنی اس کے مشکلات میں جو گر ہیں لگی ہوئی تھیں انظار کے پورے انہیں حل نہیں کر سکتے تھے حل بمعنی کھولنا تو یہاں انتظار کو تشبیہ دی صاحب الانامل کے ساتھ یہ استعارہ بالکنایہ ہوا اور اشت انامل تیلیہ اور حل عقد تر شیعیہ ہوا ۔ ولا يفتح بنات الاروس الاصابع یعنی بیان کے پورے اس کے میلا دروازوں کو نہیں کھول سکتے تھے یہاں بھی بطور استعارہ بالکنایہ کے بیان کو ڈمی بنان کے تشبیہ دی جو مضمر فی النفس ہے بنان ذی بنان کے لئے لازم ہے اسکا اثبات ہے اور فتح تر مشکلات کتاب کو بطور استعارة بالکتا یہ کے تشبیہ دی ان خرام کیا تھے جنیر ابواب مغلقہ ہیں اور ابواب مغلقہ کا اثبات تخلیلیہ مغلقہ کا اثبات تخلیلیہ ہے اور فتح تر جیسے پہلے استفادہ کے لئے ترشیمیہ تھا۔ فلطائفه بعد یعنی ان حواشی و انظار اور بیان کے باوجود اس كتاب التنقيح مع التوضیح کے لطائف ابھی تک عجب الفاظ یعنی لفظوں کے پردوں میں مستور اور پوشیدہ پڑے تھے ۔ وجرائدة جمع فریدہ وہی الحبيبة من النساء معافی لطیفہ کو با گراند دی ذکر مشبہ بہ اور ارادہ مشیر استفادة مصرحه ہوا اور خیام تر شیخ مجاز ہے یعنی یہ خواہک جو بمنزلہ فوائد کے تھے وہ اب تک مقصود نے انجام تھے عشاق حضرات انکے دیدار کے خونمند تھے لیکن چونکہ فرائد اب تک مستور تھیں لئے کہا کہ : تری حوالیها همما یعنی ان خیام فرائد کے گرد تم دیکھتے ہم کو جنہوں ا مالینی اور نے اپنی گردنیں اونچی کر رکھی تھیں دون الوصول الیا کہ وہاں تک پہنچ نہیں سکتی واعينا ساهرة اور آنکھیں جن کی پتلیاں ان کے دیکھنے کے لئے لئے ہر وقت بیدار تھیں لیکن دیکھنا یکھنا نصیب نہیں ہو رہا تھا دون الوصول بطور حال کے اعینا کیساتھ مرتبط ہے یعنی تری احیتا سا ہرة الاحداق حال كونها متجاوزة عن الوصول اليها اى الى نا اللطائف التی ہی بمنزلہ افخر انتہ۔ اس فقرہ میں بھی ہم کو بطور استعارة بالکتایہ کے تشبیری زی اعناق کے ساتھ اعناق جو کہ لازم شبہ یہ ہے اس کا اثبات تخییلیہ ہے اور اسے للمقاصد تر شیمیہ ہے ۔ امرت بلسان الالهام - الهام القار الخیر نے قلب الغیر کے معنی میں ہے اور یہاں الہام کو تشبیہ دی رجل متکلم بالخیر کے ساتھ یہ استعارة بالکنایہ ہوا اثبات کسان جو متکلم کے لئے لازم ہے اس کا اثبات تحلیلیہ ہے یعنی مجھے لسان الہام کے ساتھ امر ہوا یہ حقیقتا الہام تھا وہم من الاوہام نہیں تھا کس شی کا امر ہوا اس کو بیان کیا ان اخوض الفرض الدخول في الماء في لجج فوائده بج جمع ہے لجہ کی جو معظم مار کے معنی میں ہے ۔ واغوص الدخول تحت الماء یعنی خوطہ لگانا علی غیر فرائد مندر جمع ہے غرة کی معنی اکرم شیئی واولہ و منہ غرة قومه اى سيدهم وغرة الشهر ا وله فرائد جمع ہے فریدہ کی بمعنی اکبر الدرر وفرائد الدرر کبار ہا کا نہا لا نظير لها فانها ندید ووحيدة نے جنسها او لکونی منفردة نے صدقہا ۔ والنشر مطويات رموز ؟ نشہ کے معنی کھولنا اور پھیلانا مطوبات تطویہ سے ماخوذ ہے تصویہ اشرب کپڑے کو لپیٹنا اور تہہ کر نا رموز رمز کی جمع ہے بمعنی اشارات - واظهر مخفيات كنونه کنوز جمع ہے ہ کی بمعنی اخزائن - واسهل مسالك شعابہ مالک جمع ہے مسلک کی اور شوب جمع ہے شعب کی بنے طریق نے ایمیل وا ذلل شوارد صحابہ اذلل بمعنی استخر یعنی مطیع اور تابعدار کرنا شوار و جمع ہے شاردہ بمعنی نافرة صعاب جمع ہے سب بمعنی سرکش و تند خو ان فقروں کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مجھے لسان الہام کے ساتھ حکم ہوا کہ سی کتاب کے فوائد کا جو منظم ماں ہے اس کے اندر داخل ہو جاوں اور اس کے اندر فوائد و لطائف کے جو کیتا موتی اور جواہر پڑے ہیں غوطہ لگا کر انہیں نکالوں اور ظاہر کر دوں اور اسکی تہہ میں جو رموز و اشارات لیٹے پڑے ہیں ان کو پھپ لاؤں اور اس کے پوشیدہ خزائن کون؟ کروں اور اس کے مشکل ترین راستوں کو سہل و نزم کر دوں اور اس کے اندر جو فوائد منتزلر وحشی جانوروں کے نفور اور صحار ہیں جو کسی۔ سے شکار نہیں ہو سکتے انکو مسخرا در مذلل کردوں ۔ بحيث يصير مجیت یصیر المان - یعنی بایں طور کہ میری اس جدو جہد سے متن تنقیح مشروع ہو جائے اور اسکی شرح توضیح زیادہ واضح ہو جائے۔ طفق بهعنی شرع و جل والا تمام الدخول في امر بشلف وشقة اسے موارد جمع ہے مور د کی بمعنی مقام ورود اور گھاٹ کو بھی کہتے ہیں لوگ اور جانور پانی کی خاطر وارد ہوتے ہیں ۔ سھر بمعنی بیدار رہنے کے ہیں۔ ظلم الدياجر بفتح اللام جمع ظلمه دیا جر جمع ہے دیجور کی بمعنی اللیل المظلم
So from those glosses they were not disclosed; rather, they were content with non-authoritative matters that were like irrelevant things not intended, which were obtained from those glosses. The fingertips of reflections cannot untie the knots of difficulties: 'anamil' (fingertips) is plural of 'anmulah' meaning tips of fingers; 'uqad' is plural of 'uqdah' meaning knot; 'mu'dilat' meaning difficulties. That is, the difficulties that were knotted, the fingers of reflections could not untie them—'hal' meaning to open. So here reflections are likened to the owner of fingertips; this is a metaphorical allusion, and 'isht' (?) of his fingertips and 'hal' of knots are confirmatory. Nor do the fingers of the keys open the doors: i.e., the fingers of expression could not open its locked doors. Here also, by way of metaphorical allusion, expression is likened to someone who conceals what is in the mind; 'banan' (fingers) are necessary for the possessor of fingers; its affirmation is imaginative, and 'fath' (opening) of the difficulties of the book is likened to opening locked doors; the affirmation of locked doors is imaginative, and 'fath' is for benefit, as before. Then after that: i.e., despite those glosses, reflections, and expression, the subtleties of this book 'Al-Tanqih ma'a al-Tawdih' were still hidden and concealed behind strange words—i.e., behind the veils of words. And 'fara'id' (singular 'faridah') is like the beloved from women—meaning a subtlety; the mention of the thing compared and intention of the meaning is explicit, and 'khayam' (tents) is a metaphor for what is like benefits that were still not reached; the lovers were desirous of seeing them, but since the benefits were still concealed, he said: 'You see around them aspirations'—i.e., around those tents of benefits, you see aspirations that have raised their necks but cannot reach them, and eyes that are wakeful but cannot see them. 'Duna al-wusul' is a circumstantial qualifier related to 'a'yun' (eyes), meaning they are prevented from reaching them, i.e., to those subtleties that are like the most precious. In this sentence, there is also a metaphorical allusion; the raising of necks is imaginative, and it is for intention. I was commanded by the tongue of inspiration—'ilham' here means casting goodness into the heart of another; and inspiration is likened to a speaker of goodness; this is a metaphorical allusion; the affirmation of a speaker that is necessary for the speaker is imaginative—i.e., I was commanded with the tongue of inspiration; this was truly inspiration, not from delusions. What was commanded? He explained: 'That I plunge' meaning entering into water into the depths of its benefits; 'lujaj' is plural of 'lujjah' meaning deep water. 'And dive' meaning going under water, to extract its unparalleled pearls; 'ghurar' is plural of 'ghurrah' meaning the most noble thing and its first; from it: 'ghurrat qawmihi' meaning their leader, and 'ghurrat al-shahr' its beginning; 'fara'id' is plural of 'faridah' meaning the largest pearls; the noblest of pearls, the most precious, having no equal because they are unique in their kind or because they are singular in their value. 'And to unfold the folded secrets'—'nashr' means opening and spreading; 'matwiyat' from 'tayy' meaning folding and rolling up; 'rumuz' plural of 'ramz' meaning signs. 'And to bring out the hidden treasures'—'kunuz' plural of 'kanz' meaning treasures. 'And to make easy the paths of its difficult ways'—'masalik' plural of 'maslak' meaning path; 'shu'ab' plural of 'shu'bah' meaning branch or way. 'And to subdue the wild refractory ones'—'shawarid' plural of 'sharidah' meaning wild; 'si'ab' plural of 'sa'b' meaning rebellious and stubborn. The summary of these sentences is: I was commanded by the tongue of inspiration to enter into the midst of the benefits of this book, which is like a sea, and to dive and extract the pearls and jewels of benefits and subtleties lying within, and to spread out the secrets and signs lying folded in its depths, and to bring out its hidden treasures, and to make easy its most difficult paths, and to subdue its wild, rebellious, and untamable benefits that are like wild animals that cannot be hunted. So that by my effort, the text of 'Tanqih' becomes praiseworthy and its commentary 'Tawdih' becomes more clear. 'Tafaqa' meaning started and entered upon the completion of entering into a matter; 'sharshafah' (?) ; 'mawarid' plural of 'mawrid' meaning place of arrival, also a watering place where people and animals come for water. 'Sahar' meaning staying awake at night. 'Zulm al-dayajir' with fatha on lam, plural of 'zulmah'; 'dayajir' plural of 'dijur' meaning very dark night.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to his commentary on Al-Tawdih (the commentary on Al-Tanqih). He begins by lamenting that previous glosses and explanations failed to unlock the difficulties of the text. Using a series of elaborate metaphors, he describes the text's subtleties as knots that the fingers of ordinary reflection cannot untie, and its meanings as locked doors that ordinary expression cannot open. He then declares that despite these previous efforts, the true subtleties remained hidden. He likens these hidden benefits to precious tents around which aspirations circle but cannot enter, and to a beloved whom lovers desire but cannot attain. Then he states that he was commanded by divine inspiration ('amartu bi-lisan al-ilham') to plunge into the depths of the book's benefits, dive to extract its pearls (fara'id), unfold its folded secrets, reveal its hidden treasures, make easy its difficult paths, and subdue its refractory elements. The purpose of his entire endeavor is to make the original text (Al-Tanqih) praiseworthy and its commentary (Al-Tawdih) more clear. This preface establishes the author's authority and explains his motivation: he is not writing out of personal ambition but in response to a divine call. The heavily poetic language reflects the high literary style of classical Islamic scholarship and emphasizes the perceived value and depth of the text.

Key Terms
انامل (anamīl): Fingertips; used metaphorically for the extremities of intellectual effort.
عقد معضلات (uqad mu'dilāt): Knots of difficulties; refers to complex legal problems in the text.
فرائد (farā'id): Precious pearls; metaphor for the most valuable insights and rulings.
لسان الالهام (lisān al-ilhām): Tongue of inspiration; a divine command conveyed through inspiration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what compelled him to write this commentary?
A) The request of his teacher
B) His own desire for fame
C) Divine inspiration (lisan al-ilham)
D) The publisher's demand

Key Takeaway
The author uses the claim of divine inspiration as a rhetorical foundation to establish the necessity and authority of his commentary.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Author's Introduction: Inspiration and Effort in Writing a Commentary
Author describes his divine inspiration and effort

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's claim about divine inspiration and distinguish it from a legal source of law in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The author claims his commentary was inspired, but in Hanafi usul, ilhām is not a legal source—only a personal motivation.

This passage is the author's preface to his commentary on a foundational usul text. He asserts that his work was commanded by divine inspiration and describes his immense effort using vivid metaphors. Understanding this introduction helps us appreciate the author's methodology and authority, while also recognizing the boundaries of inspiration within Hanafi legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim of Inspiration
Find where the author states he was commanded by 'the tongue of inspiration' (lisān al-ilhām). Note that he explicitly denies it is a delusion (wahm).
This is a rhetorical device to assert the work's spiritual foundation.
2
Parse the Metaphors
The author uses several similes: diving into a sea for pearls, hunting wild animals, and riding difficult camels. Each metaphor represents a facet of his scholarly labor—extracting profound meanings, solving difficult issues, and mastering the subject.
These metaphors are not legal arguments but literary flourishes.
3
Understand the Rhetorical Purpose
The introduction aims to establish the author's credibility and the prestige of his work. By invoking inspiration, he aligns his effort with divine guidance, which was a common trope in classical scholarship.
This does not make the commentary a revealed text.
4
Distinguish from Legal Authority
In Hanafi usul, ilhām (inspiration) is not a source of law (dalīl shar‘ī). Authoritative rulings derive from Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. The author's claim here is personal and motivational, not legislative.
This distinction is crucial for evaluating the weight of the commentary.

اپنی بھی کبھی طاقت کبھی ادھر لگا دی ۔ حتی استولیت حتی کہ اس کتاب کے کے بارہ میں غایتہ قصومی پر غلبہ حاصل کر لیا یعنی اس کے جمیع اسرار کو میں نے علمی لحاظ سے کا کرلیا - وامطت الاماطة الازالہ اور اس کے فرائد یعنی وقائق و فوائد لطیفہ جو بمنزلہ فرائد کے تھے ان کے چہرے سے ارتیاب کے قناع اور پر دے دور کر دیتے اور انکا پورا چہرہ کھول کر سامنے کر دیا۔ تو جمعت هذا الشرح اس بد و جہد مذکورہ کے بعد میں نے اس شرح کو جمع کیا جسکا علامتی نام " التلويح الى كشف حقائق التنقيح دکھا تلویح بمعنی تجمیع ہے یعنی کسی چیز کو چکانا، روشن کرنا جیسے کہا جاتا ہے الاح البرق اور مضر
It means 'changing the other', and here inspiration is likened to a person speaking with goodness, and this is a metaphorical allusion. The affirmation that is necessary for the speaker is an analytical affirmation, meaning: I was commanded with the tongue of inspiration. This was truly inspiration, not a delusion. What was commanded? He explained that: 'I plunge into the water in the depths of its benefits' – 'lujaj' is plural of 'lujjah', meaning great water. 'I dive under water' i.e., to dive for pearls. 'gharar' is plural of 'ghurrah', meaning the most noble thing, its beginning; from it is 'ghurratu qawmihi' i.e., their master, and 'ghurratu ash-shahr' i.e., its beginning. 'fara'id' is plural of 'faridah', meaning the largest pearls. 'farā'id ad-durar' are the great ones, having no equivalent, because they are unique in their kind or singular in their value. 'an-nashr' means unfolding; 'matwiyāt' is derived from 'tayy' meaning folding; 'rumūz' is plural of 'ramz' meaning signs. 'I display the hidden treasures' – 'kunūz' is plural of 'kanz' meaning treasures. 'I make easy the paths of its difficulties' – 'masālik' plural of 'maslak' and 'shi'āb' plural of 'shu'bah' meaning branching paths. 'I subdue the fleeing ones of its battle' – 'adhlil' meaning subdue, 'shawārid' plural of 'shāridah' meaning fleeing, 'si'āb' plural of 'sa'b' meaning rebellious and stubborn. The summary of these sentences is that I was commanded by the tongue of inspiration to enter into the benefits of this book which are like a sea, and to dive and extract the pearls and jewels of benefits and subtleties, and to display them, and to bring forth the signs and indications lying in its depths, and to manifest its hidden treasures, and to make its most difficult paths easy and smooth, and to subdue its scattered benefits which are like wild animals, untamed and not hunted by anyone, so that by my effort the text of Tanqih becomes established and its commentary Tawdih becomes clearer. 'Tafiqa' means he began, 'ajal' meaning completion, 'dukhul' in a matter. 'Mawārid' is plural of 'mawrid' meaning place of arrival or drinking place; people and animals come to water. 'Sahar' means staying awake. 'Zulam ad-dayājir' – 'zulam' plural of 'zulmah', 'dayājir' plural of 'dayjūr' meaning dark night. Dark nights. He endured the hardships of thought in the thirsts of midday heats. 'Ihtamal' means bear difficulty, 'makābid' plural of 'makbadah' or 'kabid' meaning hardship, 'zama' means thirst, 'hawājir' plural of 'hājirah' which is midday heat. Riding every difficult and easy mount – 'as-sa'b' is the untrained camel that does not submit to any rider, and 'dhalūl' is the submissive camel. For hunting the wild ones of the principles – 'al-iqtinās' means hunting, 'shawārid' meaning wild animals that flee from humans. With this word, from the principles' difficult issues and problems that were unsolvable – this sentence comprises a simile. Meaning the commentator endured wakefulness of nights and hardships of summers in extracting the precise issues and subtle points of the science of principles, and endured the pains of deep thought and precise reflections. He likened this state to that of a hunter when hunting game: for example, pursuing them at their watering places and at night in their lairs, and riding both difficult and easy mounts. The hardships that hunters endure, the commentator compared his own severe state in obtaining these principles' subtleties and delicacies. He drained the last of his effort – 'an-nazf' means extracting water from a well, 'al-ulālah' means the remainder of milk in the udder, used for remainder of anything absolutely. Meaning to reach the goals of the chapters and sections, I exerted all my effort and energy from my side, and sometimes directed my power here. Until I gained mastery over this book's ultimate goal, i.e., I scientifically encompassed all its secrets. And I removed the veil of doubt from the face of its unique pearls, i.e., the facts and subtle benefits that are like pearls, and unveiled them fully. Then I compiled this commentary after the aforementioned effort, whose symbolic name is 'At-Talwīḥ ilā Kashfi Ḥaqā'iq at-Tanqīḥ'. Talwīḥ means making something shine or brighten, as said 'lama'a al-barq' (the lightning flashed).
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage is the author's introduction to his commentary, explaining the divine inspiration and immense effort behind it. He begins by stating that he was commanded by the 'tongue of inspiration' (lisān al-ilhām) to undertake this work—a claim that this is not a delusion but true inspiration. He then uses elaborate metaphors: diving into a sea of benefits to extract pearls (the profound meanings), unfolding hidden signs, and subduing wild animals (difficult issues). He compares his scholarly struggle to a hunter tracking game through night and day, riding both gentle and stubborn mounts. He emphasizes his sleepless nights and hot days of labor, ultimately mastering the book's secrets and clarifying its ambiguities. The result is this commentary, titled 'At-Talwīḥ ilā Kashfi Ḥaqā'iq at-Tanqīḥ'. Note that the author frames his work as guided by inspiration, a common trope in scholarly introductions to assert authority and sincerity. The text functions as front matter, setting the stage for the technical usul discussions that follow.

Key Terms
لسان الهام (lisān al-ilhām): The tongue of inspiration—the author claims he received a command through divine inspiration, not a mere delusion.
تمثیل (tamthīl): Simile or analogy—the author likens his scholarly efforts to a hunter's struggles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author claim about the source of his command to write the commentary?
A) He was instructed by a living teacher.
B) He was commanded by divine inspiration (ilhām).
C) He deduced it through pure reason.
D) He was ordered by a caliph.

Key Takeaway
The author's introduction uses the trope of divine inspiration to assert the significance of his commentary, but in Hanafi usul, ilhām is not a source of legal authority—it is a personal motivation.
