The Purpose and Methodology of Al-Talwih
Author explains title and methodology of his commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the function of a usul commentary as described by the author and interpret the title 'Al-Talwih'.

Core Idea
The title 'Al-Talwih' signifies that a commentary both alludes to and reveals the deeper truths of the base text.

In this short preface, the author sets out his scholarly methodology. He explains why he named his commentary 'Al-Talwih' and describes the various analytical tools he employs to unlock the meanings of al-Tanqih. Understanding this preface gives us insight into how Hanafi usul scholars approach commentary writing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated purpose
Read the passage and note why the author wrote this commentary. He states he relied upon Allah and composed a commentary on al-Tanqih with specific goals.
The author mentions establishing rules, opening knots, interpreting purposes, and multiplying benefits.
2
Analyze the literal meaning of 'talwih'
Talwih means 'allusion' or 'shining'. How does this relate to the function of the commentary? The author says it 'unveils the truths' of al-Tanqih.
The title reflects the commentary's role in revealing hidden meanings.

The author mentions taqrirat (expositions), tahqiqat (verifications), tawjibat (explanations), and taqsimat (divisions). What does each contribute?

How does the commentary 'unveil the truths' of al-Tanqih? The author says his work is 'kashif li haqa'iq al-Tanqih' (unveiler of the truths of al-Tanqih).

بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَٰنِ الرَّحِيمِ. الحمد لله رب العالمين، والصلاة والسلام على سيدنا محمد وآله أجمعين. وبعد: فقد توكلت على الله تعالى في شرح هذا الكتاب الموسوم بـ "التلويح إلى كشف حقائق التنقيح"، مشتملاً على تقرير قواعد الفن، وتحقيق معاقده، وتفسير مقاصده، وتكثير فوائده، مع تنقيح لما بسط، وتوضيح لما اقتصر، في ضمن تقريرات تأخذ الأذهان بأزرارها، وتحقيقيات تهتز لها أعطاف الأفهام، وتوجيهات ينشط بها الكسلان، وتقسيمات يطرب لها الشكلان. وقد سميته بـ "التلويح" لأن التلويح الإشارة واللمعان، وهو كاشف لحقائق التنقيح، موضح لمباني التوضيح، والله أسأل أن ينفع به ويجعله خالصاً لوجهه الكريم، إنه سميع مجيب.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds, and peace and blessings be upon our master Muhammad and his family. After: I have relied upon Allah Almighty in commenting on this book titled 'Al-Talwih ila Kashf Haqa'iq al-Tanqih', comprising the establishment of the rules of the discipline, the opening of its knots, the interpretation of its purposes, the multiplication of its benefits, along with summarizing what was expanded, and clarifying what was brief, in the form of expositions that captivate minds, verifications that make intellects sway, explanations that enliven the lazy, and divisions that delight the old. I have named it 'Al-Talwih' because talwih means indicating and shining, and it unveils the truths of al-Tanqih and clarifies the foundations of al-Tawdih. I ask Allah to make it beneficial and purely for His noble face. Indeed, He is All-Hearing, All-Answering.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to his commentary on al-Tanqih (by Sadr al-Shari'ah). He explains the title of his work 'Al-Talwih ila Kashf Haqa'iq al-Tanqih' (The Allusion to Unveiling the Truths of al-Tanqih). The author describes the extensive effort and hardship he endured in writing this commentary, likening himself to a hunter who braves difficult terrain and sleepless nights. He states that his commentary will accomplish several goals: it will establish the rules of the discipline (usul), open difficult knots (i.e., resolve complex issues), interpret the purposes of the original text, and multiply its benefits. Where the original author (al-Tanqih) expanded, he will summarize; where the author was brief, he will clarify. He further describes the work's style as containing captivating expositions (taqrirat) that seize the minds, verifications (tahqiqat) that make intellects sway with joy, explanations (tawjibat) that rouse the lazy, and divisions (taqsimat) that delight the elderly (shiklan). The name 'Talwih' is chosen because it means 'allusion' or 'shining', indicating that the commentary reveals the truths of the original text (al-Tanqih) and clarifies its foundations. This preface sets the tone for the work and highlights the author's scholarly methodology.

Key Terms
التلويح (al-Talwih): The title of the commentary, meaning 'the allusion' or 'the shining', indicating that the book alludes to and reveals the truths of al-Tanqih.
التنقيح (al-Tanqih): The original matn (text) by Sadr al-Shari'ah on usul al-fiqh, meaning 'the refinement'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The preface of Al-Talwih reveals that the author's commentary is designed to be a comprehensive guide that unveils the truths of al-Tanqih through exposition, verification, explanation, and division.

Author's Preface: Methodology and Scope of the Commentary
Author's methodological preface

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's methodological commitments (reliance on mutun al-riwaya, avoidance of nawadir) and explain why they are important for the authority of a Hanafi usul commentary.

Core Idea
Reliance on well-known authentic narrations (mutun al-riwaya) and avoidance of rare reports (nawadir) ensures the commentary's authority.

This preface sets the rigorous standard for the commentary. The author explicitly states that he will rely only on the well-established narrations of the school (mutun al-riwaya) and ignore rare or deviant reports. Understanding this methodology is crucial for appreciating how later Hanafi works were constructed and why certain positions are given precedence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated goals

Mutun al-riwaya = the six books of Imam Muhammad; nawadir = rare reports (e.g., from Hasan ibn Ziyad).
3
Recognize the intended audience and prerequisites
The author lists conditions for benefiting from the commentary: expertise in both Hanafi and Shafi'i usul, knowledge of tawjih wa ta'dil, and mastery of logic. This shows the work is for advanced scholars.
This explains why the commentary is not a beginner text; it assumes prior knowledge.

Praise be to God? ... This book Al-Talwih will be comprised of the presentation of the rules of the science and the writing of knots, meaning difficulties. It will interpret the purposes of the book, i.e., the purposes of Al-Tanqih and Al-Tawdih, and present many benefits clearly. Where the author expanded words, I will summarize; where he abbreviated, I will explain. All this will be in such presentations as to open the minds of the listeners. ... Reliance is on the well-known authentic narrations (mutun al-riwaya al-muhkama), and attention is not given to rare (nawadir) and unusual reports. Standing in the eyes of knowledge means to stay in the pure intellectual matters. Whoever dives into research will find the jewels of investigation. This book cannot be opened except by the expert from the two groups (Hanafis and Shafi'is). And none is worthy except the one who excels in the principles of the Hanafis and Shafi'is, with a knowledge of the art of tawjih and ta'dil, and mastery of the laws of logic. God, whose authority is mighty, is the one who grants success; He is sufficient for me.
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface to his commentary on Al-Tawdih and Al-Talwih. He begins by describing the book's content: it will clarify the difficult knots of the science. He compares the learning process to pearls forming in oysters when rain falls. He then states his methodology: where the original author was verbose, he will summarize; where he was concise, he will explain. He emphasizes that his work relies solely on the well-known authentic narrations (mutun al-riwaya al-muhkama) and ignores rare and deviant narrations (nawadir). This is a hallmark of the Hanafi school: preferring the zahir al-riwaya over shadhdh narratives. He further stipulates that the commentary is not for beginners; only those who are expert in both Hanafi and Shafi'i usul, and skilled in the art of reconciling divergent evidences (tawjih wa ta'dil) and logic, can truly benefit. The author concludes by invoking God's help. This preface sets the authoritative and rigorous tone of the work.

Key Terms
متون الرواية (mutun al-riwaya): The well-known authentic narrations (الرواية المحكمة) that form the core of the Hanafi school; as opposed to nawadir (rare reports).
نوادر (nawadir): Rare or unusual narrations that are not relied upon in the school's primary rulings.

Introduction and Front Matter

8 min
The Hanafi Source Hierarchy: Mutun al-Riwayah vs Nawadir
Author's preface on source hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mutun al-riwayah and nawadir and state the Hanafi rule that only the former are authoritative for argumentation.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, only mutun al-riwayah (Zahir al-Riwayah) are relied upon for proof; nawadir carry no weight.

This preface establishes the foundation of Hanafi methodology: not all transmitted texts are equal. The author clarifies that when constructing arguments, only authentic and widely transmitted narrations (mutun al-riwayah) may be used, while rare reports (nawadir) are set aside. This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi approach to istidlal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of texts
From the passage, pick out the terms 'mutun al-riwayah' and 'nawadir'. Understand that they represent two levels of authority in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the definition of mutun al-riwayah
These are the six well-known books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah), which contain the most authentic and widely accepted rulings of the school.
3
Understand the definition of nawadir
These are rare narrations transmitted from the founders via individual transmitters like Hasan ibn Ziyad; they are not considered reliable for legal argumentation.
4
State the rule
The author says 'reliance is upon mutun al-riwayah, not on nawadir.' This is a fundamental methodological principle for Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the rule
When seeking a Hanafi ruling, first consult a Zahir al-Riwayah text (e.g., al-Hidayah). If a nawadir report contradicts, it is disregarded.

وسيجد - ۔ یعنی جو شخص بھار تحقیق میں غوطہ لگا سکتا ہے اور الر تولے کیجانب سے انوار توفیق کا بھی اسپر فیضان ہو تو اس شرح کے اندر جو جو ہر تحقیق اور درر تدقیق ودیعت رکھے ہیں دریافت کر لیگا اور پالیگا - الذى یعنی یہ التلویح ایسی کتاب ہے کہ اس کے حقائق سے قناع الخالص کتا شخص نہیں کھول سكتا . الا الماهر مر - علماء الفريقير فریقین یعنی اخاف و شوافع کے علماء میں سے ماہر ہوگا ۔ ولا يستاهل - اور اس کتا اندر جو دقائق ہیں انپر اطلاع حاصل کرنے کی اہمیت نہیں رکھتا الا البارع مگر وہ شخضر جو فائق هو في اصول المذه اصول الاحناف واصول الشوافع - مع بضاعة من صنا. صناعة التوجيه والتعدیل ۔ اور اسکو متاع علمی فن وجیه و تعدیل سے بھی حاصل ہو لینی علم اخلاف میں جو تو جیبہ و تعدیل کے قوانین ہیں یہ سبھی اسے حاصل ہوں - واحاطة بقوانين توانین منطق جو تحصیل اور اکتساب مجہولات کے طریق کو واضح کرتے ہیں ان پر اسے پورا جو احاطہ حاصل ہو۔ واللہ عز سلطانہ اور اللہ جس کی سلطنت عزیز و غالب ہے وہی ولی اعانہ اور تائید ہے ۔ الملح ای بعت در با فاضة الاصابة و التسديد - یعنی صواب و سداد تک پہنچانا اسی کی قدرت میں ہے. وهو حسبي كيل يا تو نعم الوکیل کا عطف صرف لفظ حسبی پر ہے اگر چہ یہ ظاہرا سفرد ہے لیکن معنی جملہ ہے جو بتا ویل کمپنی ہے اور اس صورت میں محضوض بالمدح وہی ضمیر ہو ہوگی جو حسبی کے لئے مبتدا اور راجع بوتے اللہ تعالٰی ہے ۔ یا نعم الوکیل کا عطف سالم جملہ ہو حسبی پر ہے اور مخصوص بالمدح اس صورت میں محذوف ہوگا کہ در اصل نعم الوکیل اللہ ہے۔ لیکن دونوں صورتوں میں خطف الانشار علی الاخبار ہے کیونکہ نعم جو کہ افعال مدح میں سے ہے ! سے انشائدح کے لئے آتا ہے اور ہو حسبی یہ خبر ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ مجھے کافی ہے تو یہ معطف بعض حضرات کے نزدیک غیر مقبول ہے الا یہ کہ ہو حسبی اخبار عن الكفایت نہ ہو بلکہ انشار توکل علی اللہ ہو تو پھر عطف الانشاء علی الانشار ہو وزيادة التحقيق في الخيالي بن. جائے گا ۔ اللهم اغفر لكاتيه ولمن سعى فيه ولوالدي ام والشاي يهتم اجمعين
Reliant on the reliable texts of narration, i.e., relying on the authentic narrations according to what is well-known from the noble books – that is, in the position of argumentation, reliance will be upon authentic, sound narrations, and attention and regard will not be given to rare and unusual narrations. And turning to the eyes of understanding – al-ta'rij 'ala al-shay' means stopping and standing upon it, i.e., stopping upon one point and becoming settled upon it. 'Uyun al-dirayah wa al-riwayah, meaning understanding and transmission; 'uyun is plural of 'ayn which means pure and sincere, i.e., in pure intellectual matters, one will adopt stopping and standing upon those subtle points that are established among the people, i.e., in transmitted proofs, reliance will be upon authentic texts of narration, and in rational proofs, upon what is established among the people. And he will find – i.e., the person who can dive into the ocean of investigation and upon whom the lights of divine assistance flow from the side of the Lord, he will discover and find the jewels of investigation and pearls of exactitude deposited within this commentary. Which – i.e., this al-Talwih is a book whose realities no person can unveil except the expert – from the scholars of the two groups, i.e., the Hanafis and Shafi'is, who is a master. And he does not deserve – i.e., he does not merit obtaining acquaintance with the subtleties within this book except the excellent one, the person who is preeminent in the principles of the school, the principles of the Hanafis and the principles of the Shafi'is, along with a merchandise from the craft of tawjih and ta'dil. And he also obtains from it the academic merchandise of the science of tawjih and ta'dil, the laws of the science of disagreements – all these he has. And encompassing the laws of logic which clarify the method of acquiring and obtaining unknown things – he has complete mastery over them. And Allah, exalted is His authority, He is the Patron of assistance and support. The appendix, i.e., He is the one who grants correctness and rightness. And He is sufficient for me – either 'and what an excellent trustee' is conjoined only to the word 'hasbi', although it is apparently a single word but it is a sentence in meaning, and in that case the one praised by the laudatory verb is the same pronoun which is the subject for 'hasbi' and refers back to Allah Almighty. Or the conjunction of 'and what an excellent trustee' is a complete sentence with 'hasbi', and the one praised by the laudatory verb is omitted in that case, because in origin it is 'What an excellent trustee is Allah'. But in both forms, there is a conjunction of a performative (insha') upon an informative (khabar) because 'ni'ma' which is one of the verbs of praise comes for praise (insha') and 'huwa hasbi' is an informative sentence that Allah suffices me, so this conjunction is not acceptable according to some, unless 'huwa hasbi' is not informing about sufficiency but rather is a performative of trust in Allah; then the conjunction of performative upon performative would be valid. And more verification in the margin. O Allah, forgive its writer and whoever seeks in it, and my parents, and all believers.
Source pages p. 28

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface, establishing the methodology and intended readership of the commentary. The author begins by stating that in argumentation, reliance must be placed on mutun al-riwayah, which are the authentic, well-known transmitted texts (the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani). Rare narrations (nawadir) from individual transmitters are not to be given consideration. This reflects the Hanafi principle that Zahir al-Riwayah texts carry the highest authority. The author then clarifies that the book aims to combine both transmitted and rational proofs: in transmitted matters one depends on authentic narrations; in rational matters one depends on established principles agreed upon by the scholars. The work is titled al-Talwih, and its intended audience is a 'mahir' (expert) who is well-versed in the usul of both the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools, as well as in the sciences of jarh wa ta'dil (criticism of narrators) and logic. This high bar indicates the depth and rigor of the commentary. The preface ends with a grammatical discussion of the phrase 'huwa hasbi wa ni'mal-wakil' from the Quran. The author notes a subtle issue: conjunction of an insha' (performative) with a khabar (informative) is normally not allowed, but here if 'huwa hasbi' is itself interpreted as an insha' (a declaration of reliance on Allah), the conjunction becomes acceptable. Finally, the author invokes a prayer for forgiveness, which is a standard concluding formula.

Key Terms
متون الرواية (mutūn al-riwāyah): The authentic, well-known transmitted texts of the school, particularly the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah).
نوادر (nawādir): Rare or odd narrations transmitted from the founders of the school but not widely accepted, often via individual transmitters like Hasan ibn Ziyad.
التلويح (al-Talwīḥ): The title of this commentary by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani on al-Tawdih of Sadr al-Shariah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's preface, on what type of transmitted texts should one rely in argumentation?
A) Nawadir narrations
B) Mutun al-riwayah (authentic well-known texts)
C) Any narration from Abu Hanifa
D) Personal opinion of the scholar

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, only mutun al-riwayah (Zahir al-Riwayah) are acceptable proofs; nawadir are excluded.

Introduction and Front Matter
advanced
6 min
The Prerequisites for Studying al-Talwih: Expertise in Usul, Jarh wa Ta'dil, and Mantiq
Author's description of the intended readership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three areas of expertise required to benefit from al-Talwih and explain why each is necessary.

Core Idea
Al-Talwih's depth demands mastery of Hanafi and Shafi'i usul, hadith criticism, and logic.

The author sets a high bar for readers of his commentary. One must be a mahir (expert) in the usul of both Hanafi and Shafi'i schools, have a solid grounding in jarh wa ta'dil (criticism of narrators), and be proficient in mantiq (logic). This ensures that only qualified scholars engage with the nuanced discussions in al-Talwih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prerequisites
From the passage, find the three conditions: expertise in usul al-fiqh of both Hanafis and Shafi'is, proficiency in jarh wa ta'dil (science of criticising and authenticating narrators), and mastery of mantiq (logic).
2
Understand why usul of both schools is required
Al-Talwih often compares Hanafi and Shafi'i positions; the reader must understand both to follow the arguments and evaluate the tarjih.
3
Understand the role of jarh wa ta'dil
The science of jarh wa ta'dil is necessary to evaluate the reliability of narrations, especially when discussing differences in transmission.
4
Understand the role of mantiq
Mantiq provides the tools for sound reasoning and argumentation, essential for the logical structure of usul debates.
5
Recognize the high standard set by the author
The author uses terms like 'mahir' and 'bar' to indicate that only advanced scholars can fully benefit from this work; beginners are not the intended audience.

معولا في متون الرواية معولا اى معتمدا متون الرواية أى الرواية المحكمة على ما اشتهر من الكتب الشريفة - یعنی مقام استدلال میں رو آسیا محکمہ صحیحہ کے اوپر اعتماد ہوگا اور نوادرو شو از روایات کی طرف توجہ اور التفات نہیں کیا جائے گا ۔ معرجافيني عيون الدراية - Reliant on the reliable texts of narration, i.e., relying on the authentic narrations according to what is well-known from the noble books – that is, in the position of argumentation, reliance will be upon authentic, sound narrations, and attention and regard will not be given to rare and unusual narrations. Commentary
This passage is the author's preface, establishing the methodology and intended readership of the commentary. The author begins by stating that in argumentation, reliance must be placed on mutun al-riwayah, which are the authentic, well-known transmitted texts (the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani). The author then clarifies that the book aims to combine both transmitted and rational proofs: in transmitted matters one depends on authentic narrations; in rational matters one depends on established principles agreed upon by the scholars. The work is titled al-Talwih, and its intended audience is a 'mahir' (expert) who is well-versed in the usul of both the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools, as well as in the sciences of jarh wa ta'dil (criticism of narrators) and logic. This high bar indicates the depth and rigor of the commentary. The preface ends with a grammatical discussion of the phrase 'huwa hasbi wa ni'mal-wakil' from the Quran. Key Terms
متون الرواية (mutūn al-riwāyah): The authentic, well-known transmitted texts of the school, particularly the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (Zahir al-Riwayah).
نوادر (nawādir): Rare or odd narrations transmitted from the founders of the school but not widely accepted, often via individual transmitters like Hasan ibn Ziyad.
التلويح (al-Talwīḥ): The title of this commentary by Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani on al-Tawdih of Sadr al-Shariah.
توجيه و تعديل (tawjih wa ta'dil): The science of reconciling conflicting evidence (tawjih) and evaluating the reliability of narrators (ta'dil).
قوانين منطق (qawanin al-mantiq): The laws of logic, which provide a systematic method for deriving unknown conclusions from known premises.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Rhetorical Function of Hal in the Author's Preamble
Justification of the hal construction for hamd in the author's preamble

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two rhetorical functions (taswiyah and proportionality) of the hal construction 'حامدا' in the author's preamble and identify the reasons for omitting the conjunction and prioritising tasmiyah over hamd.

Core Idea
The hal construction equates tasmiyah and hamd as equal preconditions for any valid beginning.

In the opening of Al-Tawdih wa Al-Talwih, the author uses the word 'حامدا' in the accusative state (hal) rather than a verbal sentence like 'أحمد الله'. This seemingly grammatical choice carries deep rhetorical significance, as it establishes tasmiyah and hamd as equal and necessary conditions for the commencement of the work. The commentator unpacks this choice, explaining the need for equality (taswiyah) and proportionality (ri'aya al-tanassub), and addresses potential objections about word order and conjunction to preserve the intended parity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Grammatical Construction
Recognize that 'حامدا' is a hal (circumstantial accusative) and the implied verb is 'أبتدئ' or similar, not a separate sentence. This sets the stage for the author's rhetorical intent.
The hal indicates the state of the doer at the time of the action.
2
Understand the Alternative
Consider what the author could have written instead, such as 'أحمد الله' or 'أحمد الله تعالى' (a verbal sentence). The commentator explicitly notes this alternative was avoided.
The alternative would have been grammatically simpler but rhetorically weaker.
3
Discover the Rhetorical Goal: Taswiyah
The commentator explains that the hal construction achieves taswiyah (equality) between tasmiyah and hamd, making both equally necessary for the beginning. This is the key reason for the choice.
Taswiyah ensures that neither act is subordinate to the other.
4
See Proportionality
By making both 'بسم الله' (implied hal) and 'حامدا' (explicit hal) in the same grammatical form, the author maintains proportionality (ri'aya al-tanassub), so the two conditions are of the same kind.
Proportionality reinforces the equality.
5
Analyze Textual Issues: Conjunction and Ordering
The omission of the conjunction (wa) avoids implying subordination of hamd to tasmiyah. The ordering (tasmiyah first) is justified by conflicting hadiths; tasmiyah is prioritized based on Quran and consensus, making hamd a relative beginning.
These details show the author's careful balancing of textual authorities.

حامد الله تعالى اولا وثانيا ولسان الثناء اليه ثانياه وعلى افضل رسله محمد واله مصليات وفي حلبة . الصلوات مجليا ومصلياه حال من المستكب الخ یعنی لفظ حامدا ترکیبی لحاظ سے حال ہے اس ضمیر سے جو باشم کے متعلق یعنی ابتدئی میں مستکن اور ستر ہے اسی ابتدی الکتاب حامدا - ابتدی کا مفعول ذکر کر کے اشارہ کیا کہ حقیقت بہ اللہ کی با ظرف لغو صله ابتدی ہو کر واقع موقع المفعول به نہیں دور نہ تو معنی یہ ہوگا کہ شروع کرتا ہوں تعمیر کو کتاب کی ابتدار تو بالتسمیہ نہ ہوئی حالانکہ مقصود ثانی ہے ۔ بلکہ در حقیقت بار کا متعلق متبرکا ہے جس کے اندر لفظ ابتدی حامل ہے ۔ معنی یہ ہوگا کہ مستر کا بالله ابتدئ الكتاب - اسی طرح حامدا حال ہوگا است رتی کی ضمیر ستان سے اور یہ دونوں حال ابتدئی کی قیدیں ہونگی حامرا معنی ہوگا کہ اسم اللہ کیساتھ تبرک اور اللہ کے لئے حمد کرنے کی حالت میں ابتدائے کتاب کر رہا اشر طريقة الحال - یعنی اس مقام افتتاح اور ابتداء میں طریق متعارف جملہ ہمیر
ہوں۔
احمد احمد اللہ یا جلہ فعلیہ احمد اللہ بولنے کا تھا تو اس کو ترک کر کے طریق حال و اختیار کیا اس کی وجہ ہے کہ تشویة بين الحمد ابو تا که حمد و تسمیہ کے درمیان تسویہ دوبرابری رہے اور رعایتہ تناسب بھی برقرار رہے تویہ سے مراد تو یہ فی امید یہ ہے یعنی حمد اور تسمیہ یہ دونوں
الم
که
ابتداء کی قید ہو جائیں اور وہ ان دونوں سے مقید ہو جائے اور رعایہ تناسب سے مراد یہ ہے دنوں قیدیں ایک ہی جنس سے ہو جائیں یعنی جیسے بالشم مستر کا کے ساتھ متعلق ہو کر حال ہے اسی طرح تحمید بھی حامد کی صورت میں حال آجائے تو اس وقت ابتدار مقید بقید میں ہو جائے گا تو مقصود یہ ہوگا کہ ابتداء کے لئے یہ دونوں قیدیں ضروری ہیں ان کے بدون ابتدار معتبر یہ مستر نہیں ہے ۔ فقد روى في الحديث الذيہ تسمیہ اور تحمید میں مساوات کرنے کی مجھ یش کر رہا ہے مقصد یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں چونکہ تسمیہ اور تحمید دونوں کو ابت رائے فعل میں ضروری قرار دیا گیا ہے اس لئے اس تویہ نے القیدیہ کو اختیار کیا اور ان دونوں کو بصورت حال ابتداء کی قید بنا دیا ۔ فحاول ار يجعل قيدا الا يه تفريع على التسوية ب حالا عنه - یہ متفرع ہے رعایة للام پر یعنی حال بنا کر دونوں کے اندر تن سب کو برت رار رکھا کہ یہ قیود ایک ہی جنس سے ہوں۔ الا انه قدمان

دفع ہے اس اشکال کا کہ مصنف نے ترتیب ذکری کے اندر تسمیہ کو مقد ما ذ کر کیا ہے اور محمد کو مؤخراً یہ تو تسویہ کی جو قصد کی تھی اس کے خلاف ہے تو اس کا جواب دیتے ہوئے کہا کہ لان النصين متعارضا انار یعنی دونوں حدیثیں ظاہرا آپس میں متعارض ہیں کیونکہ ایک حدیث ابتداء بالتسمیہ کو ضروری قرار دیتی ہے اور دوسری ابتداء بالتحمید کو اور دونوں پر بیک وقت عمل کرنا مشکل ہے اذا الابتداء باحد الامرين اخر کیونکہ ایک امر کے ساتھ ابتداء دوسرے کے ساتھ ابتداء کرنے کو فوت کر دیتا ہے لہذا ہمارے لئے یہی ممکن ہے کہ ایک کو دوسرے پر مقدم کریں اس کے ساتھ ابتدار حقیقی ہو جائے گی دوسرے کے ساتھ اضافی یعنی با نسبت ماسوی الاول کے باقی رہی یہ بات کہ کس کے ساتھ ابتدا حقیقی ہونی چاہئے تو اس کو واضح کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ مصنف نے تقدیم تسمیہ کر کے اس کے ساتھ ابتدار حقیقی کی اور حمد کے ساتھ اضافی کیونکہ کتاب مجید پر عمل کرنا اسی کا متقاضی تھا کیونکہ قرآن مجید میں تسمیہ مقدم علی التحمید ہے اور اجماع امت بھی اسی پر منعقد ہے کہ وہ بھی اپنے افعال ذی بال میں تسمیہ کو مقدم علی التجميد کرتے ہیں۔ وترك العاطف یعنی جب تسمیہ اور حمد دونوں بصورت حال ہیں تو ان کے درمیان حرف عاطف کیوں استعمال نہیں کیا مثلاً فحامدا یا وحامدًا بولتا اور اس کا عطف متبو کا پر ہو جاتا جو بسملہ کی باجارہ کا متعلق ہے تو اس کا جواب دیا لئلا يشعر بالتبعية يعني حرف عطف اس چیز کی طرف مشعر ہوتا کہ ادائیگی حمد بالتبع ہے مقصود بالذات نہیں ہے کیونکہ تابعية في اللفظ تابعية في المعنیٰ پر دال ہوتی ہے تو اس صورت میں جو تسویه بین التسميه والتجميد مقصود تھا وہ مختل اور منتقض ہو جاتا ولا يجوزان يكون حامدا الا يعني لفظ يقول جو يقول لما وفقني کے اندر مذکور ہے اس کے فاعل سے حامدا کو حال بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
لان قوله وبعد فان العبد الم یعنی مصنف کے نزدیک نسخہ مقروہ کی جو عبارت ہے فان العبد المتوسل الا اس سے مانع ہے اولاً یہ کہ ان مکسورہ چونکہ صدارة کلام کو تقاضا کرتا ہے اس لئے اس کا ما بعد اس کے ماقبل میں عمل نہیں کر سکتا اور لفظ یقول لفظ ان کے بعد مذکور ہے اور حامدا پہلے جب یہ عمل نہیں کر سکتا تو حامدا اس کے فاعل سے حال نہیں ہو سکتا اور ثانیاً یہ کہ بعد کا مضاف الیہ منوی ہے یعنی بعد الحمد والصلوۃ تو اس صورت میں معنیٰ یوں ہو جائے گا۔ بعد الحمد و الصلاة يقول حامد ا جو کہ خلاف مقصود ہے۔ ثالثاً یہ کہ وبعد کی واو عطف اثناء معطوف میں آجائے گی کیونکہ اس صورت میں عبارت یوں ہو جائے گی وبعد يقول العبد حامد ا حالانکہ متن میں حامدا پہلے اور وابعد اس کے مابعد میں ہے تو معطوف کا کچھ حصہ عاطف
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Praising Allah first and second, and the tongue of praise to Him second, and upon the best of His messengers Muhammad and his family, prayers and salutations. 'حامدا' is a hal (state) grammatically from the pronoun that relates to 'باسم' meaning at the beginning. The author mentioned the object of 'أبتدئ' to indicate that the reality is that 'بسم الله' is a zarf (adverb) connected to 'أبتدئ' and is not in the position of the object. Otherwise the meaning would be 'I begin the construction of the book with the tasmiyah' which is not intended. Rather, 'بار' (?) is connected to 'متباركا' which contains the word 'ابتدى'. The meaning is that 'I begin the book with the name of Allah'. Similarly, 'حامدا' is a hal from the pronoun of 'استعنت', and these two are conditions for the beginning. The meaning is 'I am initiating the book in the state of seeking blessing with the name of Allah and praising Allah'. He adopted the method of hal – that is, at this place of opening and beginning, the conventional method of the sentence... He could have said 'أحمد الله' or the verbal sentence, but he left it and adopted the method of hal. The reason is to establish equality between hamd and tasmiyah so that they are equal and maintain proportionality. This equality means that both become conditions for the beginning, and proportionality means that both conditions are of the same kind. Just as 'باسم' is a hal connected to the implied verb, similarly 'تحميد' comes as 'حامدا' in the form of hal. Thus the beginning becomes bound by both conditions, meaning that both conditions are essential for the beginning; without them the beginning is not valid. For it is narrated in the hadith that... He is striving to equalize tasmiyah and hamd. The intent is that since the hadith made both tasmiyah and hamd necessary in the beginning of an action, he adopted 'القيدية' and made both conditions in the form of hal. So he tried to make them conditions... This is a branch of maintaining proportionality, meaning by making them hal, he maintained their equality as conditions of the same kind. Except that they progressed... [Page 31] This is a response to the objection that the author mentioned tasmiyah first and hamd later, contrary to the intent of equality. He said: 'Because the two texts are apparently conflicting.' One hadith makes beginning with tasmiyah necessary, another makes beginning with hamd necessary, and it is difficult to act on both simultaneously because beginning with one precludes beginning with the other. So the only possibility is to give precedence to one over the other. One becomes the real beginning, the other relative. As to which should be the real beginning, he clarified: the author gave precedence to tasmiyah as the real beginning and hamd as relative, because acting on the Noble Book (Quran) required that, since in the Quran tasmiyah precedes hamd, and the consensus of the Ummah is also on that – they give precedence to tasmiyah over hamd in their significant actions. He omitted the conjunction – that is, when both tasmiyah and hamd are in the form of hal, why was the conjunction not used, e.g., 'fahamidan' or 'wahamidan'? The answer: 'لئلا يشعر بالتبعية' – meaning the conjunction indicates that the performance of hamd is subordinate, not the primary intent, because subordination in wording indicates subordination in meaning. In that case, the intended equality between tasmiyah and hamd would be disrupted and invalidated. It is not permissible to make 'حامدا' a hal from the agent of 'يقول' which appears in 'لما وفقني'... Because his statement 'وبعد فان العبد' – meaning according to the author, the reading of the manuscript is 'فان العبد المتوسل' [؟] – hinders. First, because 'إن' with kasrah requires being at the beginning of the sentence, so what follows cannot have grammatical influence on what precedes, and the word 'يقول' is after 'إن', while 'حامدا' is before, so it cannot be a hal from its agent. Second, because 'بعد' has an implied idafah: 'بعد الحمد والصلوة', so the meaning becomes 'After praise and prayer, he says praising', which is contrary to the intent. Third, because the waw of 'وبعد' would be a conjunction within the conjunctive phrase, because in that case the expression would be 'وبعد يقول العبد حامدا' while in the text 'حامدا' is before 'وبعد' in its place, so part of the conjunctive phrase comes after the conjunction.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an analysis of the author's choice of the word 'حامدا' (praising) as a hal (state) rather than using a verbal sentence like 'أحمد الله' (I praise Allah). The commentator explains that this grammatical choice serves a rhetorical purpose: to establish equality (taswiyah) between the tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah') and the hamd (praise of Allah) as preconditions for beginning the book. By making both 'بسم الله' (an implied hal) and 'حامدا' (an explicit hal) conditions of the beginning, the author emphasizes that both are necessary and of equal importance. The commentator then addresses potential objections: first, why tasmiyah is mentioned before hamd in the text, contrary to the intended equality. The answer is that the two hadiths (one commanding beginning with tasmiyah, another with hamd) are apparently conflicting, so it is necessary to give precedence to one. The author prioritized tasmiyah because the Quran itself begins with the Basmalah, and the Ummah's consensus also gives precedence to tasmiyah. The hamd is then a relative beginning. Second, why no conjunction (like 'و') between the two hal phrases. The commentator explains that using a conjunction would imply that the hamd is subordinate to the tasmiyah, undermining the intended equality. Therefore, the author deliberately omitted the conjunction. Finally, the commentator argues against a potential grammatical parsing (making 'حامدا' from the agent of 'يقول' in the phrase 'لما وفقني') by citing textual and syntactic reasons, including the presence of 'إن' and the position of words. This is a typical front-matter discussion in Hanafi usul works, where the author's methodology and textual choices are justified.

Key Terms
حال (hal): A grammatical state (accusative) indicating the condition of the doer at the time of the action.
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): Saying 'بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم' (In the name of Allah).
تحمید (tahmid): Saying 'الحمد لله' (Praise be to Allah) or expressing praise.
تسویہ (taswiyah): Equality; in this context, making tasmiyah and hamd equally essential preconditions.
رعایة التناسب (ri'aya al-tanassub): Maintaining proportionality; ensuring that both conditions are of the same grammatical form.
تبعية (taba'iyyah): Subordination; the state of being secondary or dependent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author choose the word 'حامدا' (a hal construction) instead of using a verbal sentence like 'أحمد الله'?
A) To make the grammar easier for readers.
B) To give equal weight to tasmiyah and hamd as essential conditions for beginning the book.
C) Because he was forced by the rhyme of the text.
D) To show that hamd is more important than tasmiyah.

Key Takeaway
The author's use of 'حامدا' as a hal serves to equalize tasmiyah and hamd as essential preconditions for beginning, a rhetorical strategy that carries hermeneutic weight in the usul tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The First Aspect of Hamd: Praise for Essence and Blessings
First interpretation of the twofold division of hamd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hamd on Allah's essence and hamd on His blessings, and explain how the phrase 'awwalan wa thaniyan' encompasses both.

Core Idea
Hamd includes praise for Allah's perfect essence independent of blessings, and gratitude for His favors.

This lesson unpacks the first interpretation of 'awwalan wa thaniyan' in the opening of Al-Tawdih. The commentator explains that 'awwalan' refers to praise for Allah's essential perfections, while 'thaniyan' refers to praise for His blessings. This distinction is rooted in the nature of hamd, which does not require receiving a blessing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two-fold division
Recognize that 'awwalan wa thaniyan' divides hamd into two categories: praise for essence and praise for blessings. Note that the commentator uses this as the first of three aspects.
The division is not redundant; each part has a distinct referent.
2
Analyze the definition of hamd
Understand that hamd, unlike shukr, does not require the recipient to have received a blessing. It can be for intrinsic perfections. This is the key linguistic premise.
This distinguishes hamd from shukr in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply 'awwalan' to Allah's essence
Allah is deserving of praise (mustahiqq al-hamd) for His perfect essence (dhāt kāmila) and great attributes (ṣifāt ‘aẓīma), which are inherently praiseworthy.
This praise is independent of any blessing reaching the servant.
4
Apply 'thaniyan' to Allah's blessings
Allah is also deserving of praise for His beautiful blessings (ni‘am) and abundant favors, especially the grace of enabling the author to compose this book.
This praise is contingent upon receiving blessings.

الرحیم کے ساتھ ابقار اول کی طرف اشارہ کیا گیا ہے کیونکہ ان کا مفہوم ہے المنعم سجلائل النعم ودقائقها کما ہو مذکور فی البیضاوی اور ان ہی نعمتوں پر نوع انسان کا بقافی الدنیا موقوف ہے اور مالک یوم الدین میں ایجاد ثانی کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور ایاک نعبد کے ساتھ ابھارثانی کی طرف اشارہ کیونکہ توحید اور عبادت کے جو منافع ہیں ان کا حصول فی الآخرت ہوگا جس کے نتیجہ میں وصول الی الجنہ ہو گا جو رحمتہ وسیعہ کا مظہر ہے ۔ دوسری سورۃ جس کی افتتاح بالتحمید ہے وہ انعام ہے اور تیسری کہف سورۃ انعام میں ایجاد اول کی طرف اشارہ ہے بقولہ تعالیٰ الحَمدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِي خَلَقَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وَجَعَلَ الظُّلُمَاتِ والنور اور دوسری آیت میں ہے هُوَ الَّذِي خَلَقَكُرُ مِن طِينِ الاية یہ سب کچھ ایجاد اول کی طرف اشارہ ہے اور سورۃ کہف میں ابقاء اول کی طرف اشارہ ہے بقولہ تعالٰی الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ الَّذِي أَنْزَلَ عَلَى عَبْدِهِ الْكِتَابَ وَلَمْ يَجْعَلْ لَهُ عِوَجًا کیونکہ نظام عالم اور نوع انسانی کی بقار فی الدنیا نبی علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام اور کتاب اللہ العزیز کے بسبب ہے ۔ اور چوتھی سورۃ جس کی افتتاح نجمی سے ہے وہ سورۃ سبا ہے اور پانچویں سورۃ ملائکہ جسے فاطر کہتے ہیں تو سبا میں ایجاد ثانی کی طرف اشارہ ہے بقولہ تعالی و قال الذین كفر والا تأتينا الساعة قل بلى وربي لتأتينكو الایۃ میں اثبات حشر اجساد ہے اور منکرین ساعۃ پر رد ہے اور سورۃ ملائکہ فاطر میں ابقاء ثانی کی طرف اشارہ ہے بقوله تعالى جاعل الملائكة رسلاً. فالمراد به على ما قيل اشارة الى تلقى الملئكة لاهل الجنة بالتسليم واستقبالهم بالتبجيل والتكريم الثالث الملاحظة لقوله تعالى والحمدالة قرآن مجید میں سورۃ قصص کے اندر له الحمد ہے وله الحمد واد کے ساتھ نہیں ہے ۔ اس وجہ ثالث کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ اس آیت کے لحاظ سے اولاً دار اولیٰ یعنی دار دنیا میں وہ مستحق حمد ہے بوجہ اس کے کہ دنیا میں اس کے کمال کی معرفت حجت قویہ کے ساتھ حاصل ہے اور اس کے نوال وعطا یا عباد تک پہنچ رہے ہیں اور ثانیا وہ مستحق محمد فی الاخرۃ ہے۔ علی ما شاهد انم یعنی اوپر اس نعمت کے کہ جو بصورۃ مشاہدہ کبریائیت کے ظاہر ہوگی اور جو ایسی نعمتوں کا مشاہدہ اور معائنہ ہو گا جو لا عين رأت ولا اذن سمعت و لا خطرت على قلب بشر داليه الى الى قوله وفي الآخرة على ما يشاهد من كبريائه - فان قلت قد وقع منشا سوال وجہ ثالث ہے کہ جب محمد علی الكبريا والنعماء فی الدارین ہوچکا تو پھر ولعنان الثناء الیہ ثانیا کی مراد کیا ہوگی کیونکہ تمام قسم کے حمد جو کہ شنار علی اللہ ہے یہ جب توجیہ ثالث کے لحاظ سے ہو چکے تو باقی کیا رہا ہے جس کے لئے لعنان الثناء الیہ ثانیاً کہا ۔ منشاء سوال وجہ اول نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ اس کے اندر حمد فی دار الآخرۃ کا تعرض نہیں ہے اور ثانی بھی نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ اس کے اندر حمد علی الکبریا کے ساتھ تعرض نہیں ہے۔ قلت خلاصہ جواب یہ ہے کہ اس سے مراد ہے باری تعالیٰ کی عظمت اور تعظیم کی قصد اور اس کی طرف قرب حاصل کرنے کی نیت اور ارادہ ان تمام اشیاء کے ساتھ جو اس تعظیم اور تقرب کے لئے صلاحیت رکھتی ہیں خواہ از قسم اقوال ہوں یا افعال جوارح اور قلب کے اور صرف اموال ان
The praise (hamd) can be upon His blessing and also upon other than blessing because in praise, receiving the blessing from the praised to the praiser is not a condition. So with 'awwalan' it is indicated that Allah Almighty is deserving of praise for His perfect essence and great attributes, and with 'thaniyan' for His beautiful blessings and abundant favors that reach the servants. The second aspect: The blessings of Allah, despite being numerous, return to creation and preservation firstly in the world and secondly in the Hereafter. The five surahs beginning with hamd are cited: al-Fatihah, al-An'am, al-Kahf, Saba', and al-Mala'ikah (Fatir). The third aspect: From the verse in Surah al-Qasas, it is understood that He is deserving of praise in the first abode (this world) due to knowledge of His perfection and in the Hereafter due to the witnessing of His majesty. Then a question: If all praise is already covered, what remains for 'thaniyan'? Answer: It refers to intending and seeking closeness to Allah through all things suitable for that, including words, actions of limbs and heart, and spending wealth.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'أولاً وثانياً' (firstly and secondly) from the opening of Al-Tawdih. The commentator presents three aspects (وجوه) of the praise (hamd) in 'الحمد لله'. The first aspect distinguishes between praise for Allah's perfect essence (كمال ذات) and praise for His blessings (نعم). The second aspect relates praise to the two realms: creation and preservation in this world and the Hereafter, illustrating with five Quranic surahs that begin with hamd (al-Fatihah, al-An'am, al-Kahf, Saba', al-Mala'ikah/Fatir). The third aspect is derived from Surah al-Qasas (28:70) where 'wa lahu al-hamd' indicates praise in this world (due to knowledge of His perfection) and in the Hereafter (due to witnessing His majesty). A question arises: if all praise is already covered by these aspects, what does the second 'thaniyan' add? The answer clarifies that it refers to the intention and pursuit of closeness to Allah through all suitable means—words, actions, and wealth. This is a typical scholarly explanation showing the depth of the opening phrase.

Key Terms
حمد (hamd): Praise of Allah, distinguished from thankfulness (shukr) in that it can be without receiving a blessing
أولاً وثانياً (awwalan wa thaniyan): Twofold division of hamd: firstly for Allah's perfect essence, secondly for His blessings

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first aspect, what distinguishes hamd from shukr?
A) Hamd requires a blessing; shukr does not.
B) Hamd can be without a blessing; shukr requires a blessing.
C) Both require a blessing, but hamd is general and shukr is specific.
D) Hamd is only for Allah; shukr can be for creatures.

Key Takeaway
Hamd includes praise for Allah's perfect essence and for His blessings; both are necessary for a comprehensive praise.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
The Second Aspect: Hamd Across the Two Realms and Five Surahs
Second interpretation linking hamd to the two realms with surah examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the second aspect links hamd to the two realms (this world and the Hereafter) and identify the five surahs that begin with hamd.

Core Idea
Hamd covers creation and preservation in both this world and the Hereafter, as illustrated by five Quranic surahs.

This lesson explores the second interpretation of 'awwalan wa thaniyan', which connects hamd to the two realms of existence. The commentator divides Allah's blessings into creation (ījād) and preservation (ibqā') in this world and the next, and shows how five Quranic surahs beginning with hamd highlight these aspects.

Guided Path
1
Understand the twofold scope
Recognize that 'awwalan' corresponds to this world (creation and preservation) and 'thaniyan' corresponds to the Hereafter (creation and preservation).
The commentator uses the terms 'ījād' (creation) and 'ibqā' (preservation) for each realm.
2
Identify the five surahs
List the surahs that begin with 'al-ḥamdu lillāh': al-Fātiḥa, al-An‘ām, al-Kahf, Saba’, and al-Malā’ika (Fāṭir).
These surahs are cited as examples of the opening with hamd.
3
Map surahs to the four categories
Assign each surah to one of the four categories: creation in this world (al-Fātiḥa: 'Rabb al-‘ālamīn'), preservation in this world (al-Kahf: sending down the Book), creation in the Hereafter (Saba’: resurrection), preservation in the Hereafter (al-Malā’ika: angels greeting the people of Paradise).
Al-Fātiḥa encompasses all four, so it is discussed separately.
4
Analyze al-Fātiḥa's comprehensive coverage
Note that al-Fātiḥa covers all aspects: 'Rabb al-‘ālamīn' (creation), 'al-Raḥmān al-Raḥīm' (preservation in this world), 'Mālik yawm al-dīn' (creation in the Hereafter), 'iyyāka na‘bud' (preservation in the Hereafter through worship).
This makes al-Fātiḥa the 'Umm al-Qur’ān'.

The praise (hamd) can be upon His blessing and also upon other than blessing because in praise, receiving the blessing from the praised to the praiser is not a condition. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'أولاً وثانياً' (firstly and secondly) from the opening of Al-Tawdih. The commentator presents three aspects (وجوه) of the praise (hamd) in 'الحمد لله'. The first aspect distinguishes between praise for Allah's perfect essence (كمال ذات) and praise for His blessings (نعم). The second aspect relates praise to the two realms: creation and preservation in this world and the Hereafter, illustrating with five Quranic surahs that begin with hamd (al-Fatihah, al-An'am, al-Kahf, Saba', al-Mala'ikah/Fatir). The third aspect is derived from Surah al-Qasas (28:70) where 'wa lahu al-hamd' indicates praise in this world (due to knowledge of His perfection) and in the Hereafter (due to witnessing His majesty). A question arises: if all praise is already covered by these aspects, what does the second 'thaniyan' add? The answer clarifies that it refers to the intention and pursuit of closeness to Allah through all suitable means—words, actions, and wealth. This is a typical scholarly explanation showing the depth of the opening phrase.

Key Terms
إيجاد (ījād): Creation, bringing into existence
إبقاء (ibqā’): Preservation, sustaining existence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which surah is described as covering all four categories (first creation, first preservation, second creation, second preservation)?
A) al-An‘ām
B) al-Fātiḥa
C) al-Kahf
D) Saba’

Key Takeaway
Hamd covers creation and preservation in both this world and the Hereafter, as exemplified by five Quranic surahs.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
9 min
The Third Aspect: Hamd in This World and the Hereafter and the Question of Redundancy
Third interpretation using al-Qasas, with a question-answer clarifying the role of intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the third aspect uses Surah al-Qasas to show hamd in both worlds, and evaluate the question-answer regarding the purpose of 'thaniyan'.

Core Idea
Hamd in this world is based on knowledge of Allah's perfection; in the Hereafter it is based on witnessing His majesty; and 'thaniyan' refers to the intention to seek closeness through all means.

This lesson covers the third and final interpretation of 'awwalan wa thaniyan'. The commentator cites Surah al-Qasas (28:70) to establish that hamd is due to Allah in this world (for knowledge of His perfection) and in the Hereafter (for witnessing His majesty). A question then arises: if all praise is covered, what does the second 'thaniyan' add? The answer reveals a deeper purpose—seeking closeness to Allah through intentions and actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scriptural basis
The commentator refers to the verse 'wa lahu al-ḥamdu fī al-ūlā wa al-ākhirati' (Surah al-Qasas 28:70) to prove that hamd is for both worlds.
This verse uses 'lahu al-ḥamdu' (for Him is praise) as a predicate, not a beginning.
2
Explain the two bases of hamd
In this world (al-ūlā), hamd is due because knowledge of Allah's perfection is attained through strong arguments. In the Hereafter, hamd is due because of witnessing His majesty directly.
Knowledge (ma‘rifa) vs. vision (mushāhada).
3
Formulate the question (source of wonder)
If all praise is already covered by the two bases (essence/blessings, or two realms), what remains for the second 'thaniyan' in the phrase 'ilayhi thaniyan'? The question arises from the third aspect, which seems to exhaust all praise.
This question is a deliberate scholarly inquiry (manasha’ al-su’al).
4
Understand the answer
The answer is that 'thaniyan' refers to the intention (qaṣd) and desire (irāda) to seek closeness to Allah through all means—words, actions of limbs and heart, and spending wealth. This goes beyond mere verbal praise.
This expands hamd from mere utterance to encompass all acts of worship and devotion.

The praise (hamd) can be upon His blessing and also upon other than blessing because in praise, receiving the blessing from the praised to the praiser is not a condition. So with 'awwalan' it is indicated that Allah Almighty is deserving of praise for His perfect essence and great attributes, and with 'thaniyan' for His beautiful blessings and abundant favors that reach the servants. The second aspect: The blessings of Allah, despite being numerous, return to creation and preservation firstly in the world and secondly in the Hereafter. The five surahs beginning with hamd are cited: al-Fatihah, al-An'am, al-Kahf, Saba', and al-Mala'ikah (Fatir). The third aspect: From the verse in Surah al-Qasas, it is understood that He is deserving of praise in the first abode (this world) due to knowledge of His perfection and in the Hereafter due to the witnessing of His majesty. Then a question: If all praise is already covered, what remains for 'thaniyan'? Answer: It refers to intending and seeking closeness to Allah through all things suitable for that, including words, actions of limbs and heart, and spending wealth.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'أولاً وثانياً' (firstly and secondly) from the opening of Al-Tawdih. The commentator presents three aspects (وجوه) of the praise (hamd) in 'الحمد لله'. The first aspect distinguishes between praise for Allah's perfect essence (كمال ذات) and praise for His blessings (نعم). The second aspect relates praise to the two realms: creation and preservation in this world and the Hereafter, illustrating with five Quranic surahs that begin with hamd (al-Fatihah, al-An'am, al-Kahf, Saba', al-Mala'ikah/Fatir). The third aspect is derived from Surah al-Qasas (28:70) where 'wa lahu al-hamd' indicates praise in this world (due to knowledge of His perfection) and in the Hereafter (due to witnessing His majesty). A question arises: if all praise is already covered by these aspects, what does the second 'thaniyan' add? The answer clarifies that it refers to the intention and pursuit of closeness to Allah through all suitable means—words, actions, and wealth. This is a typical scholarly explanation showing the depth of the opening phrase.

Key Terms
منشأ السؤال (manasha’ al-su’al): The source of the question; a scholarly inquiry that arises when a seeming gap or redundancy is perceived.
قصد التقرب (qaṣd al-taqarrub): Intention to seek closeness to Allah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The third aspect reveals that hamd is not only verbal but includes the intention to glorify Allah and seek His closeness through all actions, words, and wealth.

Introduction and Front Matter

Understanding the Analogy of Mujalli and Musalli in Salawat
Introductory analogy for the hierarchy of salawat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the analogy of mujalli and musalli and distinguish the primary and secondary nature of salawat upon the Prophet and his family.

Core Idea
Blessings upon the Prophet are primary like the leading horse; blessings upon his family are secondary like the following horse.

This passage uses a vivid analogy from horse racing to explain the hierarchy of salawat (blessings) in Islamic tradition. The commentator clarifies that 'mujalli' refers to the lead horse and 'musalli' to the horse that follows closely, representing the primary and secondary objects of blessings. Understanding this analogy helps us appreciate the Hanafi emphasis in prayers and invocations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two terms
Locate 'mujalli' and 'musalli' in the passage. Note that they are originally terms for racehorses.
The roots: j-l-w (to appear first) and s-l-w (to follow close behind).
2
Understand the literal meaning
The passage explains that 'musalli' is a horse that stays level with the forelock of the preceding horse – i.e., it follows just behind the leader 'mujalli'.
3
Apply the analogy to salawat
The author then transfers this to blessings: 'mujalli' represents salawat directly upon the Prophet (primary), while 'musalli' represents salawat upon his family (secondary/intrinsic).
This aligns with the Hanafi practice of sending blessings in tashahhud: 'Allahumma salli ala Muhammad wa ala ali Muhammad'.
4
Recognize the purpose
Understand that the analogy emphasizes priority and proper order – blessings upon the Prophet himself are direct and essential, while blessings upon his family are implicit and follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ای صلوی المجلی اور صلوین سرینوں کو کہتے ہیں یعنی مصلی اس گھوڑے کو کہتے ہیں جس کار میں سابق گھوڑے کے ٹرینوں کے برابر رہے و معنی ذرات یعنی میدان صلوات میں مجلی اور مصلی ہونے سے مراد صرف تکثیر صلوات ہے یا مجلی کے ساتھ صلواۃ علی النبی علیہ السلام کی طرف اور مصلی کے ساتھ صلواۃ علی الآل والاصحاب کی طرف اشارہ ہے چونکہ صلواۃ علی النبي علیہ السلام قصدا اور اولاد بالذات ہوتی ہے لہذا وہ بدرجہ مجلی کے ہوگی اور آل پر ضمناً و تبعا اور بالعرض ہوتی ہے لہذا وہ ثانی درجہ پر ہو کر ہم رتبہ مصلی ہو گی۔
It is said: 'Mujalli' in salawat and 'sallawin' means manes – i.e., 'musalli' refers to a horse that remains level with the forelock of the preceding horse. And the meaning of 'dharrat' is: in the field of salawat, the meaning of being 'mujalli' and 'musalli' is either merely the multiplication of salawat, or with 'mujalli' it indicates salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), and with 'musalli' it indicates salawat upon the family and companions. Since salawat upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) is primary and essential, it is at the level of 'mujalli'; and upon the family it is implicitly and secondarily, so it is at the second level, equal to 'musalli'.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a definition and analogy from the author's introduction. The commentator explains the terms 'mujalli' and 'musalli', which are terms for horses: the 'mujalli' is the first horse, and the 'musalli' is the second horse that follows close behind. In the context of sending blessings (salawat), the author uses this analogy to distinguish between blessings upon the Prophet himself (which are primary and direct, like the leading horse) and blessings upon his family and companions (which are secondary and indirect, like the following horse). This rhetorical device emphasizes the proper order and relative merit.

Key Terms
مجلی (mujalli): The first horse in a race, used as analogy for primary salawat upon the Prophet.
مصلی (musalli): The second horse in a race, used as analogy for secondary salawat upon the family.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, salawat upon the family (al wa al-ashab) is described as:
A) Primary and direct
B) Secondary and implicit
C) Of equal status to salawat upon the Prophet
D) Optional and not required

Key Takeaway
The analogy of mujalli (lead horse) and musalli (following horse) teaches that blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad take priority and are primary, while blessings upon his family follow as secondary but are still included.

Introduction and Front Matter

Tajnis (Paronomasia) in Classical Text Introductions
Identifies and explains the rhetorical device of tajnis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify tajnis in Arabic texts and explain its rhetorical effect using the examples from this passage.

Core Idea
Tajnis uses identical script for words with distinct meanings, adding elegance.

This passage reveals how classical scholars often employ literary devices in their opening praises. Understanding tajnis helps you appreciate the linguistic artistry and avoid misinterpretation of homographic terms.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of tajnis
Tajnis (paronomasia) occurs when two words are identical in form (script) but differ in meaning. This is a common rhetorical device used to add elegance and depth.
2
Identify the two pairs of words in the passage
The passage gives examples: 'thaniyan' appears twice in the hamd phrases, and 'musalliyan' appears twice in the salawat phrases.
3
Differentiate the meanings of each occurrence
For 'thaniyan': the first means 'second time', the second means 'one who turns the horse's rein'. For 'musalliyan': the first means 'one who sends blessings', the second means 'a horse that comes second in a race'.
4
Appreciate the rhetorical function
Tajnis adds beauty and invites the reader to reflect on the layered meanings. In a legal text, recognizing tajnis prevents confusion when the same word form carries different senses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثولا يخفى حسن ما فی قرائن یعنی حمد و صلواۃ کے فقروں میں جو تجنیس موجود ہے اس کا حسن مخفی نہیں ہے بلکہ حسن ظاہر ہے تجنیس اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ دو لفظ ایسے اطلاق کئے جائیں جو صورة مجانس ہوں اور معنی مختلف جیسے حمد کے فقرات میں لفظ ثانیا دو مرتبہ مذکور ہے پہلے کا معنی دوسری بار کا ہے اور دوسرا بمعنی صارفاًا یعنی شاہ کی باگ کو موڑنے والا اور اسی طرح صلوۃ کے فقرات اور قرائن میں بھی بجنیس موجود ہے کہ لفظ مصلیا دوبار مذکور ہے پہلا بمعنی صلوٰۃ و درود بھیجنے کے معنی میں ہے اور دوسرے سے مراد وہ فرس ہے جو ثانی مرتبہ میں رہتا ہے دوڑ کے میدان میں۔
Second, the beauty of what is in the 'qara'in' [indicators] is not hidden, meaning the tajnis present in the phrases of hamd and salawat is not hidden; rather its beauty is apparent. Tajnis is when two words are used that are similar in form but different in meaning. For example, in the phrases of hamd, the word 'thaniyan' is mentioned twice: the first means 'second time', and the second means 'turning away' i.e., one who turns the horse's rein. Similarly, in the phrases of salawat and the qara'in, there is also tajnis: the word 'musalliyan' is mentioned twice; the first means 'sending salawat and blessings', and the second refers to the horse that stays in the second place in the racecourse.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage explains the rhetorical device of tajnis (paronomasia) used in the author's introductory lines. The commentator notes that in the praise (hamd) and blessings (salawat) sentences, there is tajnis, which adds elegance. He gives examples: 'thaniyan' appears twice – once meaning 'second' and once meaning 'one who turns the reins' (a metaphor for directing). Also 'musalliyan' appears twice – once meaning 'one who sends salawat' and once meaning 'a horse that is second in a race'. This is a classic example of complete tajnis where two words are written identically but have different meanings.

Key Terms
تجنیس (tajnis): A rhetorical device where two words are similar in form but different in meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two words with similar form but different meanings
C) A metaphor for horse racing
D) Repeating the same word for emphasis

Key Takeaway
Tajnis is a rhetorical device where identical words have different meanings, used here to add elegance to the author's praise.

Three Types of Isti'ara in the Second Qarina
Analyzes types of metaphors in the second qarina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish isti'ara bi'l-kinaayah, takhyiliyyah, and tarshiihiyyah in a given analogy from a Hanafi legal text.

Core Idea
In the second qarina, praise is implicitly likened to a horse, and its attributes are assigned to reveal three metaphor types.

The commentator unpacks the layered metaphors in the author's phrase. Understanding these isti'ara types is crucial for usul al-fiqh because metaphors carry legal implications—misreading a metaphor can alter the derivation of a ruling. This lesson will guide you through the commentator's analysis so you can apply the same rhetorical toolkit to other passages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the implicit simile
Find the two elements being compared: the mushabbah (the thing described) and the mushabbah bihi (the thing it is likened to). In this passage, praise (thana') is implicitly likened to a spirited horse (faras dhi 'inan).
This is the foundation of isti'ara bi'l-kinaayah.
2
Distinguish necessary vs. suitable attributes
Determine whether the attribute ascribed to the mushabbah is a necessary property (lazim) of the mushabbah bihi or merely a fitting/proper attribute (munasib). The rein ('inan) is necessary for a horse; reaching the objective (isal ila al-maqsud) is a suitable attribute.
Lazim leads to takhyiliyyah; munasib leads to tarshiihiyyah.
3
Classify each metaphor
Based on the above, assign each as: takhyiliyyah (necessary attribute ascribed) or tarshiihiyyah (suitable attribute ascribed). The implicit comparison itself is isti'ara bi'l-kinaayah.
All three appear in the same phrase, layered together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما في القرينة الثانية المقرينه ثانيه يعني ولقان الثناء الیہ ثانیا میں جو استعارات ہیں ان کا حسن بھی مخفی نہیں ہے اس عبارت میں استعارہ بالکنا جسے استعارہ مکنیہ کہتے ہیں موجود ہے اور اسی طرح استعارہ تخیلیہ اور ترشیحیہ بھی مذکور ہے جب صرف مشبہ کا ذکر کیا جائے اور تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہوا سے استعارہ بالکنا یہ کہتے ہیں اور اس تشبیہ مضمر پر بطور قرینہ والہ کے لازم مشبہ بہ کو مشبہ کے لئے ثابت کیا جاتا ہے یہ استعارہ تخیلیہ ہوتا ہے اور اگر ملائمات و مناسبات مشبہ بہ کو مشبہ کے لئے ثابت کیا جائے تو یہ استعارہ ترشیحیہ ہوتا ہے تو اس فقرہ ثانیہ میں ثناء کو فرس ذی عنان کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی گئی ہے جو مضمر فی النفس ہے یہ استعارہ بالکنایہ ہے اور وجہ تشبیہ ایصال الی المقصود ہے اور ذی عنان کے لئے عنان لازم ہے جو ولعنان الثناء میں ثنا کے لئے ثابت کی گئی ہے یہ تخییلیہ ہے اور صرف الی المقصود یہ ملائمات مشبہ بہ سے ہے جو بقولہ ثانیاً ثابت للثناء ہے یہ تر شیمیہ ہے۔
And what is in the second qarina – i.e., the second indicator – meaning in the phrase 'wa laqan al-thana' ilayhi thaniyan', the metaphors in it are not hidden. In this phrase, isti'ara bi'l-kinaayah, which is called isti'ara makniyyah, is present, and similarly isti'ara takhyiliyyah and tarshiihiyyah are mentioned. When only the mushabbah is mentioned and the simile is implicit in the mind, it is called isti'ara bi'l-kinaayah. And on this implicit simile, by way of a qarina indicating the lazim of the mushabbah bihi being established for the mushabbah, this is isti'ara takhyiliyyah. And if the muwaafiqat and munasabaat of the mushabbah bihi are established for the mushabbah, then it is isti'ara tarshiihiyyah. So in this second sentence, 'thana' (praise) is likened to a spirited horse, which is implicit – this is isti'ara bi'l-kinaayah. The point of similarity is 'reaching the objective'. And for the spirited horse, the rein is necessary, which is established for 'thana' in 'wa 'inan al-thana' – this is takhyiliyyah. And 'attaining the objective' is from the fittings of the mushabbah bihi, which is established for 'thana' by his saying 'thaniyan' – this is tarshiihiyyah.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage analyzes the metaphorical language in the second qarina (clue) of the author's introduction. The commentator identifies three types of isti'ara (metaphor) based on the way the simile is presented. First, isti'ara bi'l-kinaayah (implicit metaphor) where only the thing being compared is mentioned, and the comparison is in the mind. Here, praise (thana') is implicitly compared to a horse. Second, isti'ara takhyiliyyah where a necessary attribute of the compared-to thing (the horse's rein) is ascribed to the thing compared (praise), as in 'rein of praise'. Third, isti'ara tarshiihiyyah where suitable attributes of the compared-to thing (attaining the objective) are ascribed. This shows the commentator's deep rhetorical analysis of the text.

Key Terms
استعارہ بالکنایہ (isti'ara bi'l-kinaayah): A metaphor where only the mushabbah is mentioned and the comparison is implicit.
استعارہ تخیلیہ (isti'ara takhyiliyyah): A metaphor where a necessary attribute of the mushabbah bihi is ascribed to the mushabbah.
استعارہ ترشیحیہ (isti'ara tarshiihiyyah): A metaphor where suitable/fitting attributes of the mushabbah bihi are ascribed to the mushabbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of metaphor arises when a necessary attribute (lazim) of the mushabbah bihi is ascribed to the mushabbah?
A) Isti'ara bi'l-kinaayah
B) Isti'ara takhyiliyyah
C) Isti'ara tarshiihiyyah
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
The second qarina exemplifies three types of isti'ara, each serving a different rhetorical function that affects how legal analogies are interpreted.

Tamthil: The Compound Simile as a Qarina in Usul al-Fiqh
Defines tamthil and illustrates it with the author's allegory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tamthil, identify its components, and explain its use in the author's introduction.

Core Idea
Tamthil is a compound simile that compares abstract forms derived from multiple elements, not single objects.

In classical usul texts, authors often use rhetorical figures to clarify legal concepts. One such figure is tamthil, a compound simile where a whole situation is likened to another. This lesson unpacks the definition of tamthil as explained in the commentary on the fourth qarina of the author's preface, and shows how it functions as a conceptual indicator.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of tamthil
Tamthil is defined as extracting an abstract form (hay'ah intiza'iyyah) from multiple mixed things and comparing it to another abstract form derived from other mixed things.
It is not a simple simile but a compound one involving multiple elements.
2
Analyze the example in the passage
The author compares the situation of people sending salawat (some ahead, some behind) to a horse race (some leading, some second, some behind). Both situations are abstract forms derived from multiple elements (different ranks of doers, different positions of horses).
This shows how tamthil works as an allegory.
3
Identify the structure of tamthil
Tamthil requires two abstract forms, each composed of multiple mixed things. The comparison is between these forms, not between individual objects.
This distinguishes tamthil from simple tashbih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما في الرابعة من التمثيل تمثیل اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ چند ملی جلی اشیاء سے ایک ہمیئہ انتزاعیہ منتزع کر کے اس کو تشبیہ دی جائے دوسری ہیئہ منتزعہ کے ساتھ جو وہ بھی چند اشیاء ملی جلی سے ماخوذ ہو تو یہاں فقرہ رابعہ میں ایسے ہے کہ مقام صلوۃ میں مصنف اور دیگر مصلین جو صلواۃ علی الرسول میں سعی بلیغ کر رہے ہیں اور ان میں ان کے مراتب مختلف ہیں کوئی سابق ہے کوئی مسبوق اس سے جو ہیکہ من ہے اس کو تشبیہ دی گئی ہے اس ہیئتہ منتزعہ کے ساتھ جو ماخوذ ہے اس میدان مسابقت سے جس میں مختلف گھوڑے دوڑ رہے ہیں کوئی مجلی ہے اور کوئی مصلی اور کچھ اس سے پیچھے بھی ہوں گے اسی طرح مصنف نے اپنے آپ کو مجلی اور مصلی قرار دیا اور دوسروں کو مسبوق یہ ہے تمثیل جس کو تشبیہ مرکب اور مؤلف بھی کہتے ہیں۔
And what is in the fourth [qarina] of tamthil. Tamthil is called when from several mixed things an abstract form is extracted and then likened to another abstract form, which is also taken from several mixed things. Here, in the fourth sentence, it is like this: in the place of salawat, the author and other prayer-offerers who are making utmost effort in sending salawat upon the Messenger, and among them their ranks are different – some are ahead, some are behind. This is likened to that abstract form which is taken from the racecourse where various horses are running – some are mujalli, some are musalli, and some are behind them. Similarly, the author has placed himself as mujalli and musalli and others as masbuq. This is tamthil, which is also called compound or composite simile.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage explains tamthil (allegory or compound simile) found in the fourth qarina of the author's introduction. Tamthil is a complex figure of speech where a whole scene or situation is compared to another scene, not just a single object. Here, the situation of the author and others sending salawat is compared to a horse race: some are ahead (mujalli), some second (musalli), and some behind (masbuq). This allegory illustrates the different levels of effort and precedence in sending blessings upon the Prophet. The commentator elaborates that the author thus places himself as the leading horse and others as followers, which is a form of conceptual metaphor.

Key Terms
تمثیل (tamthil): An allegory or compound simile where an abstract form derived from several things is likened to another abstract form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) A compound metaphor derived from multiple elements
C) A type of horse race
D) A rhetorical question

Key Takeaway
Tamthil is a compound simile that serves as a conceptual indicator in usul, comparing abstract forms derived from multiple elements.

Tanwin on 'Awwalan': Adverbial vs. Adjectival Use
Explains why 'awwalan' takes tanwin when used adverbially

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when 'awwal' takes tanwin (munsarif) and when it does not (ghayr munsarif), and explain the grammatical reasoning using the example from Arabic usul al-fiqh texts.

Core Idea
'Awwalan' takes tanwin because it is an adverb meaning 'before', not a superlative adjective.

This passage addresses a grammatical objection about the word 'awwalan'. In usul al-fiqh, precise understanding of Arabic grammar is essential for interpreting legal texts. Here, the commentator explains why 'awwalan' can accept tanwin even though 'awwal' is normally non-declinable, by distinguishing its adverbial use from its adjectival use.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Read the objection: 'awwal' is an ism tafdil (superlative), which is normally ghayr munsarif (no tanwin). So why does 'awwalan' have tanwin?
This is a common grammatical puzzle.
2
Recognize the answer
The answer: when 'awwal' is used as an adverb (zarf) meaning 'before', it is not functioning as an adjective, so it becomes munsarif and takes tanwin.
The key is the adverbial vs. adjectival function.
3
Analyze the example
Consider the phrase 'laqaytuhu 'aam awwalan'. Here 'awwalan' means 'in a prior year' (indefinite time). If it were adjectival, it would be 'laqaytuhu 'aam awwalu' meaning 'the first year of this set' (specific).
The tanwin signals the adverbial use.
4
Connect to usul al-fiqh
In legal texts, misidentifying the grammatical function can change the meaning. For example, in a hadith, 'awwalan' could indicate a general prior time rather than a specific first instance.
This affects how we derive rulings (istinbat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان انتصاب اولا وثانياً یعنی اولاً و ثانیا اس مقام پر منصوب على الظرفیہ ہیں یعنی فی الاوقات الاولية والثانوية - واما التنوين في اولاً یہ جواب ہے اس اشکال کا کہ لفظ اول اسم تفضیل ہے جیسے کہ شارح نے اس کے نظائر سے استدلال کیا ہے تو اس وقت لفظ اول میں وصفیہ اور وزن فعل موجود ہے تو غیر منصرف ہوگا تو اس پر تنوین کا لانا کیسے صحیح ہو سکتا ہے تو اس کا جواب دیتے ہوئے کہا لانه ظرف یعنی یہ وصفیہ کے معنی میں نہیں بلکہ بطور ظرفیہ کے مذکو ہے جو بمعنی قبل کے ہے یہی مراد ہے صحاح کی کہ جب اس کو بطور وصفیہ کے استعمال کیا جائے تو اس کو غیر منصرف کیا جائے گا اور کہا جائے گا لقیتہ عاما اول اور جب اس کو صفہ قرار نہ دیا جائے بلکہ ظرفیہ کے طور پر استعمال ہو تو منصرف ہو گا اور کہا جائے گا لقیتہ عاما اولاً بالتنوین پہلی صورت میں اس کا معنی ہوگا اول من ہذا العام یعنی اس سال کی بنسبت جو پہلا ہے اور ثانی صورت میں معنیٰ ہوگا قبل ہذا العام یعنی اس سال سے سابقہ مدت میں مثلاً اس وقت سال چودہ سو آٹھ ہجری ہے تو پہلی صورت کے لحاظ سے اول من هذا العام مراد ہو گا یعنی صرف چودہ سو سات ہجری اور ثانی صورت میں قبل هذا العام یعنی اس سال سے پہلے والے برس خواہ وہ سات ہو یا چھ ہو یا پاسخ و چار جو اس سابقہ مدت میں گزر چکے ہیں تعیین نہیں ہے ۔
And that 'awwalan' and 'thaniyan' are accusative as adverbs of time – i.e., 'in the first and second times'. As for the tanwin on 'awwalan', this is the answer to an objection: that the word 'awwal' is a superlative noun (ism tafdil) as the commentator argued from its parallels, so it would have adjectival quality and the verb pattern, thus it would be non-declinable (ghayr munsarif). So how can tanwin be correct? The answer: because it is an adverb (zarf), i.e., it is not in the adjectival meaning but used adverbially, meaning 'before'. This is the meaning from al-Sihah: when it is used adjectivally, it is made non-declinable, and one says 'laqaytuhu 'aam awwalu' (plural?). And when it is not made an adjective but used adverbially, it becomes declinable and one says 'laqaytuhu 'aam awwalan' with tanwin. In the first case, its meaning is 'the first of this year' – i.e., relative to this year, the first. In the second case, its meaning is 'before this year' – i.e., a prior period to this year. For example, when the current year is 1408 AH, in the first way, it means only 1407 AH, and in the second way, it means the years before this year – whether 7, 6, 5, 4, etc., that have passed in the prior period – no specific year is determined.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage deals with a grammatical objection regarding the word 'awwalan' (first). The objection is that 'awwal' is an ism tafdil (superlative), which normally is ghayr munsarif (does not accept tanwin), so why does it have tanwin? The commentator answers that when used as an adverb (zarf) meaning 'before', it is not functioning as an adjective, so it becomes munsarif and takes tanwin. He illustrates with the example 'laqaytuhu 'aam awwalan' (I met him a year first) meaning in a prior year. This distinguishes between the adjectival use (specific first within a set) and the adverbial use (indefinite prior time).

Key Terms
اول (awwal): When used as an adverb (ظرف), it means 'before' and is munsarif; when used as a superlative adjective, it means 'the first' and is ghayr munsarif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is a proper noun
B) Because it is used adverbially, not adjectivally
C) Because it is a superlative
D) Because it is a verb

Key Takeaway
The tanwin on 'awwalan' indicates its adverbial function meaning 'before', distinguishing it from the adjectival 'awwal' which is non-declinable.

Iham (Double Entendre) in 'Sa'da Jaddahu'
Explains the rhetorical device of iham in the phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify instances of iham in Arabic phrases and distinguish between the near and far meanings.

Core Idea
Iham uses a word's two meanings—near and far—to hint at the far one.

Rhetorical devices like iham (double entendre) are not mere literary flourishes; they can affect how we interpret legal texts. In this lesson, we examine the phrase 'Sa'da Jaddahu' where the word 'jadd' carries two distinct meanings. Understanding which meaning is intended is crucial for accurate comprehension in fiqh and usul contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term with dual meanings
Locate the word that has more than one lexical meaning. In 'sa'da jaddahu', it is 'jadd'.
2
List the two possible meanings
Determine the near (aqrab) and far (ab' ad) meanings. Here, 'jadd' can mean grandfather (near) or luck (far).
The near meaning is more common; the far is less obvious.
3
Determine the intended meaning from context
Based on the overall phrase or context, decide which meaning is intended. The commentator states that here 'jadd' means luck.
Context often involves other words in the sentence or the author's purpose.
4
Recognize the iham effect
Iham occurs when the author deliberately uses a word with two meanings, allowing the reader to momentarily consider the near meaning before realizing the far one is intended.
This adds subtlety and can emphasize a point.
5
Apply awareness in usul al-fiqh
In legal texts, iham can cause interpretive ambiguity. A Hanafi usuli must be alert to such devices to avoid misreading a ruling.
For example, if a hadith uses a word with iham, the correct meaning must be determined before applying it as a dalil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سعد جدہ فیه ایهام فن بدیع میں ایہام اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ ایسا لفظ ذکر کیا جائے جس کے دو معنی ہوں ایک قریب اور دوسرا بعید اور مراد بعید ہو تو کہا جاتا ہے کہ جد کا معنی ابو الاب قریبی ہے اور بخت بعیدی اور یہاں بمعنی بخت ہے کیونکہ
'Sa'da jaddahu' – in it is iham. In the art of rhetoric, iham is when a word is mentioned that has two meanings, one near and one far, and the far meaning is intended. So it is said that 'jadd' means grandfather (near) and luck/bakt (far), and here it means luck because...
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage explains the rhetorical figure of iham (double entendre) in the phrase 'sa'da jaddahu'. Iham is using a word that has two meanings: one straightforward (near) and one less obvious (far), but the speaker intends the far one. Here, 'jadd' could mean 'grandfather' (aqrab) or 'fortune/luck' (ab'ad). The commentator states that in this context, the intended meaning is 'luck', not 'grandfather'. This is a typical example of iham in Arabic rhetoric, often used for subtlety and wordplay.

Key Terms
ایہام (iham): A rhetorical device where a word with two meanings is used, and the distant meaning is intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the phrase 'sa'da jaddahu', what is the far (intended) meaning of 'jadd'?
A) Grandfather
B) Luck
C) Severity
D) New

Key Takeaway
Iham is a rhetorical device where a word's far meaning is intended, requiring careful context analysis to avoid misinterpretation.
