Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
The Superiority of Usul al-Fiqh and Its Four Pillars
Introduction to usul al-fiqh and its four foundational pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define usul al-shariah and explain its four foundational pillars and their superiority over fiqh and kalam.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh is the science of universal evidences — its four pillars are the Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.

This lesson introduces the discipline of usul al-fiqh and its foundational sources. The author begins by praising Allah for granting the science of usul a noble status. We will explore why usul is superior to fiqh and kalam, and understand the metaphor of the castle of rulings built on four pillars. By grasping these foundational concepts, you will appreciate how all fiqh rulings are derived from these universal evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of praise
The author praises Allah for the science of usul. Why is this science singled out? It indicates the great status of usul al-fiqh among other sciences.
The commentator explains that the specification of this blessing highlights the nobility of the subject matter.
2
Define usul al-shariah
Usul al-shariah are the universal evidences (al-adillah al-kulliyyah): the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, Ijma, and Qiyas.
These are the four agreed-upon sources in Hanafi usul.
3
Understand the metaphor of the castle
The shariah rulings are likened to a castle (qasr) that provides protection from spiritual harm, just as a castle protects from physical dangers.
This metaphor emphasizes the protective function of following the rulings.
4
List the four pillars
The author lists the four pillars in order: first the Book, then the Sunnah, then Ijma, then acting upon Qiyas.
This order reflects the hierarchical priority in legal reasoning.
5
Differentiate usul from fiqh and kalam
Usul al-fiqh discusses the universal evidences and their conditions, fiqh deals with detailed rulings, and kalam provides the foundation for proving the sources.
Usul is considered superior to fiqh and kalam because all fiqh rulings depend on it, and usul itself depends on kalam for establishing the sources.

He attached praises and made them dependent upon this matter that Allah has made the foundations of the Shariah (usul al-shariah) a solid foundation and the branches of the Shariah (furu al-shariah) delicate of edges and subtle of meanings. And these are not some of the blessings of Allah, yet praises are a comprehensive plural that should be attached to all bounties. So why the specification of some bounties? The commentator, presenting its reason, said: an indication to the greatness of the science, i.e., this is a specification of the scientific bounty, aiming to indicate the greatness of status and noble worth of this science in which this composition lies. 'And Shariah includes fiqh' meaning by Shariah is meant the general meaning which includes fiqh, and besides them includes usuli issues that are established by transmitted evidences, such as the issue of seeing Allah, the Hereafter, and the authority of Ijma and Qiyas. And by 'usul al-shariah' is meant the universal evidences, i.e., the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, Ijma, and Qiyas, and their foundations are the science of Tawhid, attributes, and prophecies, i.e., the science of Kalam which discusses these matters. Since the establishment of the Book and Sunnah depends on these issues of Kalam, these issues are a foundation for usul al-fiqh. 'Tamhid' means preparation, and their rectification according to the truth, i.e., Allah made the foundations of Shariah well-established and upon the correct way and in accordance with truth, He placed and rectified them. This is the meaning of 'tamhid al-mabani'. 'And their branches (furu'uha)' i.e., the branches of Shariah, meaning detailed rulings which are explained in fiqh. Since Shariah was taken in the general meaning that includes fiqh, therefore the addition of 'branches' to 'Shariah' is the addition of the part to the whole, and the addition of 'usul' to 'Shariah' is the addition of the evidence to the proven. In 'daqiqat al-ma'ani', 'ma'ani' refer to detailed partial causes (ilal) that are presented in fiqh for every issue, and those causes are subtle; not every person can easily reach them, rather their derivation is the work of a mujtahid. And all these things are blessings from Allah deserving of praise. Because Shariah is a blessing by which the system of the world remains established and correct, and in the Hereafter reward depends on it. And due to the subtlety of meanings, the ranks of scholars become high, and they obtain reward from Allah. From this speech it becomes known that the science of Usul holds a superior rank over the science of Fiqh, because the knowledge of detailed fiqhi rulings from detailed evidences (which are fiqhi issues) depends on the knowledge of the conditions of universal evidences that Usul discusses. And this science of Usul, since it depends on the knowledge of Allah and His attributes, and likewise on the knowledge of the truthfulness of the messenger by evidence of miracles which Kalam discusses, therefore Usul has a loftier rank than Kalam. And Kalam is the science that discusses the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, the Hereafter, etc., upon the way of the Islamic law on the method of divine philosophy. 'It is built upon four pillars.' This sentence is like a substitute of inclusion for the previous sentence, because the previous sentence is superior in showing the greatness and nobility of the science, just as a substitute of inclusion clarifies the intended meaning relative to the substituted, but it is not a true substitute. The summary of this sentence is that Allah has built the castle of rulings upon four pillars, and strengthened it with muhkam verses, and confined the mutashabih verses within the tents of curtains so that the firmly rooted scholars may be tested, as is the chosen view of the Hanafis that the stop is upon 'and none knows its interpretation except Allah'. The firmly rooted scholars must restrain their minds and abandon striving to reach the beloved and desirable occupation of esoteric knowledge. Allah has not informed anyone of the mutashabih. This is the elucidation of the text. Now turn to the commentary. 'He likened the shariah rulings' meaning the author likened the shariah rulings to a castle. Just as in a castle, one obtains protection from heat and cold and security from the dangers of enemies by entering the fortress, similarly by resorting to these shariah rulings one obtains protection from the destructive things of religion, i.e., Satan, and protection from the heat and cold of Hellfire by acting upon these rulin A castle's need for pillars: here the author is establishing the need of the castle of rulings for four pillars, i.e., even though the detailed evidences of shariah rulings are numerous, they all refer to four pillars that are the pillars of the castle of rulings. The purpose is to establish the need for these four pillars. Just as a spatial castle is in need of pillars, even though the pillars are internal parts of the spatial castle, but in the castle of rulings these four pillars are not internal, yet the need for them is like the need of the whole for the part. 'Then he mentioned in the midst of speech' the author mentioned these four pillars in the same order as the Lawgiver established the rulings upon them: first the Book, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then acting upon Qiyas.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening of a usul al-fiqh work, explaining the author's praise and the superiority of usul al-fiqh over fiqh and kalam. The commentator clarifies that the specification of the blessing of this science indicates its great status. He defines usul al-shariah as the universal evidences (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and explains that their foundation is the science of kalam. The passage then discusses the four pillars (arkan) upon which the shariah rulings (qasr al-ahkam) are built, likening rulings to a fortress that provides protection. The commentator also touches on the Hanafi position regarding the interpretation of mutashabih verses, stating that only Allah knows their interpretation. The author then lists the four sources in the order of priority: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, then Qiyas. This passage establishes the framework for usul al-fiqh as the science that derives rulings from these four foundations.

Key Terms
اصول الشریعت (usul al-shariah): The universal evidences (al-adillah al-kulliyyah) of the Shariah, i.e., the Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
فروع الشریعت (furu al-shariah): The detailed rulings (ahkam tafsiliyyah) derived from the universal evidences, discussed in fiqh.
قصر الاحکام (qasr al-ahkam): A metaphor likening the shariah rulings to a castle (qasr) that provides protection and is built upon pillars.
اربعہ ارکان (arba' arkan): The four foundational pillars of the shariah rulings: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many foundational pillars (arkan) are mentioned upon which the shariah rulings are based?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of the four universal evidences—the Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas—which provide the foundation for all fiqh rulings.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
The Four Pillars in Detail: Order and Function
Detailed explanation of the four pillars and their priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the priority order of the four pillars and the Hanafi position on the interpretation of mutashabih verses.

Core Idea
The four pillars are ranked: Book, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas — a hierarchy that guides legal derivation.

In this lesson, we delve deeper into the four pillars themselves. The author lists them in a specific order, reflecting their priority in legal reasoning. We also explore the Hanafi view that mutashabih verses are known only to Allah, reinforcing the primacy of clear texts. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Recall the four pillars
The four universal evidences are Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas. They form the foundations of all shariah rulings.
The passage uses the metaphor of a castle to illustrate their foundational role.
2
Observe the order of listing
The author explicitly mentions them in the order: first the Book, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then acting upon Qiyas.
This order is deliberate and reflects the hierarchy of strength and priority in evidence.
3
Understand the priority in derivation
A jurist must exhaust higher sources before resorting to lower ones. The Book is the highest, followed by Sunnah, then Ijma, then Qiyas.
This ensures that rulings are based on the most authoritative evidence.
4
Examine the Hanafi view on mutashabih
The passage states the chosen Hanafi view that the interpretation of mutashabih verses is known only to Allah; scholars should refrain from speculation.
This reinforces reliance on clear (muhkam) texts for legal rulings.

تخصیص ہے اس کے ساتھ اس علم کی عظمت شان اور حلالہ قدر کی طرف اشارہ کر نا مطلوب ہے جس میں یہ تصنیف واقع ہے۔ والشريعة تعمر الفقہ یعنی شریعت سے مراد عمومی معنیٰ ہے جو فقہ کو بھی شامل ہے اور انہیں کے علاوہ ان اصولی مسائل کو بھی جو ادلہ سمعیہ سے ثابت ہیں جیسے مسئلہ رویہ باری تعالیٰ و معاد و اجماع و قیاس کا حجت ہونا۔ اور اصول الشریعت سے مراد ادلہ کلیہ ہیں یعنی کتاب الله سنت رسول علیہ الصلوۃ والسلام اجماع و قیاس اور ان کے مبانی علم التوحید والصفات والنبوات ہیں یعنی علم الکلام جوان امور سے بحث کرتا ہے چونکہ کتاب و سنت کا اثبات ان مسائل کلامیہ پر موقوف ہے اس لئے یہ مسائل اصول فقہ کے لئے مبنی نہیں تمهیدھا کا معنی ہے تویہ اور ان کی اصلاح علی وفق الحق یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ نے اصول شریعیت کا تسویہ کر دیا اور علی طریقہ الصواب اور حق کے موافق ان کی وضع اور اصلاح فرمائی یہ ہے مراد از تمہید مبانی وفروعها ای فروع الشریعہ اس سے مراد احکام تفصلیہ جو علم الفقہ میں بیان کئے گئے۔ یعنی مسائل فقیہ چونکہ شریعت سے عمومی معنی مراد لیا گیا ہے جو فقہ کو بھی شامل تھا اس لئے فروعها ای فروع المشریعت میں اضافت فروع الی الشریعت اضافة الجزر الی الکل ہوگی اور اضافہ الاصول الی الشریعۃ اضافة الدليل الى المدلول ہوگی۔ دقيقة المعانی میں معانی سے مراد علل جزئیہ تفصیلیہ ہیں جو علم الفقہ میں ہر مسئلہ پر پیش کی جاتی ہیں اور وہ علل دقیقہ ہیں ہر ایک انسان ان تک بالسہولت نہیں پہنچ سکتا بلکہ ان کا استخراج مجتہد کا کام ہے اور یہ تمام اشیاء اللہ تعالیٰ کی طرف سے نعمتیں ہیں جو کہ مستوجب محمد ہیں کیونکہ شریعت ایک ایسی نعمت ہے جس کے ساتھ نظام عالم قائم اور صحیح رہتا ہے اور عالم آخرہ میں ثواب کی دارو مدار اسی پر ہے اور رقت معانی کی وجہ سے علماء کے درجات رفیع ہوتے ہیں اور اللہ تعالیٰ کے ہاں انہیں حصولِ ثواب ہو گا اس کلام سے معلوم ہوا کہ علم الاصول علم الفقہ سے فوقانی درجہ رکھتا ہے کیونکہ احکام جزئیہ فقہیہ کی معرفت از ادلہ تفصیلیہ جو مسائل فقہ ہیں یہ ادلہ کلیہ کے احوال کی معرفت پر موقوف ہیں جن سے علم الاصول بحث کرتا ہے اور یہ علم الاصول چونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ اور اس کی صفات کی معرفت پر اور اسی طرح صدق مبلغ بدلالتہ المعجزات کی معرفت پر موقوف ہے جن سے علم الکلام بحث کرتا ہے ۔ لہذا علم الکلام کی بنسبت اسے درجہ سختانی حاصل ہے اور علم الکلام وہ علم ہے جو احوال صانع اور احوال نبوت و امامت و معاد وغیرہ سے بحث کرتا ہے علی طریقہ قانون الاسلام على طريقة الحكمة الالهية الفلسفية بنى على اربعة اركان یہ جملہ اپنے سابقہ جملہ سے بمنزلہ بدل اشتمال کے ہے کیونکہ جملہ سابقہ یعنی جعل اصول الشریعہ اخذ کی بنسبت عظمت علم اور اس کی جلالت قدر کو بیان کرنے میں اونی ہے جیسے کہ بدل او فی ابتبیین المراد ہوتا ہے بنسبت مبدل منہ کے اور حقیقی بدل نہیں کیونکہ مبدل منہ مقصود بالنسیتہ نہیں ہوتا اور یہاں ایسے نہیں بلکہ جملہ سابقہ بھی مقصود ہے خلاصہ اس جملہ کا یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے احکام کے قصر کو اربعہ ارکان پر مبنی فرمایا اور آیات محکمات کے ساتھ اسے انتہائی مستحکم اور مضبوط بنا دیا اور آیات متشابہات کو استار کے خیموں میں مقصور اور محبوس کر دیا تا کہ علماء راسخین کی ابتلاء و آزمائش ہو جیسے کہ مختار عند الاحناف ہے کہ وَمَا لَ لَم تَأْوِيلَهُ إِلَّا الله پر وقف نام ہے یعنی ان متشابہات کی تاویل و تفسیر صرف اللہ تعالیٰ ہی کو معلوم ہے علماء راسخین کا کام یہ ہے کہ اپنے اذہان کی باگ وڈور کو یہاں تھام لیں اور جو علم بالاسرار ان کا محبوب اور قابل اشتیاق مشغلہ ہے اس تک پہنچنے کی کوشش ترک کر دیں اللہ تعالیٰ نے ان متشابہات پر کسی کو مطلع نہیں فرمایا یہ تو ہے تو ضیح متن اب شرح کی طرف توجہ کیجیے ۔ شبه الاحكام الشرعية یعنی مصنف نے احکام شرعیہ کو قصر کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی ہے جس طرح قصر میں جگہ پکڑ کر گرمی سردی سے بچاؤ حاصل کیا جاتا ہے اور اعداء کے خطرات سے اطمینان قصر قلعہ میں داخل ہو کر حاصل کیا جاتا ہے اسی طرح ان احکام شرعیہ کی طرف التجا اور پناہ حاصل کرنے کے ساتھ عدود دین یعنی شیطان کے مہلکات سے پناہ حاصل ہوتی ہے اور جہنم کے عذاب کی گرمی و سردی سے بچاؤ حاصل کرنا ان احکام شرعیہ پر عمل کرنے سے حاصل ہوتا ہے قصر الاحکام میں مشبہ بہ کی اضافت الی الشیہ ہے جیسے لجین الماء میں لجین یعنی فضہ ہے یعنی پانی جو صفائی میں چاندی کی طرح ہے ۔ والاحکام تستند یہاں قصرا حکام کا احتیاج الی اربعہ ارکان کو ثابت کر رہا ہے یعنی احکام شرعی کے ادلہ جزئیہ کثيرة التعداد ہونے کے باوجود ان کا رجوع اربعہ ارکان کی طرف ہے جو قصر احکام کے ارکان ہیں مقصود ان اربعہ ارکان کی طرف شدہ احتیاج کو ثابت کرنا ہے جیسے قصر مکانی ارکان کی طرف محتاج ہے اگرچہ ارکان قصر مکانی کے داخلی اجزاء ہیں اور قصر احکام میں یہ اربعہ ارکان داخل تو نہیں ہیں لیکن ان کی طرف احتیاج ایسے ہے جیسے احتیاج کل الی الجز ہوتا ہے۔ فذكر في اثناء الكلام پھر مصنف نے اللہ کلام میں ان زریعہ ارکان کا ذکرہ اسی ترتیب سے کیا جس طرح شارع نے احکام کی بنیاد ان یہ رکھی تھی کتاب کو پہلے ذکر کیا پھر سنت پھر اجماع اس کے بعد عمل بالقیات
He attached praises and made them dependent upon this matter that Allah has made the foundations of the Shariah (usul al-shariah) a solid foundation and the branches of the Shariah (furu al-shariah) delicate of edges and subtle of meanings. And these are not some of the blessings of Allah, yet praises are a comprehensive plural that should be attached to all bounties. So why the specification of some bounties? The commentator, presenting its reason, said: an indication to the greatness of the science, i.e., this is a specification of the scientific bounty, aiming to indicate the greatness of status and noble worth of this science in which this composition lies. 'And Shariah includes fiqh' meaning by Shariah is meant the general meaning which includes fiqh, and besides them includes usuli issues that are established by transmitted evidences, such as the issue of seeing Allah, the Hereafter, and the authority of Ijma and Qiyas. And by 'usul al-shariah' is meant the universal evidences, i.e., the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of the Messenger, Ijma, and Qiyas, and their foundations are the science of Tawhid, attributes, and prophecies, i.e., the science of Kalam which discusses these matters. Since the establishment of the Book and Sunnah depends on these issues of Kalam, these issues are a foundation for usul al-fiqh. 'Tamhid' means preparation, and their rectification according to the truth, i.e., Allah made the foundations of Shariah well-established and upon the correct way and in accordance with truth, He placed and rectified them. This is the meaning of 'tamhid al-mabani'. 'And their branches (furu'uha)' i.e., the branches of Shariah, meaning detailed rulings which are explained in fiqh. Since Shariah was taken in the general meaning that includes fiqh, therefore the addition of 'branches' to 'Shariah' is the addition of the part to the whole, and the addition of 'usul' to 'Shariah' is the addition of the evidence to the proven. In 'daqiqat al-ma'ani', 'ma'ani' refer to detailed partial causes (ilal) that are presented in fiqh for every issue, and those causes are subtle; not every person can easily reach them, rather their derivation is the work of a mujtahid. And all these things are blessings from Allah deserving of praise. Because Shariah is a blessing by which the system of the world remains established and correct, and in the Hereafter reward depends on it. And due to the subtlety of meanings, the ranks of scholars become high, and they obtain reward from Allah. From this speech it becomes known that the science of Usul holds a superior rank over the science of Fiqh, because the knowledge of detailed fiqhi rulings from detailed evidences (which are fiqhi issues) depends on the knowledge of the conditions of universal evidences that Usul discusses. And this science of Usul, since it depends on the knowledge of Allah and His attributes, and likewise on the knowledge of the truthfulness of the messenger by evidence of miracles which Kalam discusses, therefore Usul has a loftier rank than Kalam. And Kalam is the science that discusses the states of the Creator, prophethood, imamate, the Hereafter, etc., upon the way of the Islamic law on the method of divine philosophy. 'It is built upon four pillars.' This sentence is like a substitute of inclusion for the previous sentence, because the previous sentence is superior in showing the greatness and nobility of the science, just as a substitute of inclusion clarifies the intended meaning relative to the substituted, but it is not a true substitute. The summary of this sentence is that Allah has built the castle of rulings upon four pillars, and strengthened it with muhkam verses, and confined the mutashabih verses within the tents of curtains so that the firmly rooted scholars may be tested, as is the chosen view of the Hanafis that the stop is upon 'and none knows its interpretation except Allah'. The firmly rooted scholars must restrain their minds and abandon striving to reach the beloved and desirable occupation of esoteric knowledge. Allah has not informed anyone of the mutashabih. This is the elucidation of the text. Now turn to the commentary. 'He likened the shariah rulings' meaning the author likened the shariah rulings to a castle. Just as in a castle, one obtains protection from heat and cold and security from the dangers of enemies by entering the fortress, similarly by resorting to these shariah rulings one obtains protection from the destructive things of religion, i.e., Satan, and protection from the heat and cold of Hellfire by acting upon these rulin A castle's need for pillars: here the author is establishing the need of the castle of rulings for four pillars, i.e., even though the detailed evidences of shariah rulings are numerous, they all refer to four pillars that are the pillars of the castle of rulings. The purpose is to establish the need for these four pillars. Just as a spatial castle is in need of pillars, even though the pillars are internal parts of the spatial castle, but in the castle of rulings these four pillars are not internal, yet the need for them is like the need of the whole for the part. 'Then he mentioned in the midst of speech' the author mentioned these four pillars in the same order as the Lawgiver established the rulings upon them: first the Book, then Sunnah, then Ijma, then acting upon Qiyas.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the opening of a usul al-fiqh work, explaining the author's praise and the superiority of usul al-fiqh over fiqh and kalam. The commentator clarifies that the specification of the blessing of this science indicates its great status. He defines usul al-shariah as the universal evidences (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) and explains that their foundation is the science of kalam. The passage then discusses the four pillars (arkan) upon which the shariah rulings (qasr al-ahkam) are built, likening rulings to a fortress that provides protection. The commentator also touches on the Hanafi position regarding the interpretation of mutashabih verses, stating that only Allah knows their interpretation. The author then lists the four sources in the order of priority: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, then Qiyas. This passage establishes the framework for usul al-fiqh as the science that derives rulings from these four foundations.

Key Terms
اصول الشریعت (usul al-shariah): The universal evidences (al-adillah al-kulliyyah) of the Shariah, i.e., the Book, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
فروع الشریعت (furu al-shariah): The detailed rulings (ahkam tafsiliyyah) derived from the universal evidences, discussed in fiqh.
قصر الاحکام (qasr al-ahkam): A metaphor likening the shariah rulings to a castle (qasr) that provides protection and is built upon pillars.
اربعہ ارکان (arba' arkan): The four foundational pillars of the shariah rulings: Kitab, Sunnah, Ijma, and Qiyas.
محکم (muhkam): Clear verses of the Quran whose meaning is unambiguous and which form the basis for legal rulings.
متشابہ (mutashabih): Ambiguous verses whose interpretation is known only to Allah, according to the Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on the interpretation of mutashabih verses?
A) Open to qualified scholars
B) Known only to Allah
C) Known only to the Prophet
D) Known to all Muslims

Key Takeaway
The four pillars of evidence are ordered: Book, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas; and mutashabih verses are known only to Allah, reinforcing the primacy of clear texts.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Author's Motivation and Method for Tanqih al-Usul
Author's preface explaining motivation and method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the author's motivation for writing Tanqih al-Usul and identify the key sources and stylistic choices he makes.

Core Idea
Tanqih al-Usul is a revision of Bazdawi's work, blending conciseness with depth and incorporating Razi and Ibn al-Hajib.

In this preface, the author reveals his scholarly mission: to unlock the treasures of Usul al-Bazdawi, which were hidden behind difficult expressions. He explains his method of combining conciseness with subtle investigations, and names the major usul works that inform his project.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
What difficulties did scholars face with Bazdawi's text? The author notes that its meanings are hidden in 'difficult expressions like rocks', and many scholars fail to grasp its depth due to limited perception.
This establishes the need for a revision.
2
State the author's solution
The author intends to 'revise and organize' (tanqih wa tanzim) the work, determine its intended meanings, and establish its topics according to sound rational principles.
Tanqih means clarification and refinement.
3
Recognize the additional sources
The author will incorporate summaries of Imam al-Razi's al-Mahsul and Ibn al-Hajib's Mukhtasar (al-Hasil) to enrich the presentation.
This shows the synthetic nature of the work.
4
Understand the stylistic approach
He promises conciseness and brevity, using metaphors of 'clinging to the fringes of magic' and 'the strong rope of wonder' to indicate captivating yet precise language.
He explains why he uses singular 'urwah' with i'jaz (singular method) and plural 'ahdab' with sihr (multiple methods).
5
Name the final product
The book is titled Tanqih al-Usul, and the author seeks Allah's help in its completion.
This concludes the preface.

قال المصنف في التوضيح وبعد فان العبد المتوسل با قوى الذریعہ اقوى الذریعہ سے مراد ایمان مکمل اور رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی ذات گرامی ہے قبیل المراد به علم الاحكام والشرائع لما رأيت مصنف یہاں سے اپنی کتاب التنقیح کی وجہ تصنیف اور اس کی کیفیت پیش کر رہا ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب میں نے فحول علماء کو دیکھا کہ ہر دور و زمان میں اپنی انتہائی توجہ اور غایت اقبال کے ساتھ اصول فقہ کے مباحث میں مصروف تھے یہ اصول فقہ فخر الاسلام علی بزدوی رحمتہ اللہ علیہ کی تصنیف تھی جو اصول بزدوی کے نام سے مشہور ہے اور یہ کتاب جلیل الشان اور فائق البرھان تھی لیکن اس کے معانی کے کنز و خزینے ان کی عبارات مشکلہ جو بمنزلہ چٹانوں کے تھیں ان میں مرکوز و مدفون تھے اور نکات غامضہ و پوشیدہ اور اسرار دقیقہ کی طرف رموز و اشارات تھے اور بعض علماء اس کے الفاظ ظاہرہ پر طاعنین تھے در حقیقت ان کی نظر کوتاہ تھی جہاں بزدوی کی لحاظ یعنی آنکھ کے پچھلے حصہ کی نگاہ پہنچتی تھی وہاں ان لوگوں کی گہری نظرو نگاہ نہیں پہنچ سکتی تھی اس لئے اردت تنقیحہ تو میں نے ارادہ کیا کہ اصول بزدوی کی تنقیح و تنظیم کروں اور میں نے قصد کی کہ اس کی تعیین مراد کروں اور قواعد معقول کے موافق اس کی تاسیس اور تقسیم کروں اور میں اپنی اس کتاب تنقیح میں محصول امام رازی کا خلاصہ اور اصول ابن حاجب کا الحاصل بھی پیش کرتا رہوں گا اور ایسی تحقیقات عجیبہ اور تدقیقات غامضہ پیش کروں گا جن سے باقی کتب خالی ہیں عبادت و کلام میں تطویل نہیں کروں گا بلکہ ضبط و ایجاز کا طریقہ اختیار کرتے ہوئے اھداب سحر کے ساتھ تشبث اور عروہ اعجا کے ساتھ تمسک اختیار کروں گا۔ اختار فی الاعجاز یعنی چونکہ اعجازہ فی الکلام سحر کلامی سے قومی ہے اس لئے اعجاز کے ساتھ لفظ عروہ اختیار کیا جو احداب سے قوی ہے جن کو سحر کے ساتھ استعمال کیا پھر اعجاز فی الکلام چونکہ ادائے معنی کے جمیع طرق کلامی سے ابلغ ہوتا ہے لہذاوہ ایک ہی طریقہ ہو سکتا ہے اس لئے اس کے ساتھ لفظ عروہ جو کہ واحد ہے استعمال کیا بخلاف سحر کے کہ اس کے طرق متعدد ہیں لہذا اس کے ساتھ اہداب لفظ جمع کا اختیار کیا وسميته تنقيح الاصول واللہ تعالیٰ مسئول
The author said in al-Tawdih: 'After that, the servant who seeks the strongest means' — 'strongest means' refers to complete faith and the noble personality of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) — it is said that what is meant by it is knowledge of rulings and laws. 'When I saw the author' — from here he presents the reason for writing his book al-Tanqih and its nature, the summary of which is: When I saw the great scholars in every era and time engaged with utmost attention and complete focus in the discussions of usul al-fiqh — this usul al-fiqh was the work of Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi (may Allah have mercy on him), known as Usul al-Bazdawi, and this book was of great status and superior proof, but its treasuries of meanings were hidden and buried in its difficult expressions which were like rocks, and there were allusions and indications to subtle points and hidden secrets. And some scholars were disparagers of its apparent words, in reality their sight was short; where the glance of Bazdawi's 'lahaz' (the back part of the eye) reached, their deep vision could not reach. Therefore I intended to revise it (tanqih) and organize it, and I aimed to determine its intended meanings, and to establish and divide it according to reasonable principles. And in this book of mine, al-Tanqih, I will also present summaries of Imam al-Razi's al-Mahsul and Ibn al-Hajib's al-Mukhtasar (known as al-Hasil), and I will present such amazing researches and subtle verifications that are absent from other books. I will not prolong in worship and speech, but will adopt the method of conciseness and brevity, clinging to the fringes of magic (ahdab al-sihr) and holding fast to the strong rope of wonder ('urwat al-i'jaz). He chose 'i'jaz' — since 'i'jaz' in speech is related to linguistic magic, therefore he chose the word 'urwah' with 'i'jaz', which is stronger than 'ahdab' used with 'sihr'. Moreover, 'i'jaz' in speech is more eloquent than all other ways of conveying meaning, so it can be only one method, therefore he used the singular 'urwah' with it, unlike 'sihr' which has multiple methods, therefore he chose the plural 'ahdab' with it. And I named it Tanqih al-Usul. And Allah is the one from whom help is sought.'
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface explaining why he wrote his book Tanqih al-Usul. He observes that scholars of every era have been deeply engaged with the study of usul al-fiqh, specifically the work of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (Usul al-Bazdawi). That book is highly esteemed but its meanings are difficult and hidden behind complex expressions, like treasures buried in rocks. Many scholars fail to grasp its deep insights because their understanding is limited, unlike Bazdawi's sharp perception. To remedy this, the author decided to 'revise and organize' (tanqih wa tanzim) al-Bazdawi's work. He aims to clarify its intent, and to establish and divide its topics according to sound rational principles. He will also incorporate summaries from other major usul works: Imam al-Razi's al-Mahsul and Ibn al-Hajib's Mukhtasar (al-Hasil). He promises to include novel and subtle investigations not found in other books. He will avoid verbosity and adopt a concise style, which he illustrates with the metaphor of clinging to the fringes of magic (sihr) and the strong rope of wonder (i'jaz). He explains that he used 'urwah' (singular) with 'i'jaz' because i'jaz in speech is singular in method, whereas sihr has multiple methods, so he used 'ahdab' (plural) with sihr. Finally, he names his book Tanqih al-Usul and ends by seeking Allah's help.

Key Terms
تنقیح (Tanqih): To revise, clarify, and organize a text, removing ambiguities and difficult expressions.
اعجاز (I'jaz): Inimitability or wonder, particularly of the Quran, but here used metaphorically for miraculous conciseness in speech.
سحر (Sihr): Magic, used metaphorically for the captivating effect of eloquent speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of the author in writing Tanqih al-Usul?
A) To write a completely new book on usul al-fiqh.
B) To clarify and organize the difficult text of Usul al-Bazdawi.
C) To criticize Imam al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib.
D) To compile all the rulings of the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
The author wrote Tanqih al-Usul to make the deep insights of Usul al-Bazdawi accessible through revision, organization, and integration of other major usul works.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Author's Purpose in Writing Tanqih al-Usul
Explaining the author's motivation and methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the author's motivation for writing Tanqih al-Usul and identify the key methodological features he employed.

Core Idea
Tanqih refines Bazdawi's dense usul, exposing hidden treasures through rational organization.

Every great work of usul is born from a scholarly need. The author of Al-Tawdih saw that Usul al-Bazdawi, a monumental text, was beset with difficult expressions that obscured its profound meanings. Some critics even misunderstood it. This lesson unpacks the author's response: a deliberate refinement (tanqih) that cleans and organizes the text while integrating insights from other masters like al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the observation
What did the author observe about scholars and Usul al-Bazdawi? Note that he saw experts engaging with it, yet its meanings were buried in rock-like expressions.
The phrase 'jaleel al-shan wa bahir al-burhan' shows respect for Bazdawi's work.
2
Identify the problem
The author noted two issues: difficult expressions that were like rocks hiding treasures, and critics who lacked deep insight. What were these critics missing?
Bazdawi's 'lahaz' (back-of-the-eye glance) reached where others could not.
3
Identify the author's solution
The author decided to perform 'tanqih' and 'tanzim' (refinement and organization). What does tanqih mean in detail?
Tanqih is like pruning a palm tree of excess branches, preserving the core.
4
Identify the methodological additions
Besides clarifying Bazdawi, what other sources does the author incorporate?
He includes a summary of al-Muhassal (al-Razi) and the essence of Usul Ibn al-Hajib.
5
Identify the stylistic choice
The author emphasizes conciseness (ijaz) and uses metaphorical language. How does he describe his style?
He clings to the 'eyelashes of magic' and the 'handle of inimitability' — using singular/plural to reflect uniqueness.

It is said that the Quran interprets some of it by other parts, so in that respect 'Fasl al-Khitab' means divine address. His saying 'ma rufi'a' i.e. 'madam' — he indicated with it that 'ma' means 'madaam' which is an adverb, meaning that as long as the banners of religion and the cool consensus of the mujtahids remain raised and high, then blessings and peace continue to descend from Allah upon the Prophet and his companions. A consensus issue is always elevated, never lowered, always established, never humiliated. This is the meaning of 'raised without being placed and established without being lowered.' The author said in al-Tawdih: 'And after, the servant who seeks the strongest means' — by 'strongest means' is meant complete faith and the noble personality of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. 'Qabil al-murad bihi 'ilm al-ahkam wa al-shara'i'' — when I saw the author' — from here he presents the reason for writing his book al-Tanqih and its quality. The summary is that when I saw the senior scholars engaging with utmost attention and complete acceptance in the discussions of usul al-fiqh, this usul al-fiqh was the work of Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi, may Allah have mercy on him, famous as Usul al-Bazdawi. This book was of great dignity and brilliant proof, but its treasures of meanings and its difficult expressions, which were like rocks, were buried and hidden within. There were subtle points and concealed allusions and indications of precise secrets. Some scholars criticized its apparent words, but in reality their sight was short; where Bazdawi's glance (the back of the eye) reached, their deep vision could not. So I intended to revise (tanqih) it — I intended to revise and organize Usul al-Bazdawi. I aimed to determine its meanings and to establish and classify it according to rational principles. In my book al-Tanqih, I will also present the summary of al-Muhassal by Imam al-Razi and the essence of Usul Ibn al-Hajib. I will present such wonderful investigations and complex verifications that other books lack. I will not lengthen in worship and speech, but will adopt the method of conciseness and brevity, clinging to the eyelashes of magic and holding fast to the handle of inimitability. He chose in al-I'jaz because the inimitability in speech is akin to verbal magic, so he used the word 'urwa (handle) with i'jaz, which is stronger than 'ahdab (eyelashes) used with magic. Then since i'jaz in speech is more eloquent than all verbal methods of conveying meaning, it can be a single method, so he used the singular 'urwa, unlike magic which has multiple methods, so he used the plural 'ahdab. He named it Tanqih al-Usul, and Allah is the one asked for help. The commentator said in al-Tadrij: 'His saying 'jaleel al-shan' to 'azeem al-amr' — 'azeem' and 'jaleel' are synonymous, and 'amr' is a metaphor for rank and station. 'Bahir al-burhan' — 'bahir' means dominant and surpassing, and 'burhan' means proof and evidence. 'Murkez' means buried; when a spear is planted in the ground, it is said 'rakaztu al-rumh'; this word 'murkez' is derived from that usage. 'Kunooz' refers to buried wealth. 'Al-Sukhur' are great rocks. The author likened the difficult expressions of Usul al-Bazdawi, which are full of benefit, to rocks in that reaching their meanings is very difficult, just as reaching things hidden in the belly of rocks is difficult. He likened the hidden meanings in those expressions to precious jewels hidden in rocks. 'Maroom' is derived from 'ramz', which refers to a gesture made with lips and eyebrows; it is transitive with 'ila', but here by deletion and modification, the preposition is dropped and the verb is made directly transitive, so the word 'ghawamid' becomes the subject of 'maroom'. 'Al-nukta al-latifa' — the word 'nukt' mentioned by the author in his worship is the plural of 'nukta', which refers to a subtle point that is refined and free of excess. It is derived from 'nakata fi al-ard bi al-qadib'; generally, a person, when deep in thought, pokes the ground with a stick, so this is the cause and means of obtaining that subtlety, hence it was named 'nukta'. The summary is that in Usul al-Bazdawi there were precise indications towards hidden points. 'Al-Nazar' means to look at something with the eyes and then ponder with deep sight. 'Lahz' is to look at something with the back of the eye; 'lahaz' is the back of the eye, just as 'mugh' is the front of the eye. 'Al-Tanqih' is refinement, i.e., cleaning something by removing excess. It is said 'naehtu al-jidh' when a palm tree is pruned of excess branches, provided that the core and brain branches are not cut. 'Tanzim' is stringing pearls in a proper order. 'Wa al-kalam la yakhloo' — the author has included some definitions in this speech; there were some excesses in Usul Fakhr al-Islam that needed removal, some scattered issues that needed organization, and some difficult matters that needed resolution. They were not based on rational principles, i.e., the conditions of definitions and proofs mentioned in the science of logic were not observed, and in classifications the non-overlap of categories was not considered. These are matters that the earlier scholars did not pay attention to. His saying 'li'an al-i'jaz' — the author, interpreting i'jaz, said 'an buwa al-ma'na', i.e., conveying the meaning [in a way]...
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn of Al-Tawdih by Sadr al-Shariah. It begins with an explanation of a phrase about the Quran interpreting itself, then moves to the author's statement in Al-Tawdih where he describes his motivation for writing Tanqih al-Usul. The commentator explains that the author of Al-Tawdih saw that scholars were engaged with Usul al-Bazdawi, a highly respected but difficult work. The author found that the meanings were hidden like treasures in rocks, and some critics misunderstood the text due to their limited insight. Therefore, he decided to revise (tanqih) and organize Bazdawi's work, clarifying its meanings and arranging it according to rational rules. He also intended to incorporate insights from Imam al-Razi's al-Muhassal and Ibn al-Hajib's al-Mukhtasar. The passage then elaborates on specific terms used by the author, such as 'jaleel al-shan' (great dignity), 'bahir al-burhan' (brilliant proof), 'murkez' (buried), and 'tanqih' (refinement). The commentator explains these definitions lexically, drawing from Arabic usage. The passage concludes with a discussion of the author's choice of words like 'urwa' and 'ahdab' to illustrate the concept of inimitability (i'jaz). This is all front matter, setting the stage for the author's methodology and goals in writing Tanqih al-Usul.

Key Terms
جلیل الشان (jaleel al-shan): The text defines it as synonymous with 'azeem al-amr', meaning 'great in rank and station'.
باهر البرهان (bahir al-burhan): The text defines 'bahir' as 'dominant and surpassing', and 'burhan' as 'proof and evidence'.
تنقیح (tanqih): The text defines tanqih as refinement (tahdhib), i.e., cleaning something by removing excess, like pruning a palm tree of excess branches.
مرکوز (murkez): The text defines it as 'buried', derived from the phrase 'rakaztu al-rumh' (I planted the spear).
مرفوع لا یوضع ومنصوب لا یخفض (marfoo' la yooda' wa mansoob la yukhfad): The text explains that a consensus issue is always elevated (marfoo') and established (mansoob), never lowered or humiliated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the primary reason the author wrote Tanqih al-Usul?
A) To write a completely new usul al-fiqh work without reference to previous scholars
B) To clarify the difficult expressions of Usul al-Bazdawi and organize it according to rational principles
C) To refute Imam al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib
D) To write a simplified version for beginners

Key Takeaway
Tanqih al-Usul is a methodological refinement of Bazdawi's work, combining clarification, rational organization, and synthesis with other usul authorities.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Defining Usul al-Fiqh and Distinguishing It from 'Ilm al-Khilaf
Defining Usul al-Fiqh and defending its scope from 'ilm al-khilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of Usul al-Fiqh and explain why the qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq excludes 'ilm al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh is the knowledge of universal qawā'id by which fiqh rulings are derived, not dialectically defended.

This passage presents the formal definition of Usul al-Fiqh as knowledge of universal principles (qawā'id kulliyyah) that enable the jurist to derive particular rulings from detailed evidences. The author of al-Tawdih added the phrase 'ala wajh al-tahqiq (in a verified manner) to exclude 'ilm al-khilaf, which is the science of dialectical disputation. An objector argues that the rules of 'ilm al-khilaf also lead to fiqh, but the response clarifies that 'ilm al-khilaf is for preservation and defense, not derivation. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing the proper scope of usul work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of Usul al-Fiqh
Locate the phrase that defines Usul al-Fiqh: 'al-'ilm bi al-qawa'id allati yutawassalu biha ila al-fiqh.' Note the key terms: qawā'id (rules/principles) and yutawassalu (arrive at/derive).
The definition emphasizes universality (kulliyyah) — the rules are not case-specific.
2
Understand the function of the qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq
The author added this phrase to exclude 'ilm al-khilaf. Ask: what does 'ala wajh al-tahqiq add? It means 'in a verified manner,' indicating a direct, proper derivation process.
Without this qualification, one might think that any knowledge leading to fiqh (including dialectics) is part of Usul.
3
Analyze the objection and response
An objector claims that the rules of 'ilm al-khilaf also lead to fiqh, so the qualification is unnecessary. Read the response: 'ilm al-khilaf leads to preservation and defense, not derivation. Its connection to fiqh is not exclusive.
The response uses the phrase 'illa anna al-fuqaha' — the fuqaha' have discussed fiqh issues in 'ilm al-khilaf, causing a misconception.
4
Apply the definition to a concrete example
Consider the Hanafi qā'idah: 'al-umur bi-maqāṣidihā.' This is a universal principle used to derive rulings about intention in acts of worship and contracts. That is Usul al-Fiqh. Using the same rule to defend a ruling in debate is 'ilm al-khilaf.
The test: is the rule being used to derive or to defend? That decides the discipline.

احکام جزئیہ کے استنباط از ادلہ تفصیلیہ تک رسائی حاصل ہوسکتی تھی پھر ان تمام امور کو ضبط کر کے تدوین کی اور ان کے ساتھ نواحی اور متممات و بیان اختلافات جو مناسب ولائق تھا ان کا اضافہ کیا اب ان قضایا کلیہ مذکورہ کے ساتھ جو علم متعلق ہے اس کا نام اصول فقہ رکھا حصار ای اصول الفقه عبارة عن العلم بالقواعد التي يتوصل بھا الی الفقہ اور لفظ قواعد خود مشعرالی قید الاجمال ہے کیونکہ قواعد کلیہ میں جزئیات تفصیلیہ کا ذکر نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اجمالاً اس کی کلیتہ میں درج ہوتی ہیں۔ زاد المصنف قيد التحقيق يعنی مصنف نے علم الخلاف سے احتراز کرنے کی خاطر قید علی وجہ التحقیق کا اضافہ کیا۔ و لقائل ان يمنع اس سے مصنف " پر اس قید کے اضافہ پر اعتراض کر دیا کہ یہ تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ قواعد علم الخلاف کے ساتھ فقہ کی طرف توصل قریب ہے جب توصل قریب نہ ہوا تو یہ تو صلاً قریبا سے خارج ہو جائے گا۔ بل انما يتوصل به الا یہ علم الخلاف کا فائدہ عمومی بیان کر رہا ہے کہ اس کے ساتھ در حقیقت حکم مستنبط کی محافظہ تیا مدافعہ تک وصول ہوتا ہے اور اس کی نسبت فقہ اور غیر فقہ کی طرف برابر درجہ کی ہے فان الجدلی یعنی جدلی انسان جو علم الخلاف کے قواعد کے ساتھ تمسک اختیار کرتا ہے یا تو وہ مجیب ہو گا تو اس صورت میں اپنی مقرر کردہ وضع کی محافظت کر رہا ہوتا ہے یا معترض ہو گا تو اس صورت میں پھر موضعا یعنی مخالف کی مقرر کردہ وضع کو توڑ رہا ہو گا الا ان الفقهاء یہ اس اعتراض مذکورہ کا جواب ہے حاصل اس کا یہ ہے کہ چونکہ فقہاء نے اس علم الخلاف میں بہت سے مسائل فقہ میں کلام کی ہے اور اس پر بہت سے نکات خلافیہ کی بنا رکھی ہے اس لئے توہم پیدا ہوتا تھا کہ اس علم کو اختصاص بالفقہ ہے اس تو ہم کو دفع کرنے کے لئے مصنف نے علی وجہ التحقیق کی قید لگا کر اس تو ہم کو دفع کیا ہے۔
From the detailed evidences, access to deriving particular rulings could be obtained. Then, after recording all these matters, he compiled and added to them related, complementary, and explanatory matters of differences that were appropriate. Now, the knowledge related to these mentioned universal propositions is named Usul al-Fiqh. In summary, Usul al-Fiqh is the knowledge of the rules (qawā'id) by which one arrives at fiqh. The word 'qawā'id' itself indicates the condition of totality, because universal rules do not mention particular partials in detail, but rather they are included in its universality summarily. The author added the condition 'ala wajh al-tahqiq', meaning the author added the qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq' to avoid 'ilm al-khilaf. An objector may deny this: he objected to the addition of this qualification, saying that it is not accepted that the rules of 'ilm al-khilaf lead to fiqh in a proximate manner; when they do not lead proximately, then this knowledge would be excluded from being proximate at all. Rather, it is only led to through it: this explains the general benefit of 'ilm al-khilaf, that with it one actually attains preservation and defense of the derived ruling, and its relation to fiqh and non-fiqh is equal. For the dialectician (jadalī) who adheres to the rules of 'ilm al-khilaf is either a respondent, in which case he preserves his established position, or an objector, in which case he breaks the opponent's established position. Except that the fuqaha'... This is the answer to the mentioned objection. Its summary is that since the fuqaha' have discussed many fiqh issues in this 'ilm al-khilaf and have built many points of disagreement upon it, a misconception arose that this knowledge is specific to fiqh. To repel this misconception, the author added the qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq, thus repelling the misconception.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the subject matter of Usul al-Fiqh. The author explains that Usul al-Fiqh is knowledge of universal qawā'id (principles) that enable one to derive particular fiqh rulings from detailed evidences. The qualification 'qawā'id' indicates that these principles are general and do not enumerate particular cases. The author of al-Tawdih added the phrase 'ala wajh al-tahqiq (in a verified manner) to distinguish Usul al-Fiqh from 'ilm al-khilaf (the science of dialectical disputation). An objector argues that the rules of 'ilm al-khilaf also lead to fiqh, so the qualification is unnecessary. The response is that 'ilm al-khilaf is used for defending or opposing positions, not for deriving rulings; its relation to fiqh is not exclusive. However, because fuqaha' often use it for fiqh issues, there is a misconception that it is part of fiqh. The qualification clarifies that Usul al-Fiqh is specifically the principles for deriving rulings, not the dialectical defense of them.

Key Terms
قضایا کلیة (qaḍāyā kulliyyah): Universal propositions that serve as principles for deriving particular fiqh rulings
علم الخلاف ('ilm al-khilāf): Science of dialectical disputation used to defend or oppose legal positions, not for deriving rulings
علی وجہ التحقیق ('alā wajh al-taḥqīq): Qualification meaning 'in a verified manner' to exclude 'ilm al-khilaf from the definition of usul al-fiqh

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author of al-Tawdih add the qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq to the definition of Usul al-Fiqh?
A) To exclude the science of hadith from the definition
B) To exclude 'ilm al-khilaf (dialectical disputation) from the definition
C) To emphasize that fiqh rulings are definitive (qat'i)
D) To restrict usul to the Hanafi madhhab only

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Fiqh is knowledge of universal principles for deriving fiqh rulings, not for dialectical debate; the qualification 'ala wajh al-tahqiq safeguards this distinction.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
Defining Usul al-Fiqh and Its Subject Matter
Defines usul al-fiqh and clarifies its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of usul al-fiqh and identify the types of evidences and discussions included in the phrase 'ma yata'allaqu biha'.

Core Idea
Usul al-Fiqh studies the conditions of primary evidences and everything connected to them, including disputed proofs and ijtihad.

The passage opens with a clarification of the widely accepted definition of usul al-fiqh. It then expands on the phrase 'what relates to them' (ma yata'allaqu biha) to show that the science covers not only the four primary proofs but also disputed evidences like istishab and istihsan, as well as discussions of ijtihad and taqlid. This lesson unpacks that definition and its scope.

Guided Path
1
Parse the definition
Identify the two key components of the definition: 'conditions of the evidences' and 'what relates to them.' The 'fa' in 'fayabhathu' connects to the earlier definition.
The passage is a commentary (sharh) on a prior definition.
2
Understand 'ma yata'allaqu biha'
Analyze what is included: disputed evidences (e.g., istishab, istihsan) and matters that have a role in establishing rulings (e.g., ijtihad, taqlid). Note that the pronoun 'ha' refers to the primary evidences.
This expands the scope beyond the four agreed-upon sources.
3
Identify the scope
Recognize that the definition intentionally includes all shar'i evidences and their related concepts, making usul al-fiqh a comprehensive science of evidence and methodology.
Contrast with a narrow definition that only covers the four sources.
4
Apply the definition
Connect this definition to the subsequent classification: the 'conditions of evidences' correspond to the first type of essential attributes (being establishers of rulings), while 'what relates to them' includes the second and third types.
This sets up the division in the next lesson.

فیبحث فيه عن احوال الادلة المذكورة وما يتعلق بھا یہ اصول فقہ کی حدو تعریف پر تفریح ہے لہذا فیجت کی فا متعلق بالحد و التعریف ہوگی ۔ و ما يتعلق بها عطف على الادلة يعنى وما يتعلق کا عطف الادلہ پر ہے اور بھا کی ضمیر راجع الی الا دلتہ ہوگی اور اس مایتعلق بالادلہ سے مراد وہ ادلہ ہیں جو مختلف فیھا ہیں جیسے استصحاب اور استحسان اور ادلہ مقلد وستفتى وايضا ما يتعلق الم یعنی وہ اشیاء جوادلہ اربعہ سے متعلق ہیں اور ان کو مثبت للحکم ہونے میں دخل ہے جیسے بحث عن الاجتہاد وغیرہ ان سے بھی بحث کی جائے گی۔ وَاعْلَمْ ان الْعَوَارِضَ الذَّاتِيَّةَ لِلْاَدِلَّةِ ثَلَاثَةُ اَقْسَامٍ یعنی ادلہ کے عوارض ذاتیہ تین قسم ہیں ایک قسم وہ عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں جو ہمارے اس فن میں مبحوث عنہا ہوتے ہیں اور یہ ہیں وَهُوَ كَوْنُهَا مُثْبِتَةً لِلْاَحْكَامِ یعنی ادلہ کا عارض ہو ان کا مثبت للاحکام ہونا ومنها ما ليست الجزیہ عوارض کی دوسری قسم ہے یعنی یہ وہ عوارض ہیں جن سے اس فن میں بحث تو نہیں کی جاتی لیکن عوارض مبحوث عنہا کے لحوق میں انہیں دخل ہوتا ہے جیسے ادلہ کا عام ہونا اور مشترک و خبر واحد ہونا - ومنها ما ليس كذلك يہ عوارض کی قسم ثالث ہے یعنی ایسے عوارض ہیں کہ نہ تو خود مبحوث عنہا ہیں اور نہ مبحوث عنہا کے لحوق میں انہیں مداخلت ہے جیسے دلیل کا قدیم یا حادث ہونا ۔ فَالْقِسْمُ الْاَوَّلُ یہ طریق بحث کی توصیح ہے یعنی عوارض کی قسم اول محمول نہیں گے ان قضایا میں جو ہمارے فن کے لئے وہ مسائل ہیں۔ وَالْقِسْمُ الثَّانِی یعنی عوارض کا قسم ثانی ان قضایا مذکورہ کے موضوع کے لئے اوصاف وقیور بنیں گے جیسے الْخَبَرُ الَّذِی یہ د یہ واحد یو جب غلبة الظن تو الخبر موضوع ہے اور الَّذِی یَرْوِیْہِ اس کی صفت اور قید ہے اور یہ قسم ثانی کبھی قضایا مذکورہ میں موضوع بن جائیں گے جیسے الْعَامُّ يُوجِبُ الْحُكْمَ قَطْعًا اور کبھی محمول بن جائیں گے جیسے الْفِكْرَةُ فِي مَوْضِعِ النَّقْی عَامَّةً وكذلك الاعراض الذاتية للحكوثلثة اقسام ايضا یعنی حکم کے اعراض ذاتیہ بھی تین قسم ہیں الْاَوَّلُ مَا يَكُونُ یعنی پہلی قسم اعراض کی وہ ہے جو اس فن میں مبحوث عنہا ہیں کہ ان کی بحث کی جاتی ہے وَهُوَ كَوْنُ الْحَكْمُ یعنی حکم کا ادلہ مذکورہ سے ثابت ہونا وَالثَّانِی اور دوسری قسم عوارض حکم کی وہ ہے جنہیں مبحوث عنہا عوارض
'So in it are discussed the conditions of the mentioned evidences and what relates to them.' This is an elaboration on the definition and limits of usul al-fiqh. Hence the 'fa' in 'fayabhathu' relates to the definition. 'And what relates to them' is a conjunction on 'the evidences' meaning 'and what relates' is attached to 'the evidences', and the pronoun 'ha' refers to the evidences. By 'what relates to the evidences' is meant those evidences which are disputed, such as istishab and istihsan, and the evidences of the muqallid and the one seeking fatwa. Also 'what relates to' – i.e., those things that relate to the four evidences and have a role in establishing rulings, such as the discussion of ijtihad etc.; these are also discussed. 'And know that the essential attributes of the evidences are three types': that is, the essential attributes of the evidences are three types: one type are those essential attributes which are discussed in our art, and they are: their being establishers of rulings – meaning the attribute of the evidences being establishers of rulings. 'And from them are those that are not' – the second type of attributes: that is, those attributes which are not discussed in this art, but they have an effect in the occurrence of the discussed attributes, such as the evidence being general ('amm), shared (mushtarak), and khabar wahid. 'And from them are those not like that' – the third type: that is, such attributes that are neither discussed themselves nor do they have interference in the occurrence of the discussed attributes, like the evidence being ancient or contingent. 'So the first type' – this clarifies the method of discussion: i.e., the first type of attributes will be predicates in those propositions which are the issues of our art. 'And the second type' – i.e., the second type of attributes will serve as qualifiers and restrictions for the subject of those mentioned propositions, like 'the report which' – here 'report' is the subject and 'which is narrated by him' is its attribute and restriction. And sometimes this second type becomes the subject in those propositions, like 'the general (al-'amm) necessitates the ruling definitively', and sometimes becomes the predicate, like 'the thought in the place of purity is general.' Similarly, the essential attributes of the ruling are also three types: the first type are those attributes which are discussed in this art, and they are: the ruling being established by the mentioned evidences. The second type... (text cuts off)
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of usul al-fiqh and then methodically classifies the essential attributes (a'radh dhatiyyah) of both the evidences (adillah) and the rulings (ahkam). It begins by clarifying that the definition 'the science that discusses the conditions of the shar'i evidences and what relates to them' is elaborated here. The 'what relates to them' refers to disputed evidences like istishab and istihsan, as well as discussions of ijtihad and taqlid that are connected to the four primary evidences (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas). Then it divides the essential attributes of the evidences into three categories: (1) attributes that are directly discussed in usul al-fiqh, namely the fact that they establish rulings (kawnuha muthbitatan lil-ahkam); (2) attributes that are not directly discussed but affect the occurrence of the discussed attributes, such as generality ('umum), sharedness (ishtirak), and being a solitary report (khabar wahid); (3) attributes that are neither discussed nor influential, such as the evidence being eternal (qadim) or created (hadith). The first category forms the predicates of the propositions of this science, the second category can serve as either qualifiers of the subject or become subjects/predicates themselves (e.g., 'al-'amm yujibu al-hukm qat'an'), and the third is irrelevant. The same three-type classification applies to the rulings: (1) the attribute that is discussed is the ruling being established by the mentioned evidences; (2) other attributes that affect this (not completed in the text). This systematic classification reflects the Hanafi concern with precise categorization of the objects of study in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
عارض ذاتی (arad dhati): An essential attribute intrinsic to the subject (evidence or ruling). Classified into those directly discussed, those indirectly relevant, and those irrelevant.
حدود و تعریف (hudud wa ta'rif): The definition and limits of a science. Here, the definition of usul al-fiqh is given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the phrase 'ma yata'allaqu biha' (what relates to them) include according to the passage?
A) Only the four primary evidences.
B) Disputed evidences like istihsan and discussions of ijtihad.
C) Only the historical context of verses.
D) The rulings themselves, not the evidences.

Key Takeaway
Usul al-fiqh is the science of the conditions of shar'i evidences AND everything connected to them, making it a comprehensive methodology.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
The Three Types of Essential Attributes (A'radh Dhatiyyah)
Classifies essential attributes of evidences and rulings into three types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the essential attributes of evidences and rulings into three categories and provide examples of each.

Core Idea
Only the attribute of establishing rulings is directly discussed; others are contextual or irrelevant.

Building on the definition, the passage now classifies the essential attributes (a'radh dhatiyyah) of both evidences and rulings into three types. This classification helps us understand which aspects of evidences are the primary focus of usul al-fiqh, which are secondary but relevant, and which are irrelevant. The same three-fold division applies to rulings, showing the systematic nature of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
State the three-type division for evidences
List the three types: (1) attributes directly discussed – the evidence being an establisher of rulings; (2) attributes not directly discussed but affecting the first type – e.g., generality, sharedness, being a solitary report; (3) attributes neither discussed nor affecting – e.g., being ancient or contingent.
Memorize the three categories with examples.
2
Differentiate direct vs indirect relevance
Understand that type 2 attributes (like 'amm, mushtarak, khabar wahid) are studied because they impact the evidence's ability to establish rulings. They themselves are not the primary subject but are necessary to understand the first type.
For example, 'amm is studied to know whether a general command is definitive or not.
3
Recognize irrelevant attributes
Type 3 attributes (e.g., the evidence being eternal or created) have no effect on the evidence's legal function. They belong to other sciences like kalam, not usul al-fiqh.
This demarcates the boundaries of usul al-fiqh from other disciplines.
4
Apply the same classification to rulings
The text states that rulings also have three types of essential attributes. The first type is the ruling being established by the mentioned evidences. The second and third types are analogous to those of evidences.
The passage cuts off, but the symmetry is clear.
5
Summarize the analytical function
The first type becomes predicates in the propositions of usul (e.g., 'The evidence establishes the ruling'). The second type can be either subjects or predicates (e.g., 'The general necessitates the ruling definitively'). The third type does not appear in usul propositions.
This is a meta-classification of the propositions of the science.

فیبحث فيه عن احوال الادلة المذكورة وما يتعلق بھا یہ اصول فقہ کی حدو تعریف پر تفریح ہے لہذا فیجت کی فا متعلق بالحد و التعریف ہوگی ۔ و ما يتعلق بها عطف على الادلة يعنى وما يتعلق کا عطف الادلہ پر ہے اور بھا کی ضمیر راجع الی الا دلتہ ہوگی اور اس مایتعلق بالادلہ سے مراد وہ ادلہ ہیں جو مختلف فیھا ہیں جیسے استصحاب اور استحسان اور ادلہ مقلد وستفتى وايضا ما يتعلق الم یعنی وہ اشیاء جوادلہ اربعہ سے متعلق ہیں اور ان کو مثبت للحکم ہونے میں دخل ہے جیسے بحث عن الاجتہاد وغیرہ ان سے بھی بحث کی جائے گی۔ وَاعْلَمْ ان الْعَوَارِضَ الذَّاتِيَّةَ لِلْاَدِلَّةِ ثَلَاثَةُ اَقْسَامٍ یعنی ادلہ کے عوارض ذاتیہ تین قسم ہیں ایک قسم وہ عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں جو ہمارے اس فن میں مبحوث عنہا ہوتے ہیں اور یہ ہیں وَهُوَ كَوْنُهَا مُثْبِتَةً لِلْاَحْكَامِ یعنی ادلہ کا عارض ہو ان کا مثبت للاحکام ہونا ومنها ما ليست الجزیہ عوارض کی دوسری قسم ہے یعنی یہ وہ عوارض ہیں جن سے اس فن میں بحث تو نہیں کی جاتی لیکن عوارض مبحوث عنہا کے لحوق میں انہیں دخل ہوتا ہے جیسے ادلہ کا عام ہونا اور مشترک و خبر واحد ہونا - ومنها ما ليس كذلك يہ عوارض کی قسم ثالث ہے یعنی ایسے عوارض ہیں کہ نہ تو خود مبحوث عنہا ہیں اور نہ مبحوث عنہا کے لحوق میں انہیں مداخلت ہے جیسے دلیل کا قدیم یا حادث ہونا ۔ فَالْقِسْمُ الْاَوَّلُ یہ طریق بحث کی توصیح ہے یعنی عوارض کی قسم اول محمول نہیں گے ان قضایا میں جو ہمارے فن کے لئے وہ مسائل ہیں۔ وَالْقِسْمُ الثَّانِی یعنی عوارض کا قسم ثانی ان قضایا مذکورہ کے موضوع کے لئے اوصاف وقیور بنیں گے جیسے الْخَبَرُ الَّذِی یہ د یہ واحد یو جب غلبة الظن تو الخبر موضوع ہے اور الَّذِی یَرْوِیْہِ اس کی صفت اور قید ہے اور یہ قسم ثانی کبھی قضایا مذکورہ میں موضوع بن جائیں گے جیسے الْعَامُّ يُوجِبُ الْحُكْمَ قَطْعًا اور کبھی محمول بن جائیں گے جیسے الْفِكْرَةُ فِي مَوْضِعِ النَّقْی عَامَّةً وكذلك الاعراض الذاتية للحكوثلثة اقسام ايضا یعنی حکم کے اعراض ذاتیہ بھی تین قسم ہیں الْاَوَّلُ مَا يَكُونُ یعنی پہلی قسم اعراض کی وہ ہے جو اس فن میں مبحوث عنہا ہیں کہ ان کی بحث کی جاتی ہے وَهُوَ كَوْنُ الْحَكْمُ یعنی حکم کا ادلہ مذکورہ سے ثابت ہونا وَالثَّانِی اور دوسری قسم عوارض حکم کی وہ ہے جنہیں مبحوث عنہا عوارض
'So in it are discussed the conditions of the mentioned evidences and what relates to them.' This is an elaboration on the definition and limits of usul al-fiqh. Hence the 'fa' in 'fayabhathu' relates to the definition. 'And what relates to them' is a conjunction on 'the evidences' meaning 'and what relates' is attached to 'the evidences', and the pronoun 'ha' refers to the evidences. By 'what relates to the evidences' is meant those evidences which are disputed, such as istishab and istihsan, and the evidences of the muqallid and the one seeking fatwa. Also 'what relates to' – i.e., those things that relate to the four evidences and have a role in establishing rulings, such as the discussion of ijtihad etc.; these are also discussed. 'And know that the essential attributes of the evidences are three types': that is, the essential attributes of the evidences are three types: one type are those essential attributes which are discussed in our art, and they are: their being establishers of rulings – meaning the attribute of the evidences being establishers of rulings. 'And from them are those that are not' – the second type of attributes: that is, those attributes which are not discussed in this art, but they have an effect in the occurrence of the discussed attributes, such as the evidence being general ('amm), shared (mushtarak), and khabar wahid. 'And from them are those not like that' – the third type: that is, such attributes that are neither discussed themselves nor do they have interference in the occurrence of the discussed attributes, like the evidence being ancient or contingent. 'So the first type' – this clarifies the method of discussion: i.e., the first type of attributes will be predicates in those propositions which are the issues of our art. 'And the second type' – i.e., the second type of attributes will serve as qualifiers and restrictions for the subject of those mentioned propositions, like 'the report which' – here 'report' is the subject and 'which is narrated by him' is its attribute and restriction. And sometimes this second type becomes the subject in those propositions, like 'the general (al-'amm) necessitates the ruling definitively', and sometimes becomes the predicate, like 'the thought in the place of purity is general.' Similarly, the essential attributes of the ruling are also three types: the first type are those attributes which are discussed in this art, and they are: the ruling being established by the mentioned evidences. The second type... (text cuts off)
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage provides a definition of usul al-fiqh and then methodically classifies the essential attributes (a'radh dhatiyyah) of both the evidences (adillah) and the rulings (ahkam). It begins by clarifying that the definition 'the science that discusses the conditions of the shar'i evidences and what relates to them' is elaborated here. The 'what relates to them' refers to disputed evidences like istishab and istihsan, as well as discussions of ijtihad and taqlid that are connected to the four primary evidences (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas). Then it divides the essential attributes of the evidences into three categories: (1) attributes that are directly discussed in usul al-fiqh, namely the fact that they establish rulings (kawnuha muthbitatan lil-ahkam); (2) attributes that are not directly discussed but affect the occurrence of the discussed attributes, such as generality ('umum), sharedness (ishtirak), and being a solitary report (khabar wahid); (3) attributes that are neither discussed nor influential, such as the evidence being eternal (qadim) or created (hadith). The first category forms the predicates of the propositions of this science, the second category can serve as either qualifiers of the subject or become subjects/predicates themselves (e.g., 'al-'amm yujibu al-hukm qat'an'), and the third is irrelevant. The same three-type classification applies to the rulings: (1) the attribute that is discussed is the ruling being established by the mentioned evidences; (2) other attributes that affect this (not completed in the text). This systematic classification reflects the Hanafi concern with precise categorization of the objects of study in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
عارض ذاتی (arad dhati): An essential attribute intrinsic to the subject (evidence or ruling). Classified into three types: directly discussed, indirectly relevant, and irrelevant.
مثبت للاحکام (muthbitah lil-ahkam): The attribute of an evidence that it establishes rulings – the primary subject of usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a third-type essential attribute (neither discussed nor affecting discussed attributes) for an evidence?
A) The evidence being general ('amm).
B) The evidence being ancient (qadim).
C) The evidence being a solitary report (khabar wahid).
D) The evidence being an establisher of rulings.

Key Takeaway
The essential attributes of evidences and rulings are divided into three types; only the attribute of establishing rulings (for evidences) or being established by evidences (for rulings) is the direct subject of usul al-fiqh.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Sections of the Book: Benefit of Meaning and Benefit of Ruling
Outlining the two main divisions of Quranic study as a source.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul divides the study of the Quran into two categories: ifadat al-ma'na and ifadat al-hukm al-shar'i, and identify which linguistic topics belong to each category.

Core Idea
Before deriving a ruling from the Quran, you must first understand its meaning.

This passage introduces the structure of a classical Hanafi usul work (Al-Tawdih) by outlining its two main chapters. The author emphasizes that the Quran's primary purpose is to convey legal rulings, but this can only happen after the linguistic meaning is clarified. Therefore, the first chapter deals with how the Quran conveys meaning—covering topics like general and specific terms, truth and metaphor—while the second chapter focuses on how the Quran conveys legal rulings through commands and prohibitions. Understanding this division is foundational for any student of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main chapters
Read the passage carefully and note that the book is divided into two parts: the first on 'ifadat al-ma'na' (benefiting meaning) and the second on 'ifadat al-hukm al-shar'i' (benefiting legal ruling).
These are not arbitrary; they reflect the logical order of deriving rulings.
2
Understand the relationship between meaning and ruling
The passage states that benefiting a legal ruling depends on the composition benefiting meaning. This means that without a clear understanding of what the words convey, you cannot extract a legal ruling. Recognize the dependency: meaning → ruling.
This is a key methodological principle in Hanafi usul.
3
List the topics covered in the first chapter
The first chapter discusses topics such as general (عام), specific (خاص), common (مشترک), truth (حقیقت), and metaphor (مجاز). These are all related to how the text conveys meaning.
These linguistic categories help determine the correct interpretation before ruling.
4
List the topics covered in the second chapter
The second chapter deals with commands (امر) and prohibitions (نہی), which indicate obligation (وجوب) and prohibition (حرمت) respectively—both of which are legal rulings.
This chapter builds on the meaning established in the first chapter.
5
Appreciate the pedagogical flow
Recognize that this structure is typical in Hanafi usul works: first establish the linguistic principles, then apply them to derive rulings. This ensures rigorous and systematic derivation.
Sadr al-Shariah and the commentator (Sharh) highlight this organization as essential.

قال المصنف في التوضيح ونورد ابحاثه ای ابحاث الكتاب في ما بين الاول في افادته المعنی اعلم الخ یعنی کتاب اللہ کی غرض اصلی تو حکم شرعی کا افادہ ہے لیکن حکم شرعی کا افادہ اس پر موقوف ہے کہ نظم مفید معنی ہو تو معنی کے سمجھنے کے بعد حکم معلوم ہو سکتا ہے تو فلابد من البحث یعنی کتاب اللہ کا مفید معنی ہونا اس کے متعلق بحث کرنا ضروری ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے باب اول افادہ معنی کی بحث کے متعلق ہے تو اس باب میں خاص عام د مشترک اور حقیقت و مجاز و غیرہ کی بحث بائیں حیثیت کی جائے گی کہ یہ مفید معنی ہیں۔ والثاني في افادته الحكم الشرعى باب ثانی میں کتاب اللہ کا مفید برائے حکم شرعی ہونا اس کے متعلق بحث کی جائے گی تو امر کی نحث اس حیثیت سے کی جائیگی کہ وہ مفید وجوب ہے اور نہی میں بائیں حیثیت کہ وہ موجب حرمت ہے اور وجوب و حرمت حکم شرعی ہے۔ قال الشارح قولہ نورد ابحاثہ یعنی ہم اس کے اقسام بیان کریں گے اور وہ احوال
He said: The author in al-Tawdih said: 'And we present its investigations' i.e., the investigations of the book, in what is between them: the first is on benefiting meaning, know that... i.e., the primary purpose of the Book of Allah is to benefit a legal ruling, but benefiting a legal ruling depends on the composition benefiting meaning. So after understanding the meaning, the ruling can be known. Therefore, research is necessary, i.e., that the Book of Allah benefits meaning, it is necessary to discuss it. Therefore, the first chapter is about the discussion of benefiting meaning. So in this chapter, the discussions of specific, general, common, and truth and metaphor etc. will be conducted in terms of whether these benefit meaning. And the second [chapter] is on its benefiting the legal ruling. In the second chapter, the Book of Allah's benefiting a legal ruling will be discussed. So the discussion of command (amr) will be conducted in terms that it benefits obligation (wujub), and prohibition (nahy) in terms that it causes prohibition (hurmah), and obligation and prohibition are legal rulings. The commentator said: his statement 'we present its investigations' means we will explain its divisions and its conditions.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage introduces the structure of the book (Al-Tawdih) by outlining its two main chapters. The author, Sadr al-Shariah, states that the primary purpose of the Quran is to convey legal rulings. However, to derive rulings, one must first understand the meaning of the text. Therefore, the first chapter (باب اول) deals with how the Quran conveys meaning (افادہ معنی) — covering topics like general (عام), specific (خاص), common (مشترک), truth (حقیقت), and metaphor (مجاز). These discussions ensure that the text is understood properly. The second chapter (باب ثانی) deals with how the Quran conveys legal rulings (افادہ حکم شرعی). This includes analysis of commands (امر) and prohibitions (نہی), which indicate obligation (وجوب) and prohibition (حرمت) respectively — both of which are legal rulings. The commentator (Sharh) clarifies that 'we present its investigations' means that the book will explain the various aspects (اقسام) and conditions (احوال) pertaining to these topics. This organizational framework is typical of Hanafi usul works that systematically break down the study of the Quran as a primary source.

Key Terms
إفادة المعنى (ifadat al-ma'na): The Quran's function of conveying linguistic meaning, prior to deriving any legal ruling.
إفادة الحكم الشرعي (ifadat al-hukm al-shar'i): The Quran's function of specifying a legal ruling (e.g., obligation, prohibition) once meaning is understood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is the first chapter of the book dedicated to 'ifadat al-ma'na' (benefiting meaning)?
A) Because legal rulings are irrelevant without meaning.
B) Because understanding the meaning is a prerequisite for deriving legal rulings.
C) Because the Quran primarily focuses on meaning not rulings.
D) Because the author wants to discuss metaphor first.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the study of the Quran as a source is divided into two sequential stages: first analyzing its linguistic meaning (ifadat al-ma'na), then deriving legal rulings (ifadat al-hukm al-shar'i).
